## INT. ISLAND RECORDS – A&R WAR ROOM – LOWER MANHATTAN – LATE WINTER 1991

A long conference table. Whiteboards. Stacks of DAT tapes. A monitor flickers with a paused freeze-frame of Gilley, shirtless, mid-shout in some Ohio bar.

**SARAH MALCOM** (23), sharp, composed, hair pinned back with unnecessary precision, stands with her arms folded. Beside her on the table: the gold master of *Sixty Nine Reasons*, still warm from Ocasek’s Boston studio, with a handwritten Post-it note:

“Raw. Brilliant. Don’t fuck it up. — R.O.”

Across from her: **JONATHAN WYLER** (41), her division chief—gray suit, British, condescending, not entirely wrong about most things. He’s reviewing two manila folders labeled TRADITIONAL and MALCOM.

**WYLER (clapping the folders closed)**
Here’s the game. We know what we’d normally do with this kind of noise-forward, rustbelt freakshow: target college stations, chase a CMJ chart, pray to Peel.

(pauses, grins slightly) But you’ve been flapping about “predictive acoustic matrices” and “market adjacency deltas,” and frankly, Sarah, this is your shot.

Sarah doesn’t flinch. She’s heard this tone before. She’s already building the counterargument in her head.

**WYLER (CONT’D)**
So: you model it. You predict breakout markets, you identify genre straddlers, and you tell me which domino tips first. Cleveland or Phoenix. Kansas City or fucking Camden.

(leans in) 
I’ll run the other model alongside yours. Old school. Heat maps, tour history, meat-and-potatoes instincts.

(points to the master) 
You win, we go full data-forward. I back your methodology for the next three signings. You lose? You spend the summer running focus groups for our U2 reissues.

Sarah raises an eyebrow, then picks up the master tape. She runs a thumb along the edge, eyes narrowed.

**SARAH**
Fifteen days. Ric tracked this in fifteen days.

**WYLER**
Yes. Apparently, they recorded one track in the hallway because the snare kept knocking the lights loose in the studio. They’re animals.

**SARAH**
Or prophets.

**WYLER**
That’s your job to prove.

(beat) 
You have one week.

Sarah exits with the tape.

---

**INT. SARAH’S OFFICE – ISLAND RECORDS – SAME DAY**

The walls are covered in show fliers, genre maps, printouts of early social response algorithms, and a giant U.S. map with thumbtacks. Sarah sits at her desk, headphones on, eyes shut.

SOUND: The first track of *Sixty Nine Reasons* explodes into being — aggressive, chaotic, but held together by something unmistakably intentional.

On her screen: an audio waveform pulses. Code scrolls. A model she’s building in Lotus 1-2-3 pulls frequency data, emotional arc predictions, and vocal abrasion metrics.  She starts querying the model.

**VOICEOVER – SARAH (V.O.)**
The vocals don’t blend. That’s the point.  The first chorus sounds like a garage fire, and the second sounds like an alibi.  The drummer doesn’t hit the beat — he harasses it.  
And the girl? She’s either a cult leader or an open wound.  

Her eyes flick to a sticky note:  Target demo: Who needs this album?  She crosses it out. Replaces it with:  Who survives because of this album?

Cut to:

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS BASEMENT STUDIO – NIGHT**

Sarah’s set up an impromptu listening lab. Four interns, one jaded assistant, two hip hop heads from marketing, and an NPR-type classical composer sit in beanbags, listening.

SOUND: Track 4\. Kathy howls like someone remembering what violence felt like.

Every person in the room reacts differently: two lean in, one grimaces, one sits upright and just stares. That’s the face Sarah wants. She writes: This isn’t about preference. It’s about voltage.

**INT. BACK TO A\&R WAR ROOM – ONE WEEK LATER**  

Sarah presents.

**SARAH**  
Launch in Cincinnati. Not New York.  
(next slide…)
Leverage regional envy.
(next slide…)
Map secondary cities with high female youth rebellion indices.  
(next slide…)
Delay video. Let the voice hit first.  
(next slide…)
Break the band through anger, not image.  
(next slide…)
This isn’t radio bait. It’s a manifesto.

**WYLER** (reading the top of her packet)  
“What if we made pain go platinum.”  
(beat)  
*Jesus*.

**SARAH** (coolly)  
That’s your memo.  

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – DATA AND STRATEGY OFFICE – MIDDAY – WINTER 1991**

A sterile glass-walled cube. Fluorescent buzz. IBM PS/2 humming on the desk. A whiteboard covered in touring clusters, genre proximity charts, and a printout of a Rolling Stone reader poll taped sideways.

**SARAH MALCOM**, 23, sits cross-legged in a blazer that doesn’t quite fit and jeans that shouldn’t be office-legal. Her desk is chaos: a half-eaten apple, two fountain pens, and a printout titled:

**69 REASONS: CRITICAL DECONSTRUCTION & EMOTIONAL VOLTAGE MAPPING S. MALCOM, ISLAND RECORDS**

The gold master cassette is in front of her. A note taped to it, Ric Ocasek’s familiar handwriting:

*Sarah—*  
*Have clean panties ready.  These Dayton freaks will break you in half.  Savage, profane, sincere.*  
*— Ric*

She stares at it. Then presses play.

SOUND: Track 1. Gilley screaming something incoherent. Then Kathy howling like a siren raised by wolves. Her face doesn’t flinch. She’s already scribbling notes.

---

**MONTAGE – **SARAH MALCOM vs. 69 REASONS**

* Scene 1: Her tiny apartment.

   She’s cross-legged on the floor with headphones, scribbling down a column labeled:

  * “Kathy = Joan Didion possessed by Janis Joplin.”
  * “Track 3 = banned in at least 3 states by default.”
  * “This album doesn’t play to an audience. It accuses one.”

* Scene 2: Sarah dragging the label’s IBM into a soundproof closet, patching in EQ values and lyrical sentiment tagging, tracking profanity by tempo.

* Scene 3: A late-night phone call with her college roommate, half-manic from caffeine and genius.

   **SARAH**
   “Imagine if Fiona Apple, Trent Reznor, and Samantha from Sex and the City raised a feral daughter in a dive bar.  That’s Kathy. That’s this band.”

* Scene 4: Sarah at 3 a.m. overlaying Commuted’s track BPMs with female-led rock markets, marking cities on a U.S. map: CINCINNATI. DETROIT. ST. LOUIS. TULSA.

   She mutters, “Not New York. Not L.A. This album breaks in the shadows.”

---

**INT. ISLAND EXECUTIVE WAR ROOM – MONDAY – DAY**

Sarah walks in with a full report. 92 pages. Spiral-bound, color-coded tabs, and one page near the front with the headline:

### THESE SONGS ARE GOING TO MAKE PEOPLE FUCK AND RIOT.  

**WYLER** (her boss, bemused, flipping pages):  
What the hell is ‘Grunge American Primitivism’?

**SARAH** (without hesitation):  
It’s the sound of what happens when the Midwest stops apologizing.

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – CONFERENCE ROOM – MANHATTAN – LATE WINTER 1991**

The room is full. Execs in gray suits. Sarah in red lipstick, Doc Martens, and a vintage Joy Division T-shirt under her blazer. On the wall, a giant U.S. map. Thumbtacks jammed into college towns nobody in this building has ever cared about.

She slams a box on the table: it’s filled with autographed Kleenex packs.

**SARAH** (zero irony)
They’re not getting stickers. They’re not getting T-shirts. They’re getting proof this album makes you climax and cry at the same time.

(beat)
And the first dose goes to Oxford, Ohio.

The room doesn’t blink. Oxford? Is that even a city?

---

**EXT. 97X – OUTSIDE STATION PARKING LOT – NIGHT – A FEW DAYS LATER**

Sarah, in a rental car smelling like spilled fries and high risk, throws it into park. She grabs the *Sixty Nine Reasons* master and a Sharpie. Inside the station, the late-night DJ is eating vending machine pretzels and running Bauhaus for the sixth time this shift.

**SARAH (V.O.)**
97X. The future of rock and roll. You can’t buy that kind of legacy, but you can show up at 3 a.m., beg for airtime, and hand them a box of these…

**DJ (SKEPTICAL)**
You got stickers?

**SARAH**
No. I have a box of autographed Kleenex. And a song that’s going to get at least one listener pregnant tonight.

Sarah puts a little cleavage on display. He stares. She slides in the tape. They play it once—After Hours. The switchboard lights up like it’s prom night and someone brought drugs.

---

**INT. 97X RADIO STUDIO – MINUTES LATER**

*AFTER HOURS* plays. Kathy’s voice cuts through the ether like someone whispering sin into the apocalypse. Phone lines light up.

**Caller 1**
Who the hell is this?

**Caller 2**
Did she just say “fuck and hide”?

**Caller 3 (female)**
Play it again. I’m not even done screaming.

---

**MONTAGE – “THE BLITZ” BEGINS**

SARAH’S PLAN – FROM HER MEMO:

Forget the coasts. They’ll follow when it’s safe. This album isn’t safe. It’s necessary. We flood the flyovers. We take the small towns first. The Midwest will eat this alive. Then it’ll spread like a brushfire across dorms, discmans, and guilt.

* Bogart’s, Cincinnati. Flyers stapled to telephone poles. 200 kids show up. Half of them weren’t alive the last time a band played this raw.

* WALB, Bowling Green State. Sarah trades a limited bootleg cassette for a 1 a.m. timeslot. The tape gets stolen by the next DJ. They play it again. And again.

* WIDR, Kalamazoo. She shows up unannounced with a shoebox of dubbed demos and a bag of weed gummy frogs. Nobody checks credentials. They give her 10 minutes. She makes it 40\.

* Grinnell, NE. Carbondale, IL. Lawrence, KS. Stillwater, OK.

Every town a band van could hit, Sarah hit first—with a copy of *Sixty Nine Reasons*, a fake name, and a promise:

## “Play this, and no one in your city will fuck the same ever again.”

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – WAR ROOM – TWO WEEKS LATER**

Phone ringing. Wyler staring at airplay heatmaps. A new sound is emerging on the charts—not in LA, not in NYC, but Fargo, ND. Athens, OH. Urbana, IL. Columbia, MO.

**WYLER** (to himself):
Jesus Christ, she’s feeding them gasoline.

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – WAR ROOM – EARLY MORNING**

**SARAH** stands at the whiteboard, sweaty and sharp from another all-nighter. Circles on the map are shifting—not to New York, not to Boston, but sliding hard downward.

**WYLER**, sleeves rolled up, tie loose, eyes locked on the same board. He’s chewing a pencil like it’s made of nicotine.

**SARAH** (tapping thumbtacks into Knoxville TN, Athens, GA, Tuscaloosa, AL)
The coasts will come—but not first. This isn’t a style play. It’s a sensation play. They feel it before they understand it. And the South doesn’t flinch when things get sweaty.

**WYLER** (half to himself)
Fuck the coasts.

(then louder) 
Go South.

(beat) 
You’ve got three weeks. Do what you do.

And… (grudgingly) 
I’ll argue for a couple grand for videos.

**SARAH** (eye-rolls into a smile)
You want a video budget for Commuted? I hope you like seeing one of them piss on a light fixture

**WYLER** (deadpan)
I’ll pitch it as avant-garde.

---

**INT. SARAH’S OFFICE – LATER THAT DAY**

She drags open a cardboard box marked:

FIELD DATA – UNRELEASED – FEMALE DEMO RESPONSE

Typed memos. Handwritten comment cards. Survey feedback. Unsolicited letters. Napkins with lipstick notes. A header sheet from a University of Cincinnati field test reads:

*“We did not expect this level of emotional combustion. Of the 62 women in the listening session, 14 cried.  9 left to call someone. 3 threw up. 1 masturbated in the library bathroom.  ‘After Hours’ should carry a legal disclaimer.”*

Another excerpt:

*“Listening to ‘Not Taken Kindly’ made me rethink my entire sexual history. I was halfway through a Pop-Tart and suddenly remembered a breakup from 8th grade and started sobbing.”*

Sarah lays it out like evidence in a murder case. Then dials Wyler’s extension.

**SARAH** (into phone)
I’ve got something for you. If you don’t greenlight this promo surge into the South, I’m going to take this data straight to fucking Sire.

**WYLER** (on speaker, dry)
And what would you call this document?

She smiles.

**SARAH**
Proof women don’t want indie boys in sweaters anymore. They want blood, sweat, and orgasms on vinyl.

---

**INT. WYLER’S OFFICE – LATER**

He’s holding her 92-page memo.

On the cover: THE SIREN MODEL: How *Sixty Nine Reasons* Weaponizes Desire Across the Flyover Belt – Sarah Malcom

He flips to the graph: 18-29 FEMALE DEMO: EMOTIONAL VOLTAGE INDEX BY SONG

The curve isn’t just high—it’s exponential. Spiking around *After Hours*, detonating at *Not Taken Kindly*, going completely off the grid at *Tangled Up*.

There’s a handwritten note in the margin: “This isn’t audience targeting. This is audience possession.”

**WYLER** (quietly)
Jesus Christ. This isn’t a record release. It’s a goddamn exorcism.

---

**MONTAGE – THE SOUTHERN BLITZ BEGINS**

(Title Card: “Three Weeks Until Release.”)

(Background Track: “After Hours” – fade-in just past the first verse, sultry and low.)

**EXT. SAVANNAH, GEORGIA – EARLY MORNING**

**SARAH MALCOM** steps out of a beat-up Ford Escort. No bra. No panties. A simple floral sundress catching the humid wind. She’s not dressing down—she’s dressing correctly. Like she belongs here. Like she could charm a Confederate ghost and sell it an album.

In her arms? A bakery box of snickerdoodles and a battered boombox with the Sixty Nine Reasons master dubbed onto cassette.

**INT. WYFQ – COLLEGE RADIO STUDIO – SAVANNAH**

A DJ looks up from a paper cup of day-old coffee. She slides the tape across the counter.

**SARAH**
One listen. That’s all I ask. And these are for you. (hands him the cookies)
Fresh. The snickerdoodle’s a bribe. The music? That’s scripture.

**DJ (half-laughing)**
You trying to do payola with pastries?

**SARAH** **(already plugging in the boombox)**
Bribery’s a felony. Hospitality is Southern tradition.

---

**EXT. MACON, GA – ROADSIDE DINER – LATE AFTERNOON**

Sarah sits with a college station assistant PD. They’re splitting pecan pie and listening to Tangled Up through a shared Walkman splitter.

The kid’s face turns red halfway through the second verse.

**ASSISTANT PD**
Did she just say—?

**SARAH** (chewing calmly)
Yep.

**ASSISTANT PD**
And y’all want us to play this… like… on air?

**SARAH**
If you don’t, some other bastard will, and you’ll miss history and the street cred.

**ASSISTANT PD**
Goddamn. Gimme four copies.

---

**MONTAGE CONTINUES**

* COLUMBUS, GEORGIA – She crash-writes a promo spot in the DJ’s handwriting and tells him to say it like a late-night confession. He reads it on-air:

“If you hear this next track and don’t feel a little funny in your jeans, turn in your Southern card.”

* BIRMINGHAM, ALABAMA – A record store clerk trades wall space for a poster and a quick feel-up behind the jazz section. She doesn’t even flinch.

   **SARAH** (as she staples the flyer)

   If this album doesn’t move your soul, it’ll move your zipper.

* ATLANTA – WRAS 88.5 – A midnight show cuts to black mid-Not Taken Kindly when the FCC hotline lights up. The DJ unplugs the console, laughing.

“They ain’t banning the Stones. They’re banning us.”

---

**INT. SARAH’S MOTEL ROOM – ATHENS, GA – NIGHT**

Hotel bed covered in maps, station logs, and lipstick-stained index cards.

She circles her next hit: AUBURN.

Voice recorder to herself:

**SARAH** (V.O.)

The plan’s simple:  Follow Sherman’s path, then aim where he didn’t—into hearts, beds, and every damn girl who’s ever screamed into her steering wheel alone.  The men? They’ll catch up.  But the South bleeds first.  

---

**MONTAGE ENDS – TIME JUMP: ONE WEEK TO RELEASE**

Every radio station from Savannah to Starkville has touched Sixty Nine Reasons. Half the DJs don’t know what they played. The other half won’t stop playing it.

College campuses light up with bootlegs, whispers, new lyrics scrawled on bathroom stalls.

Back in New York, execs are baffled by why 2 a.m. call-ins in Hattiesburg, Mississippi are asking if Kathy Espich is single.

---

**INT. GREYHOUND TERMINAL – JACKSON, MISSISSIPPI – NIGHT**

Sarah Malcom sits alone on a bench under a buzzing sodium light, sipping warm Dr. Pepper and scribbling into her notebook titled:

“The Gospel According to Kathy: Phase Two – Texas.”

The Southland has fallen in lust. But Texas?  Texas is a fortress. A religion. A sovereign entity that eats bands for breakfast and spits out broken van axles and demo tapes.

She’s not intimidated. She’s aroused.

---

**MONTAGE: OPERATION LONE STAR THRUST – “GOD BLESS TEXAS, AND GODDAMN DOES SHE BLEED”**

(Cue: Kathy’s wail from “Not Taken Kindly” tearing across the screen like a sonic whip.)

---

**INT. KTCU – FORT WORTH – LATE NIGHT**

A DJ in snakeskin boots stares at the liner notes of Sixty Nine Reasons. He’s holding a napkin Sarah handed him—on it, in lipstick:  “This isn’t girl rock. This is what happens when a woman stops apologizing.”

He drops the needle on Eyes Lost in Desire. The phone rings before the second verse.

---

**EXT. AUSTIN – HOLE-IN-THE-WALL RECORD STORE**

Sarah’s outside under the neon with a boombox and a box of custom tapes labeled “69 RX – TAKE TWO, CALL HER BACK.” She hands one to a girl in a UT hoodie.

**SARAH**

Play Track 4\. Then text your ex and say you forgive him only because you’ve moved on to better orgasms.

---

**INT. KVRX – AUSTIN – LIVE BOOTH – AFTER MIDNIGHT**

The host hesitates. It’s Tangled Up. The chorus is loaded. No euphemism. Just squirt, sweat, climax.

**DJ: (on-air, unbothered)**
Warning: this song may make you cum. You’re welcome.

---

**INT. DIVE BAR – HOUSTON – POSTER STAPLED TO DOOR**

WHO THE FUCK IS COMMUTED?  
FIND OUT. BRING LUBE.

Inside, a low-slung projector blares grainy VHS clips of the band’s only known live footage. Kathy spits lyrics in shadows. Gilley’s shirtless, vibrating. No one’s breathing.

At the bar, Sarah’s sipping Lone Star and watching women nod silently, like this is a sermon they didn’t know they were waiting for.

---

**EXT. MARFA, TEXAS – DESERT RADIO RELAY STATION**

An aging FM relay engineer picks up a copy of the album left under a rock by the service door. Inside the case: one Polaroid of Sarah, dress caught in the wind, smiling like she already won.

She scribbled on the photo: “This one’s for the ghosts. Play it loud.”  

---

**INT. DALLAS – UNDISCLOSED COLLEGE STATION – NIGHT**

Sarah stands in a booth. A crowd of students presses against the glass outside.

**SARAH**
You want to know why this album matters? Because it doesn’t ask permission. It gets in your bed, your bloodstream, and your worst mistake. Then it tells you to own it. Out loud. In stereo.

She presses PLAY.

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – WAR ROOM – SAME NIGHT**

The fax machine explodes with rotation reports from Texas stations that were never even serviced. College blogs post audio leaks with headlines like:

“Who TF Is Kathy Espich and Why Am I Crying After This?”

Wyler is in a bathrobe with a tumbler of scotch, staring at a real-time airplay graph that looks like a rocket launch from Lubbock.

He mutters:

**WYLER**
…she just broke Texas. With cookies and cassette tapes. Jesus fucking Christ.

---

**INT. EL PASO BUS STATION – SUNSET**

A cracked leather boot hits the dry cement.  Dust swirls. A lone cicada screams. Sarah Malcom adjusts her sunglasses, grabs her suitcase (tapes, posters, cookies, lipstick, tequila minis), and steps into the desert like she’s entering the final boss level of seduction-driven promo warfare. 

Her target: The Desert Southwest. Land of broken radio towers, long-haul truckers, and desperate AM broadcasters running on 14 watts and loose FCC oversight.

---

**OPERATION BORDERLINE BLISS**

(Codename: “Oye, Señor, Play This and Regret Nothing.”)

---

**MONTAGE – DESERT RADIO TAKEOVER**

**EXT. TIJUANA AM TOWER – LATE NIGHT**

A dusty-stubbled DJ leans over his mic, still high from the bottle of mescal Sarah left.
Sarah, grinning in floral print and boots, leans in and whispers, sultry and low, into the booth mic:

**SARAH**
*Oye, tengo la mejor música que jamás escucharás en tu vida, y si la pones a todo volumen, convocarás a mujeres lujuriosas que bailarán bajo la pálida luz de la luna completamente desnudas contigo, señor.*  
(I have the best music you’ll ever hear in your life. If you play it loud enough, it will summon lustful women to dance naked in the moonlight with you, sir.)

**DJ (beat, grinning)**
Mierda santa… dale play.

He slams After Hours to air. The broadcast bleeds past the border like a siren’s call. Somewhere in the desert, someone opens a truck door and cries from their knees.

---

**TUCSON, AZ – DORM COMMON ROOM – 1:32 A.M.**

Girls dancing barefoot to “The Left Hand.” One guy asks what band this is. No one answers. They just turn it up louder.

---

**SANTA FE – SMALL GALLERY INSTALLATION**

A curator plays Initiating Connection through a looped VHS video of coyotes under neon signs. A priest walks in and blesses the whole exhibit without being asked.

---

**PHOENIX – GRITTY VINYL SHOP – POSTER IN WINDOW**

Handwritten with a Sharpie:

COMMITTED TO COMMUTED  
NO SHAME. NO PANTS. NO RETURNS.  
FREE LISTEN TONIGHT. BRING A TONGUE.

Inside, Sarah DJs under the alias “La Gringa del Ruido.” No shoes. Two beers. Five new disciples by morning.

---

**SARAH’S DESERT STRATEGY – INTERNAL MEMO EXCERPT**

“Forget LA. Forget press. We hijack Mexican AM, crank college FM from Albuquerque to Flagstaff, and feed the desert night.  The girls will find it. The boys will chase the girls.  
And by the time Billboard notices, they’ll already be naked and dancing.  No one questions where a wildfire started once it’s burning the country down.”  

---

**INT. MARFA – TRAILER WITH SATELLITE DISH – RADIO HACKER HAVEN**

Sarah plugs into an unlicensed rebroadcast relay.  A woman in snakeskin heels asks, “What are we broadcasting?” Sarah answers by handing her headphones.

**SOUND**: The climax of Tangled Up.

The woman inhales, closes her eyes. Then flips every switch on the panel. The desert hears everything.

---

**INT. MOTEL ROOM – NEEDLES, CALIFORNIA – LATE NIGHT**

The air conditioner sounds like it’s dying of heartbreak. Sarah is spread across a motel bed, face down in a pillow, equal parts tequila and existential exhaustion, when the room phone rings.  The motel room landline. She picks up, groggy but curious.

**VOICE ON THE LINE (NERVOUS, MALE):**
Hi, uh… Sarah Malcom? This is Nate from KTNV Las Vegas. I—uh—I’m trying to make sense of… whatever the hell this is. The band. The songs. The… reactions. Are you available for an interview?

Long pause.

Sarah smiles.

**SARAH** (flat):
Nate. You just found God in a used CD bin. Let’s talk.

---

**INT. KTNV LOCAL STUDIO – VEGAS – TWO DAYS LATER**

Sarah walks in like Joan of Arc in heels and a sundress. She’s done zero PR prep. Hair still smells like desert wind and cherry ChapStick.  **NATE**, the reporter, is young, twitchy, and half-scared. He’s heard the album. Twice. He hasn’t slept since. They’re live-to-tape, barebones set. Cheap lighting. One camera. Perfect.

**NATE:**
Let’s just start here…What is Commuted?

**SARAH** (leaning forward, calm):
A mirror. Held too close. With lipstick on it.

**NATE:**
So, this music. It’s… raw. Provocative. Some say obscene.

**SARAH**:
Some people called Joan Jett a whore. Some people said Liz Phair needs therapy. Some people can’t handle a woman saying exactly what she wants, when she wants it, and what position she came in.

**NATE (half-laughing, flushed):**
…And, uh, when are they coming to Vegas?

**SARAH (without missing a beat):**
They’re already here. You just haven’t noticed yet.

**NATE:**
How do you even market this?

**SARAH** (grinning like a knife):
We don’t market. We invade. Then we hand out bandages and condoms.

**NATE:**
How has this impacted you? 

(A beat. She looks right into the lens. Her voice drops low, not for drama—but truth.)

**SARAH**:
You ever walk into a room and feel your body shift just because of what’s in the air? That’s what this album did to me. It rewired my taste, my career, my sleep schedule. 
I’ve stopped apologizing for anything. I’ve kissed people I shouldn’t have. I’ve said no louder. And yes, even louder than that.

(leans closer)

This record didn’t just change me.  It dared me to stop pretending I hadn’t already changed.

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – NYC – SAME TIME**

WYLER is in his office watching the KTNV segment on a tiny monitor.  She’s magnetic. Brazen. Calm and feral at the same time. One intern walks by and murmurs: “She’s not in A\&R anymore. She is the brand now.”

---

**INT. KTNV – STUDIO – AFTER INTERVIEW**

Sarah leans into Nate as they unclip mics.

**SARAH (quietly, sincerely):**
You ran the story no one else had the balls to chase. So I’ll give you this:

She pulls a sharpie from her purse and writes something on the inside of her palm.

**SARAH (CONT’D):**
Commuted. Pop-up. One week. Vegas strip. No permits. No warning. No survivors.

---

**INT. DAYTON, OHIO – CREMEANS’ HOUSE – LIVING ROOM – 9:46 A.M. – JANUARY 1992**

It’s cold as hell outside. Inside? Warmer, but no less raw.  The band’s scattered across couches and milk crates. GILLEY is in a robe, smoking an unlit cigarette.  JEFF scribbles chord structures on an unopened phone bill. JIM taps a beat on the back of a pizza box.
KATHY lies on the floor in a ripped long-sleeve thermal, boots still on. CREMEANS, label liaison and professional skeptic, sits in an armchair with his usual legal pad, already halfway through a list titled: “Shit We’re Not Doing.”

**SARAH** MALCOM walks in unannounced, a gust of wind behind her and a fire in her eyes that hasn’t slept in 30 hours. Her boots are covered in Vegas dust.

**CREMEANS (flatly):**
I know that look. Who’d you piss off?

**SARAH**
Not who. Where. I committed you all to a pop-up show in Las Vegas. Next Friday. On the Strip. No permits. No warning.

(drops a manila folder on the table)

Press knows. KTNV’s covering. You’ll play until the cops arrive or the amps melt. Whichever comes first.

**[[4.3 JEFF EVANS character bible|Jeff]]**
Wait, what?

**SARAH (to Cremeans):**
It’s done. I sold it like it was a sanctioned label stunt. They bought it because I had the balls to act like it was already happening.

**CREMEANS (leaning forward):**
You committed the band to a public, unauthorized street performance? In a gaming jurisdiction? Without a safety rider, without a backline list, without telling me?

**SARAH**
Correct. I also told KTNV this album would do things to people’s bodies they weren’t prepared to admit on air.

**GILLEY**
Sounds like a normal weekend.

**JIM (quietly impressed):**
Vegas, huh?

**KATHY (sitting up slowly):**
How many songs?

**SARAH**
Three. Maybe four, if you don’t get shut down. After Hours starts. Not Taken Kindly finishes. They’ll remember every fucking note in between.

(beat)

Ric Ocasek warned me. He said this record would break people. What he didn’t count on was how many of them wanted to be broken.

**CREMEANS (after a long pause):**

This stunt? It could get you arrested.

**SARAH**
Or on Entertainment Tonight.

**CREMEANS (reluctantly amused):**

You’ve got balls, Malcom.

**SARAH** (dead serious):

No, Cremeans. I’ve got Commuted.

---

**INT. CREMEANS’ LIVING ROOM – DAYTON – MOMENTS LATER**

The room is loud now. Not musical loud—band loud. Everyone talking, overlapping, post-Vegas bombshell. Sarah stands dead center, gripping a mug of instant coffee that tastes like panic.

**KATHY (flat, firm):**

We close with *Come Inside Me.* Period. We bleed it out. All eleven minutes, thirty-six seconds. If they shut us down halfway, that’s their sin.

(Gilley, flicking his lighter, flinches when Cremeans speaks.)

**CREMEANS**
Gilley, if you light that thing in my house, you’re buying me a new one. With your first royalty check.

**GILLEY (grinning)**
Hope you like wraparound decks, brother.

**BILL (serious, sincere):**
Are we aping the Beatles with a rooftop thing? Or can we do something they wouldn’t dare?

**SARAH (to Bill):**
The Beatles didn’t open with a song that caused four minor radio station blackouts. We’re doing something they’d deny writing.

**JEREMY (to Sarah):**
What time of day are you thinking? Sunset? Or full neon chaos?

**SARAH** (instantly):
Dusk. Hit After Hours as the Strip lights up. Girls will scream. Guys will pretend they don’t understand why. Cops will show by song three.

**JEFF (pushing glasses up):**
Will we have a guerrilla camera team? If we’re risking jail, I want footage.

**SARAH**
Already talked to a KTNV tech and an NYU dropout with a Hi8 and no morals.
They’ll catch every frame.  We cut it up, drop a grainy-as-sin “official” video on a midnight broadcast. Cheap. Illegal. Perfect.

**JEFF**
How soon can you get us on *120 Minutes*?

**SARAH**
I need three clean edits, one radio sponsor, and Matt Pinfield’s pager number. You give me 36 hours and a good show, I’ll get you late-night rotation by February.

---

**CREMEANS (rubbing his temples):**
Jesus, this is happening.

**SARAH** (grinning, caffeinated, already halfway to packing):
No. It’s already happened.  Now we just have to show up and let the Strip catch fire.

---

**MONTAGE – **SARAH HERDING CATS (aka BAND PREP)**

🎬 Sarah taping a city map to the wall, outlining amplifier positions like a field general.
🎬 Kathy sitting cross-legged, marking the setlist in Sharpie on a Taco Bell napkin.
🎬 Bill dragging out synth cables and muttering about voltage tolerances.
🎬 Jeff rewiring the backup camera so it can mount to a stop sign.
🎬 Jeremy testing acoustic resonance using an unplugged Strat and a garbage disposal.
🎬 Gilley asking Sarah if she thinks a mesh tank top is too much.

**SARAH (without looking up):**
You’re fronting a band called Commuted. No such thing as too much.

---

**EXT. LAS VEGAS STRIP – FOUR DAYS TO SHOWTIME – LATE AFTERNOON**

SARAH MALCOM stands across from Caesar’s Palace, wind snapping her skirt against her legs, sunglasses on, clipboard in one hand, payphone receiver in the other. Three stories are unfolding around her like plates she’s keeping spinning in a casino full of doubters.

---

### **1\. THE MEDIA – “HELP ME Help You Blow the Roof Off Vegas”**

**INT. KTNV NEWSROOM – SAME TIME**

The room smells like copier toner and fear of irrelevance.  Sarah’s already sent them the grainy rehearsal footage, a crude bootleg VHS rip of After Hours from Cincinnati. She’s now pitching a full exclusive to KTNV’s senior producer, DELANEY, who’s skeptical but secretly intrigued.

**SARAH** (into phone):
Delaney, listen—this isn’t a garage band. This is the garage burning down with all your daddy’s sins inside it. You want the shot? I’ve got your angle.

**DELANEY (on speakerphone, amused):**
And what if the cops shut it down?

**SARAH**
Even better. You’re not filming a concert. You’re filming a fucking reckoning.

---

### **2\. THE BAND – “Seduction \= Pressure with Velvet Gloves”**

**INT. BUDGET HOTEL – STRIP SIDE – BAND SUITE – SAME NIGHT**

The guys are half-wired from travel and nerves. Kathy’s pacing. Jeremy’s playing the same riff wrong on purpose just to annoy Jeff. Sarah walks in with a six-pack, a blank tape, and a look.

**SARAH**
You get one shot. One sidewalk. One outlaw broadcast.

(beat, eyes locking with Kathy)

The world will see you.  But you have to burn for them. Not just perform. I want your tightest set, your filthiest chemistry, your most feral control.

**GILLEY (half-mocking)**
You giving us a pep talk, coach?

**SARAH** (walking slowly past him)
I’m giving you permission. To be exactly what this album makes people feel. If that scares you… good. You’re close.

(leans down to Jeff)

We don’t need slick. We need conviction.

---

### **3\. THE BOSS – “The Queen’s Gambit”**

**INT. PAYPHONE BOOTH OUTSIDE THE HOTEL – MOMENTS LATER**

Sarah drops in 35 cents and dials Wyler’s office back in New York. He’s in a meeting. She doesn’t wait.

**SARAH** (to his machine):
This is what exercising initiative looks like. We’re not breaking the rules. We’re shattering them, taping them back together, and mailing the pieces to MTV with a handwritten note: 
Girls on top. You’re welcome. And if this goes sideways? You can fire me. 

But I promise—only after you give me a raise.

(click)

---

**MONTAGE – THREEWAY STRATEGY IN MOTION**

🎬 KTNV prepping with their camera team, one shaky-cam rigged to a helmet, another in a fake ice cream cart.
🎬 Sarah guiding Kathy through mic testing, whispering, “Drag their hearts out through their belt loops.”
🎬 Jeff and Jim syncing a clock-radio to the backup generator so the set hits at 6:03 PM exactly.
🎬 Sarah on the phone with Wyler’s assistant, pretending to “update press contacts” while secretly confirming with a pirate VHS duplicator in North Vegas.

---

**INT. VEGAS STRIP CLUB – BACKROOM – 1:27 A.M. – TWO DAYS TO SHOWTIME**

The club is red-lit and thudding, with tired strippers smoking menthols in corners and neon reflected in spilled whiskey. The backroom? Occupied by Commuted—and on the brink of a full-on band brawl. Empty shot glasses. Setlist notes torn in half. A Sharpie embedded in the wall like a thrown knife. It’s a donnybrook. Words flying. Ego flaring. Stakes high as hell.

**JEFF (cold, precise):**
If we only get three songs, Come Inside Me doesn’t fit. It’s eleven minutes. We need impact, not indulgence.

**KATHY (arms crossed, jaw set):**
It’s the only way we end this. That song leaves blood on the floor. You want punch? That’s the knockout.

**JIM (drumming on a napkin, trying to stay Switzerland):**
After Hours opens, that’s agreed. But if we only have time for three…

**BILL (cutting in):**
Then we need tempo balance. We can’t go *After Hours* into *Not Taken Kindly*—that’s like giving ‘em chocolate cake and then punching them in the stomach.

**GILLEY (half-drunk, shirt already unbuttoned):**
Okay, but if we do *Initiating Connection*, they’re gonna think we’re sellouts. You want slick pop in a sidewalk riot?

**KATHY**
It’s not slick. It’s bait.We bring them in soft. We finish them off hard.

**JEREMY (quiet, but pointed):**
What’s the time limit?

**CREMEANS (off to the side, arms folded):**
You’ll have eight minutes. Maybe nine if Metro PD’s slow. Twelve if you flirt with the cop.

(glances at Kathy)

Which, honestly, is our best bet.

**JEFF**
Then it’s *After Hours, Left Hand, Come Inside Me*. That gives Kathy two lead vocals, Bill one synth storm, and Gilley space to swing his dick around without setting a speaker on fire.

**GILLEY (mock offense):**
Hey, I’m refined chaos. Thank you.

**KATHY**
If we don’t close with *Come Inside Me*, I’m walking. Not a threat. A promise. I didn’t record eleven and a half minutes of hypnotic filth to be told it’s too much.

(beat, low)

If I go down, I’m taking the Strip with me.

**EPIC BEAT OF SILENCE.**

Then, slowly, a nod from Jim. Then Jeremy. Then Jeff.

**GILLEY (grinning, raising his glass):**
So it’s settled. *After Hours. The Left Hand. Come Inside Me.* Three tracks. One chance. All in.

**BILL (raising an eyebrow):**
You know we could die doing this, right?

**KATHY (standing, already walking toward the exit):**
Live fast and leave a scantily clad corpse!

---

**INT. STRIP CLUB BACKROOM – SAME NIGHT – MOMENTS LATER**

The air is thick—whiskey, sweat, tension, ego. But Kathy Espich isn’t backing down. She stands—one boot on a chair, hands on hips like Joan Jett with a gavel.

**KATHY (clear, firm):**
Gentlemen… and Gilley…It’s time. For ***Band Democracy.***

(Gasps. From no one. But still dramatic.)

She looks around the room, each bandmate sizing her up.  Then she points to Jeremy, who’s mid-sip of someone else’s beer.

**KATHY**
Jeremy. You’re secretary. Call the fucking roll.

**JEREMY (straightening up, mildly terrified but honored):**
Yes, ma’am.

(He opens a crumpled notebook, finds a blank page, licks his pen.)

**KATHY (stepping forward):**
I name the motion: “To obliterate Las Vegas with three goddamn songs.” Those songs shall be:

* *After Hours*
* *The Left Hand*
* and *Come Inside Me*

In that order. No substitutions. No edits. No regrets. Now, which one of you sumbitches is gonna second it?

**GILLEY (raising his glass, smirking):**
I second that loud, filthy, righteous motion.

**JEFF (grudgingly, under his breath):**
Point of order: that set is technically illegal in most states.

**JIM (grinning):**
But not Nevada.

**BILL (grabbing Jeremy’s pen and signing the page):**
Let the minutes reflect that democracy has never been this horny.

**KATHY (grinning, standing tall):**
Then by the power vested in distortion pedals and mutual trauma, this motion is passed. 
You’ve all been heard. Now shut up and bring the thunder.

---

**EXT. VEGAS STRIP CLUB – 2:04 A.M. – PARKING LOT OF SIN**

The club door swings open with a thud. A plume of smoke and bass rolls out behind Kathy, Jeff, Bill, Jeremy, and Jim, who march into the cool night like a five-piece war party ready to ignite the Vegas Strip.

**KATHY**
That’s it. Decision made. Setlist locked. No prisoners.

**JEFF**
We hit dusk. Three tracks. In, out, outlaw legends.

**BILL (adjusting his synth case):**
God help whoever tries to follow that.

**JIM (sniffing the air):**
Smells like destiny… and maybe piss.

**JEREMY (squinting, confused):**
Wait. That’s five of us. Where the hell’s Gilley?

(They stop in sync, slowly turn, and stare at the glowing neon club behind them.)

**KATHY (icy):**
That motherfucker…

---

**INT. STRIP CLUB – VIP BOOTH – 2:07 A.M.**

**GILLEY** is fully reclined in a red leather booth, shirt open to his navel, cocktail in hand, looking like he’s trying to audition for a Van Halen cover band that only plays in hot tubs.

Across from him?

**“AMANDA.”**

Wearing nothing but a smile and a live boa constrictor.  She’s sipping a Shirley Temple through a Twizzler straw, completely unfazed by the 40 pounds of reptile draped across her chest.

**GILLEY (grinning like an idiot):**
So you’re a dancer and a snake handler? That’s like… double artistry.

**AMANDA (deadpan):**
The snake’s name is Michael Douglas.

**GILLEY**
That’s… somehow the hottest thing I’ve ever heard.

---

**INT. CLUB ENTRANCE – MOMENTS LATER**

The rest of the band storms back in, only to be stopped by the bouncer, a linebacker-sized man in a mesh tank and a judgey expression.

**BOUNCER**:
Cover’s back on, sweethearts.

**KATHY (incredulous):**
We were just in there! We have to retrieve our lead singer!

**BOUNCER**:
Then he’s your problem. Cover’s twenty each.

**JEFF (grumbling):**
We’re paying a cover to kidnap our own bandmate from a titty trap.

**BILL (handing over cash):**
That’s a business expense, right?

---

**INT. VIP BOOTH – MOMENTS LATER**

KATHY storms up to the booth like a small tornado with combat boots. The band fans out behind her like angry backup singers.

**KATHY (dead calm):**
Gilley. Get. The fuck. Up.

**GILLEY (startled, gesturing toward Amanda and Michael Douglas the snake):**
Guys—this is Amanda. Amanda, this is… my parole board.

**AMANDA (smiling, unfazed):**
Sup.

**JEREMY**
Is that… a real boa constrictor?

**BILL**
Weirdly majestic.

**JIM (to Amanda):**

Does he usually pay for his own drinks?

**KATHY (to Gilley):**
We just had a democratic vote. You seconded the motion. You can’t skip the revolution for boobs and reptiles.

**GILLEY (reluctantly standing up, snake still draped over him):**
Can I bring her?

**KATHY (deadpan):**
You can barely bring your guitar most days.

**AMANDA (to Gilley):**
Call me when you make it big. I do birthday parties. And baptisms.

---

**EXT. STRIP CLUB – REJOINING THE NIGHT – 2:19 A.M.**

The full band finally exits together, Kathy leading like Joan of Arc with a hangover, Gilley waving at Amanda and Michael Douglas one last time.

**JEFF (shaking his head):**
So we almost lost the gig to a topless snake whisperer.

**BILL (philosophically):**
Vegas giveth. Vegas very nearly taketh away.

**KATHY (marching forward):**
Focus. We go to war in two days. Everyone sober up, shut up, and tune up. This time, we’re the main act.

---

**EXT. VEGAS ROOFTOP – PRE-DAWN STILLNESS – THE MORNING BEFORE THE SHOW**

The city is soft in the blue hour—just before sin wakes up again. Neon signs flicker low. A warm desert wind rolls over the rooftop. On the edge, legs dangling over, sit Kathy and Gilley. An empty beer can between them. A busted practice amp humming softly nearby.

Below: Vegas snores.

Above: Two bandmates balancing between history and disaster.

---

**GILLEY (stretching, grinning):**
You know why I’m in this, right?

**KATHY (dry):**
Let me guess. Artistic expression?

**GILLEY (grinning):**
Women. Always has been. Always will be. The music? The sweat? The screaming? 
It’s just… mating. I don’t care if they know my name—just that they remember how I made ‘em feel.

**KATHY (skeptical, lighting a cigarette):**
So the revolution’s just foreplay to you?

**GILLEY**
Exactly. And tomorrow? I’m giving the most electric performance of my dumb, reckless, beautiful young life.

(leans back, watching the stars disappear)

I’m gonna make the Strip blush.

**KATHY (narrowing her eyes):**
You promise me that… and deliver it…no dropped notes, no mugging, no drunk vamping…Then maybe. Maybe. I buy you a private encore with Amanda and her snake.

**GILLEY (eyes widening like Christmas):**
Michael Douglas?

**KATHY (fake smile):**
Yeah. The snake, not the actor.

**GILLEY (putting a hand over his heart):**
Katherine Espich, you’ve just given me purpose.

**KATHY**
Don’t call me Katherine. And don’t you dare embarrass me out there. 

**GILLEY (solemnly):**
You have my word. Tomorrow, I go full legend. For you. For the band. And for Michael Fucking Douglas.

**KATHY (flicking ash, staring into the city below):**
Then let’s burn this place down.

---

**INT. SARAH’S HOTEL ROOM – 4:37 A.M. – DAY OF THE STRIP SHOW**

The bed is untouched.  The window’s cracked, letting in the neon static of Vegas at half-lung.  Sarah Malcom is pacing barefoot, in a threadbare tank top and black slacks, a yellow legal pad in one hand, her third cup of hotel coffee in the other.  She stares at the wall, where she’s taped up a hand-drawn battlefield map of the Strip:

Stage Point. KTNV Camera Units. Electrical Tap. Exit Routes. Crowd Angles. Possible Cop Bottlenecks.

Underneath it all: **OPERATION STARFALL.**

**SARAH** (to herself):
Five stars. Concert review or Eisenhower’s shoulder board. And either way, I’m the one getting people killed if it goes wrong.

(She circles a spot on the map—“hot mic zone”)

This has to hit. Has to hum. Has to sting.

She checks her clipboard again:

* KTNV Confirmed: “Rolling coverage”
* Backup Generator: Delivered
* Guerrilla Camera Op: Paid in cash & weed
* Band ETA: Unpredictable
* Police ETA: Sooner than that

**SARAH (quietly, tired but dangerous):**
Miles to go before I sleep…

(beat)

…and sleep’s not coming.

(longer beat)

Sex either.

(she winces, looks at the ceiling)

God, Gilley.  You stupid, beautiful, half-naked pyromaniac.

(closes her eyes for one long moment)

I want you in bed. Instead I’ve got you on a milk crate with a stolen mic and a death wish.

She looks in the mirror—worn, wild-eyed, hair pinned back like a general at 0200.

**SARAH (to her reflection):**
You want soft? Wrong war. This is about impact. Immortality. And making Las Vegas cry blood through its mascara.

(grabs the walkie-talkie off the table)

**SARAH** (into radio):
Team 1, check sound rig. Team 2, confirm KTNV position. Streetlight kill switch—one hour before showtime. Tell the ice cream guy to run decoy. And make sure the drummer hasn’t wandered off to marry a waitress again.

(pause)
Let’s bring the noise.

---

**EXT. LAS VEGAS STRIP – 5:17 P.M. – THE DAY OF THE SHOW**

Tourists gather near the faux Roman fountains, slurping frozen margaritas the size of toddlers. Street performers pose as Elvis, Iron Man, and an Elvis-Iron-Man hybrid. KTNV’s camera crew adjusts tripods in the shadow of a palm tree wrapped in duct-taped extension cords. Tension is molten.

And then—**THE VAN SCREECHES INTO FRAME.**

A rented, barely-street-legal Dodge Ram rattles into a red zone, parks diagonally on purpose. Doors fling open.

**THE BAND HAS ARRIVED.**

GILLEY is shirtless, of course. Windblown, glistening, sunglasses on at dusk. He throws open the van’s side door like he’s invading returning to the Philippines. BILL hops out carrying three synths and a boom box strapped to his back like a cyberpunk Sherpa.
JEFF emerges adjusting cables and philosophy in the same motion, muttering something about “loudness wars and moral clarity.” JIM jumps down shirtless except for a tie, holding a snare drum like a sacred artifact, chewing a matchstick like he’s in *Cool Hand Luke*.

And then…KATHY.

Steps down from the van in a long-sleeve thermal, frayed jeans, zero makeup, barefoot. She looks like she just rolled out of a basement gig in Belltown after two packs of Camel Lights and an argument with God.

**A TOURIST (whispering):**
That’s her? The girl who sings Not Taken Kindly?

**HER FRIEND:**
Looks like she’s about to play at a grief support group.

**SARAH** (power-walking toward them):
Where the fuck have you been?

**GILLEY (grinning, hoisting a busted amp):**
We had a… gear issue.

(cut to: Jeff sitting on the amp in the van eating Fritos while everyone else loaded up. The issue was Jeff.)

**SARAH**
We’re live in thirty. KTNV is already rolling B-roll of your ugly mugs.

(She looks Kathy over—no glitz, no gloss, not even a whisper of Vegas shimmer.)

**SARAH (softly, just to her):**
You look like you’re ready to torch a poetry reading in Tacoma.

**KATHY (dead-eyed):**
Good.  Let them think I’m soft. Then I’ll scream until they feel the bones in their feet rattle.

(beat)

Besides… Vegas dresses for me.

**BILL (to Jeff):**
Why do I feel like this ends in either a Grammy or a felony?

**JEFF:**
Because we earned both.

**SARAH (clapping twice):**

Alright. Gilley—amp to zone two. Bill—synth check now. Kathy—vocal warm-up or throat punch, your call.

(walkie to mouth)

Team 2, confirm power. Team 3, ice cream decoy in motion. Let’s blow the roof off a city that doesn’t believe in ceilings.

**INT. IMPERIAL PALACE – SERVICE CORRIDOR – 5:42 P.M. – 18 MINUTES TO SHOWTIME**

The Strip is surging. KTNV is adjusting levels. The crowd is gathering like storm clouds and bad debt. But in a tucked-away access corridor behind a locked janitor’s door, Sarah and Kathy are having a secret, hushed, and very real moment.  Sarah’s flushed, pacing.
Kathy’s leaning against a wall, arms folded, cigarette unlit, face cool and distant—more Seattle in the rain than Sin City heat.

**SARAH** (low, intense):

I just need you to lean in a little. Just a little. You don’t have to wear sequins or straddle a mic stand like Gilley at a bachelorette party. But goddamn, Kath. You walked out of that van looking like you were on your way to an AA meeting in Tacoma.

(beat, softer)

I’ve spent the last two weeks skipping panties and bras, whispering promises into DJ ears and, yes, letting one of them cop a feel—for this band.

(beat)

For you.

---

**KATHY (steady, unreadable):**
You let someone feel you up for airplay?

**SARAH (not flinching):**
I let someone feel me up because he thought it would buy thirty seconds of air. I smiled, buttoned my coat, and handed her the goddamn tape anyway. Because that’s what it took.

(closer now, voice firm)

And now I need you to show the Strip what I fought for. You don’t have to sell sex, Kath.
But stop burying it.

(points to Kathy’s outfit)

Your drapes proclaim *revolution*. The carpet mutters “*I hope no one talks to me in the record store*.”  Find the middle ground.

**KATHY (quietly, almost frowning):**
You want me to be seductive.

**SARAH**:
I want you to show the power that’s already there. You don’t have to wink. Just stop hiding like it’s 1989 and someone might call you a slut.

(beat)

Own what you are. Which is dangerous as hell.

**KATHY (soft, thoughtful):**
You think I owe you a show of respect?

**SARAH**:
I think we’re both women in a war that wasn’t built for us.  And I think I just spent two weeks bleeding at the front line. So yeah. I think maybe you could nod to that.

**KATHY (long pause, then dead serious):**
Alright. 

(She crushes the cigarette in her palm. Looks Sarah dead in the eye.)

**KATHY (CONT’D):**
I’ll start Come Inside Me on my knees. Barefoot. Face up.  Let’s see them try to forget that.

Sarah exhales. A shaky laugh. Then a grin.

**SARAH**:
Now that’s a matching goddamn set of drapes and carpet.

---

**EXT. STRIPSIDE STAGING ZONE – BACK OF THE POP-UP SETUP – 5:58 P.M. – TWO MINUTES TO SHOWTIME**

The sun is melting into the neon skyline. Tourists form a half-moon arc. KTNV’s red light flickers to LIVE. The boom mic trembles. And behind the van—Commuted is huddled in a tight, primal circle. Sarah stands just outside it. Arms crossed. Stomach twisting. 
Her heart’s racing like she’s about to go on stage herself—but she’s not. This is the moment… and it’s not hers anymore.

KATHY has her head lowered. GILLEY is practically vibrating. JIM has his arms out like a Southern preacher about to call down fire. 

**JIM (loud, rhythmic, deep):**
You are not musicians right now. You are prophets. This is scripture.  This is blood. This is confession with distortion pedals.  And if God’s watching? Make him blush.

(He slams his palms together)

Let’s fucking go.

**SARAH**, two feet away and miles out.

She watches them—this chaos-born family she helped launch—caught in a moment of furious unity she can’t touch. She gave them the city.  They’re about to take it. And she’s on the sidewalk with the mortals.

Then Kathy, voice calm but deadly, speaks.

**KATHY:**

I’m starting Come Inside Me on my knees. Head tilted. Hands flat.

(She looks up at the group)

Let them see it. Let them misinterpret it. Let them remember it forever.

**SARAH**, hearing this, lets out a breath she didn’t know she’d held.

**SARAH (to herself):**
Jesus. This is either the most powerful moment in American music history…Or I just helped orchestrate a live televised blowjob metaphor in front of four hundred tourists and a frozen custard stand.

---

Her radio squawks. 

**KTNV:** 
“We’re rolling. One minute to go. You ready?”

**SARAH** (quietly):
No.

(Then louder, snapping back to command)

**Yes. Go.**

The band breaks the huddle like gladiators entering the arena. Sarah stays behind. 
Alone. Half-mother, half-martyr. Thrilled. Horrified. Proud. Jealous. Aching to be permitted inside that circle…But she wasn’t. Not this time.


**EXT. LAS VEGAS STRIP – 6:00 P.M. SHARP – SHOWTIME**

The sky bleeds pink and violet. Neon signs flicker to full power. The crowd buzzes—half curious, half intoxicated, all unaware of what’s about to hit them. And then—Jeremy steps forward. Faded jeans. Fraying cable. Pick between his teeth. He plugs into the battered amp with the reverence of someone igniting a holy relic. He looks down once. 
Then up.

Then plays the opening riff of *After Hours*.

It’s a fishhook. Not a scream. Not a thunderclap. A sound like a cigarette lit by someone you shouldn’t trust—taunting, teasing, sin-wrapped. The crowd tilts forward. Conversations cut off mid-sentence. Plastic margaritas paused mid-sip. Even the cops on patrol look up.

Sarah, off to the side, feels it first—that ripple in the air, that hush-before-the-storm. She doesn’t breathe. Can’t.

The riff doubles. Jeremy’s fingers bite harder. The second guitar kicks in—Jeff, grim-faced, locked in. And then—Jim slams the first snare hit like a lightning bolt. Bill drops synth like holy water on sin. Gilley howls the opening line like he’s breaking up with God.

And Kathy? She walks up to the mic with a stare that could gut a city block. Still barefoot.
Still solemn. Like she’s not about to sing. Like she’s about to confess.

KTNV’s control room—somewhere down the block—erupts.

**PRODUCER:**
What the fuck is this?

**CAMERA OPERATOR:**
This is live. This is perfect. Don’t. You. Dare. Cut.

The Strip is caught. Jeremy’s riff still hangs like perfume over the pavement. The fishhook is buried in every chest. Nobody’s blinking. Nobody’s moving. Everyone is about to follow Commuted down the rabbit hole.

**EXT. LAS VEGAS STRIP – SIDEWALK POP-UP STAGE – 6:05 P.M.**

Commuted is nailing it. Like they’ve rehearsed for this moment their entire lives and didn’t know it. Like someone handed them the world’s heart and said: “Break it. Beautifully.”

Kathy’s voice is razor wire dipped in honey. Jeremy’s riffs are hunting and haunting. 
Jeff’s rhythm is ironclad. Jim is half-shaman, half-drumline from hell. Bill sounds like he’s conjuring ghosts from inside a circuit board. And Gilley? Gilley is possessed—shirt off, hair everywhere, hips like sin in motion.

But Sarah Malcom?  She’s not celebrating. She’s watching, frozen, standing half in shadow, eyes locked on the chaos she summoned into being. Not laughing. Not smiling. Just… witnessing.

A crowd of actual tourists stands thirty feet out:

* Suburban couples with fanny packs.
* Retirees who stopped walking mid-buffet-beeline.
* A bachelorette party on their fourth daiquiri.
* A seven-year-old holding a balloon.
* A cop.
* Someone filming for what will become a legendary bootleg VHS that changes someone’s life in Toledo.

None of these people are the target demo. And every single one is hooked.

---

**SARAH (to herself, breathless):**
These aren’t college town critics living off student loans and zines. These are real people. Real money. Real time.

(beat)

And they’re giving it all to us.

(longer beat, half-laughing, half-reeling)

They tested nukes north of here in the ’50s…Now I did.

(wipes sweat from her forehead)

This is above ground testing. This is legit.

She turns to see the KTNV crew slack-jawed.  One of the producers is crying. Another is muttering, “*What the fuck. What the fuck*,” like a broken rosary.

KATHY hits the second chorus of The Left Hand.  People sway. Someone yells, “Take it off!”  

Kathy doesn’t flinch. She smiles. It’s the smile of someone who’s been called a problem her whole life and just found out that’s a compliment.

Sarah grips the barricade. Her nails dig into it. Her mouth is open slightly. She wants to scream yes or finally or I did this. But instead, she just stares. Outsider status. Full. Complete. Earned. This moment isn’t hers anymore. It’s theirs. She built the bomb.

They dropped it.

**EXT. LAS VEGAS STRIP – SIDEWALK EDGE – 6:11 P.M.**

The crowd has pressed in closer, murmuring in awe, in lust, in disbelief. The air hums, heavy with sound and heat and something ancient. The final song is coming. The one no one’s ready for. The one Sarah commissioned without realizing it would cost her something she couldn’t name.

**ON STAGE**
Kathy adjusts the mic.  No fanfare.  No intro. Just a look at the band. Gilley nods once.
Jeremy picks the first chord. And then—silence. Sarah knows what comes next.

She turns away.  She can’t watch it. Not this. She moves through the edge of the crowd like a ghost. Half-proud, half-pulverized. People cheer, hoot, scream behind her as the moment begins. She hears the first line of “*Come Inside Me*,” and she winces like it struck her physically.

She knows what’s happening without looking: Kathy sinking slowly to her knees. 
Hair limp with sweat. Barefoot on Vegas pavement.  Hands flat. Chin tilted upward.
The mic between her lips like a weapon or a promise.

Sarah walks faster.

**SARAH (to herself, choked):**

I made this. I fucking made this. But I’m not inside it. I’m not her. I’m not them.

She slips behind a kiosk selling plastic Eiffel Towers. Leans against the stucco wall. 
And weeps. Not loud. Not messy. Just quiet, private grief for the distance between herself and the moment she helped birth.

**SARAH (whispering):**
Helen. The face that launched ten thousand ships.

(beat)
And all I did was draw the map…and forget I couldn’t sail.

Behind her, the crowd erupts.  She hears them scream. Not for her. Never for her. 
But she keeps walking. Because this is what a five-star general does. They command the army. They don’t die on the battlefield.

They leave that to the beautiful ones.

---

**EXT. SIDE STREET OFF THE STRIP – 6:29 P.M. – DUSK FALLING**

Sarah sits on the curb. Knees pulled up. Back against a recycling bin. Mascara streaked. 
Sweat dried into salt on her collarbone.  The show is over—but the city still echoes from it. Behind her, the Strip pulses like it’s trying to pretend nothing happened.  It did.  Everything did.
 
The crowd is dispersing, still high on it, still haunted.  Some are crying. Some are calling friends. A few just stand there, staring at where it happened, like the ground might speak again. Sarah just stares at her own hands. Still trembling.

**SARAH (softly):**
Live…They make Ric’s studio sessions look like finger painting.

(She breathes. Almost laughs.)

He captured lightning. But this? This is the hurricane. She thinks of Kathy, now cloaked in legend, walking offstage like she didn’t just punch Vegas in the throat. She thinks of Gilley—sweaty, wired, probably shirtless again—somewhere nearby, prowling for applause or ass or both. And she thinks—

**SARAH (whispering):**
Do I want to go that far?

(beat)

Do I want to stay close to the fire?

Because let’s be honest—Gilley is the flame she can touch.  Not the legend. Not the art. Not the myth. But the messy, muscular, mouthy, human part of the inferno. She can fuck him. She can mine him—afterglow pillow talk as research interviews. She can ask the questions no journalist dares.

**SARAH (to herself):**
If I keep him close…I get the stories. I get the unfiltered voltage.

And maybe, if she’s lucky…She gets to feel like she’s inside the circle again. But she also knows—Every fire leaves burns. And Gilley is a bonfire with legs and a libido.

**SARAH (quiet, almost proud):**
I built a legend today. And legends don’t come with safety instructions.

(She wipes her eyes, stands, shoulders squared.)

Maybe she does go that far. But if she does, she’ll go in knowing: It’s not love. It’s proximity to the explosion. And for Sarah Malcom?  That might be the only kind of intimacy that makes sense anymore.

---

**INT. OFF-STRIP MOTEL – BAND SUITE – 8:11 P.M. – POST-SHOW CHAOS**

The room smells like sweat, smoke, cheap bourbon, and legend. Amplifiers buzz quietly in the corner. There’s a cracked lamp, two tipped-over chairs, and a box of fries someone tried to reheat on a hot plate.  The band is wrecked. Glowing. Buzzed.  Jeff’s half-asleep, arms around a hi-hat stand like it’s a date. Bill is playing arpeggios on a Casio that isn’t plugged in. Jim’s preaching softly to a Coors can on the windowsill. Gilley, naturally, is shirtless, wearing someone else’s sunglasses, dancing in place to no music. And Kathy?

Kathy is sitting on the floor, knees pulled up, eyes sharp, cigarette untouched. Her boots are back on. Her voice is low but cuttingly clear.

**SARAH** enters quietly. She doesn’t want a scene. She just wants to see the fire still smoldering. But Kathy looks up instantly. Locks eyes.

**KATHY (softly):**
You pushed me. Gently. But hard enough.

(beat)

And you were right.

The room quiets. Even Gilley slows his groove.

**KATHY (CONT’D):**

“*Come Inside Me*” was savage tonight. Not raw. Not rough. Precise. Lethal. Filthy in a way that felt earned.

(nods once)

Thanks for the nudge.

**SARAH (surprised, touched, trying to stay cool):**

I didn’t push. I just… cleared a path.

**KATHY (smirking, tired):**
You cleared a fucking highway. With explosives.

**GILLEY (from the couch, raising a can):**

To Sarah. Our five-star general with the best damn instincts and the worst sleep schedule.

(beat)

And, one hopes, a flexible conscience.

**BILL (half-chuckling):**
She got us here. Alive. Heard. Un-arrested.

(beat)

Yet.

**SARAH (laughing despite herself):**
I’m just glad you didn’t chicken out mid-kneel, Kath.

**KATHY (stone serious):**
I wasn’t kneeling. I was kneecapping. That whole city just watched a woman reclaim the goddamn stage.

(beat)

And they’ll never forget it.

The room raises whatever drinks they have. Water. Beer. Leftover soda. A toast.

**JIM (half-sermon):**
To the war. To the gospel. To the girl with the clipboard and the plan.

**ALL (in ragged unison):**
To Sarah.

Sarah stands there, not quite inside the circle—but welcomed. Not their muse. Not their leader. Not their singer. But their flame-thrower.

---

**INT. OFF-STRIP MOTEL – BACK HALLWAY – 9:02 P.M.**

The band suite still hums—laughter, guitar noise, the low buzz of people who just changed something. Something big. Sarah steps out. The hallway is empty. Buzzing light. Concrete floor. The smell of old cigarettes and swamp-cooled air. She waits.
Not because she’s nervous. Because she’s choosing her moment.

---

**INT. MOTEL COURTYARD – MOMENTS LATER**

Gilley steps out, alone now, into the desert night. Shirtless. Always. Boots unlaced. Sweaty hair in his face. A king without a crown, high on adrenaline and god-complex sparks. He lights a cigarette, still half-smiling, like he just kissed the world and it kissed back.

**SARAH (from the shadows):**
That was the best performance of your life.

**GILLEY (not startled, just pleased):**
I know.

(He exhales, slow, amused)

You look like a girl who’s about to interrogate me. Or jump me. Or both.

**SARAH (approaching, slow and calm):**
I haven’t decided yet.  You broke something open out there tonight.

**GILLEY (softly):**
Yeah. So did you.

They stand close now. Not quite touching. The silence between them buzzes.

**SARAH**
You ever wonder what it costs, lighting fires like this?

**GILLEY**
Every time I come down. Which isn’t yet. 

(He grins)

But if you want to help with that…

She doesn’t laugh.  She just looks at him.

**SARAH**
If I sleep with you tonight, I’m not looking for tenderness.

(beat)

I want proximity to the epicenter.

(another beat)

And when it’s over, I’m going to ask you questions. Because what you said, what you sang, what you did—I need to understand it.

**GILLEY (quiet, smiling now):**
Then come burn with me.

She steps forward. Not into romance. Not into fantasy.  Into the fire she built—And now finally, fully, chooses to taste.

**INT. GILLEY’S MOTEL ROOM – LATE NIGHT**

The room is dark, still humming with aftershock. An old fan spins. The sheets are a mess.
Sarah sits at the foot of the bed, bare shoulders, legs crossed, recorder in one hand, bourbon in the other.

Gilley lies on his back, one arm over his face, the other lazily strumming nothing on an unplugged guitar. They’ve already been close. But now comes the real intimacy: the truth.


**SARAH** (calm, low):
Alright, frontman. No bullshit. What was it like… on stage?
(She clicks the recorder on, sets it on the nightstand)

Because this? This means real money. Real strategy. And real people putting their necks out. Including me.

(beat)

We’re about to open for a major act with a tenth your blood and talent. I need to know you’re ready for that.

**GILLEY (still half-dazed, arm over his eyes):**
It was like flying a jet with one wing and no windshield. It was like the crowd didn’t know whether to come or pray. And halfway through The Left Hand, I realized…they’d follow us into traffic.

(beat)

It wasn’t a concert. It was a communion.  And I was the high priest of sin.

(He finally looks at her)

You proud of us?

**SARAH** (leaning back, sipping):
I am. But pride’s for after the war.  Right now, I’m focused on supply lines.  Getting you out there. Keeping you alive. And making sure the next crowd’s twice as big and just as scared.

(beat)

I don’t want you soft. I want you dangerous. But reliable. Can you do both?

**GILLEY (smiling now):**
Only if you keep waking up next to the flame.  You’re the only one I know who’s more scared of being ordinary than being burned.

**SARAH** (quiet):
Fair.

(She clicks off the recorder)
Rest up.  You’ve got six days to be God again.

(She stands, starts pulling on her clothes)

And I’ve got calls to make.  Because people are asking what the hell just happened in Vegas…and I intend to tell them.

(beat, glancing over her shoulder)

In full detail.

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – **SARAH** MALCOM’S CUBICAL– EARLY MORNING, NEW YORK**

Fluorescent lighting hums overhead.

Coffee untouched.

Shoes off.

Sarah sits at her desk like a military strategist reviewing aerial recon.

The West Coast map is unfurled in front of her, dotted with red pins:

Seattle. Portland. Boise. Puyallup. Corvallis. Eugene. Billings. Vancouver.

Each one is a fortress.

Each one is a test.

---

**SARAH** (murmuring, writing in her notebook):

The South bled for us.

The Southwest caught fire.

Now the Northwest…

That’s the forest.

Cool, damp, guarded.

You don’t walk in screaming.

You echo what they already feel—but louder.

---

STRATEGY BOARD – Labeled: “Pacific Push: Phase One”

GOAL: Break through the indie-cred firewalls without sounding like a coastal poser with a label budget.

TARGET ONE: KEXP (Seattle)

* Approach like you’re uninvited to your own funeral.

* Get local DJ with ties to Evergreen State College to play The Left Hand during a night poetry slot.

* Deliver tapes in used manila folders, no return address, marked: “TRUTH // SIDE B.”

---

**SARAH** (typing notes):

Seattle wants pain. Not polish.

Give them Kathy. Give them tape hiss.

Make it feel like the Midwest dug this out of a grave and handed it to them.

---

Puyallup & Boise State

* Hit dorms with zines made to look photocopied six times over.

* Coordinate “midnight dorm drop” cassette leave-behinds.

* Book Kathy to call into a women’s lit class under a fake name and read lyrics like spoken word.

---

Portland \+ Corvallis \+ Eugene

* Organize underground screenings of the Vegas footage with no official branding.

* Let the legend spread organically.

* “This tape got someone suspended in Arizona. Want to hear it?”

---

Billings, Montana

* Send just one tape to the right record store with a note:

“Play Track 3 loud. If no one asks about it in 48 hours, destroy this and forget we ever existed.”

---

Vancouver, BC (CANADIAN HELL LEVEL UNLOCKED)

* Hard. Polite. Paranoid.

* Trade bootlegs with Canadian college radio heads.

* Get a sound engineer in Nanaimo to remix After Hours as a “live leak.”

* Play up the “Privatism” angle: anti-industry, anti-hype, pure rustbelt gospel.

---

**SARAH** (writing, underlining):

Midwestern Grunge Privatism \=

Not garage rock. Not punk. Not even grunge.

It’s what grunge would’ve been if no one ever heard of Sub Pop.

It’s:

You’ve never heard of us, and that’s your loss.  
We don’t want your approval.  
Just your speakers.

---

She pins a final note on the board:

PACIFIC NORTHWEST \= THE FINAL FRONT.

PLAY SOFT.

BURN SLOW.

LEAVE SCARS.

---

**INT. **SARAH**’S NOTEBOOK – SCRAWLED IN BLACK INK – UNDERLINED TWICE**

KEXP IS A WAR.

They don’t hand out cred. They withhold it.

You don’t earn your way in.

You survive long enough that they’re forced to acknowledge you.

---

WHY KEXP IS UNIQUE

1. They’re curators, not broadcasters.

    They aren’t interested in heat, hype, or chart movement.

    They don’t chase trends—they bury them before they rot.

2. They hate industry fingerprints.

    One whiff of label polish or PR spin? Dead in the water.

    They don’t want your EPK.

    They want your demo, dubbed onto a TDK cassette and left in a dented shoebox behind a co-op cafe.

3. Their listeners? Cynical AF.

    These are people who still have Bleach on vinyl, who think Interscope is the Devil, and who don’t trust a song if it doesn’t sound like it was recorded in a garage with a broken space heater.

---

THE KEXP PROBLEM:

Commuted is too good. Too tight. Too crafted.

Even at their most unhinged, there’s intent behind it.

And that makes them suspect.

To KEXP, Commuted could read like:

“A Nirvana cosplay act from Dayton with a horny marketing team and a label that thinks trauma is branding.”

That’s the fight.

---

****SARAH**’S STRATEGY (DRAFT 1 – TACTICAL ASSAULT ON SEATTLE):**

STEP ONE: Hide the label.

* Strip out Island’s fingerprints.

* Send raw board tapes. No remastering.

* Include handwritten lyric sheets, creased, water-damaged.

STEP TWO: Weaponize Kathy.

* Pitch her not as the next big thing, but as a thing they missed.

* Frame her as the ghost of the grunge girl they never gave a mic to.

STEP THREE: Lean into the myth, not the music.

* Seattle hates being told what’s next.

* So don’t tell them.

* Let them overhear it.

---

PITCH TAGLINE (never to be emailed, only whispered):

“They’re not trying to be Nirvana.  
They’re what Nirvana would’ve sounded like if they’d been fronted by a woman who never forgave the Midwest for surviving.”

---

**INT. KEXP DJ BOOTH – SEATTLE – 3:17 A.M. – JANUARY 1992**

The tape’s still spinning.

Cali’s not blinking. She’s barely moved in 20 minutes.

Ash falls from her clove cigarette onto the lyric sheet.

She hasn’t written a name.

She hasn’t said a word on air since it started.

Just played “After Hours”, then “The Left Hand”, and—God help her—a portion of “Come Inside Me” before the FCC whisper in her brain made her kill the fader.

---

She leans back in her chair.

CALI (to herself):

This isn’t revival.

This is a goddamn reckoning.

She picks up the torn photo from the envelope again—Kathy’s blurred, screaming.

Half-naked.

Half-divine.

She lights a second clove and rolls a sheet of copy paper into the typewriter.

---

**ALT-WEEKLY HEADLINE – THE STRANGER – THURSDAY EDITION**

THE CHURCH OF MIDWESTERN PRIVATISM  
A cassette arrived in the dead of night. It didn’t ask for permission. It didn’t even leave a name. It just played. And now I’m different. You will be too.

By Cali St. James

“These aren’t tourists pretending to scream.  
This is the sound of rust, religion, and orgasms screamed through a cracked windshield at 90 mph.  
A band with no name (yet) just invaded the Northwest.  
You want to know what grunge would sound like if it grew up in a basement in Dayton instead of a heroin flat in Capitol Hill?  
Find this tape.  
Lock the door.  
Play it loud.  
And if you’re lucky, it’ll leave something behind.”

---

**EXT. PULLYUP, WASHINGTON – RAIN-SOAKED STREET – TWO DAYS LATER**

Sarah Malcom stands in the gray drizzle, clipboard under one arm, The Stranger folded in her coat pocket.

She’s found a one-bedroom over a closed dry cleaner.

The power’s already spotty.

The heat rattles like a broken amp.

Perfect.

---

**SARAH** (to herself, reading the last line again):

Lock the door.

Play it loud.

And if you’re lucky…

(She smiles.)

I don’t believe in luck.

(beat)

I believe in detonation.

---

She walks to the payphone outside the corner diner.

Drops a quarter.

Dials long distance.

**SARAH** (into the receiver):

Get me Commuted.

Tell them to pack for rain.

Seattle doesn’t know it yet,

but they’re about to be converted.

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – **WYLER**’S OFFICE – NYC – MID-JANUARY 1992**

Jonathan Wyler, Sarah’s boss and official chain-of-command pain-in-the-ass, is pacing his office in a fury that’s equal parts frustration, admiration, and fear of losing control of his most dangerous asset.

Phone in one hand.

Faxed copy of The Stranger in the other.

Sarah’s name is nowhere on the article—and that’s what makes it more terrifying.

---

**WYLER** (into speakerphone, pacing):

Yes, I know she’s in Washington.

Yes, I know she’s not answering her beeper.

No, I don’t know what town she’s living in—Poo-what? Pull-what?

(slams the paper on his desk)

She’s out there booking dive bars, converting disc jockeys, baptizing college towns in tape hiss and feedback…

And I haven’t heard a damn word since Vegas.

(beat)

Great. Fucking. Work.

(to himself now, pinching the bridge of his nose)

I’m not her dad.

She doesn’t get to just ghost me.

(grabs the phone, dials her direct)

---

**INT. PAYPHONE OUTSIDE PULLYUP DINER – SAME MOMENT**

Sarah’s dialing Commuted when her beeper lights up.

She sees “212” flash.

Rolls her eyes.

Calls back with a grin.

---

**SARAH** (dry):

Wyler.

Breathe into a paper bag before you stroke out.

---

**WYLER** (cracking, but relieved):

You absolute maniac.

I’ve got college station interns calling my office asking if you’re an oracle or a cult leader.

(beat)

I mean it: great fucking work.

But Jesus, Sarah—call me, maybe?

(mocking)

I’m not your dad.

I’m the dude who certifies your pay slip.

---

**SARAH** (grinning into the phone):

Relax.

We just cracked Seattle open with a bootleg cassette and a whisper campaign.

Puyallup’s next. Then Portland. Corvallis. Billings if they can plug in.

(beat)

I’m not building buzz.

I’m building mythology.

---

**WYLER**:

Yeah, well, mythology doesn’t sign invoices.

I need numbers.

I need tour schedules.

I need to tell upper brass why I just let my youngest hire operate like she’s running her own rogue label from a strip mall above a laundromat.

---

**SARAH**:

You didn’t let me do anything, Wyler.

You just haven’t caught up yet.

(beat)

I’ll fax you a schedule.

Maybe a poem.

---

**WYLER** (pausing):

Just… don’t forget who helped give you the match, alright?

**SARAH** (smiling)

I didn’t forget.

But I’m the one who lit the fuse.

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – EXECUTIVE CONFERENCE ROOM – NYC – JANUARY 1992**

Wyler’s in full pitch mode.

The long mahogany table is lined with senior execs, some wearing suits, some wearing “cool” suits (translation: no tie, slightly worse).

Overhead: the whine of a carousel slide projector.

On-screen: a blurry photo of Kathy, mid-scream on the Vegas Strip, barefoot, backlit by neon.

**WYLER** (clipped, confident):

Gentlemen.

This is not a flash-in-the-pan, regional noise act.

This is a generational combustion engine.

And the one person who saw that coming?

Was our youngest quant analyst.

---

SLIDE 2: A hand-labeled airplay graph with “AFTER HOURS” scrawled at the top. The spike hits like a missile.

**WYLER**:

This is the KEXP bump.

Unsolicited. Unpaid. Untagged.

(taps the board)

Sarah Malcom dropped an unbranded cassette in a dead-of-night mailer and made a Northwest tastemaker ask, “What the hell just hit me?”

---

SLIDE 3: A crude map. Puyallup, Portland, Corvallis, Boise, Billings—pinned and connected with string like a serial killer wall.

**WYLER**:

This is her strategic path.

Not coast-first. Not press-blitzed.

Grassroots ignition.

She’s lighting brushfires where the majors don’t even scout anymore.

---

EXEC \#1 (cynical):

So what are they? Midwestern Nirvana cosplay?

**WYLER** (with a grin he didn’t earn but is borrowing beautifully):

They’re what grunge sounds like without industry guilt.

What happens when a girl like Kathy Espich doesn’t ask for the mic—she builds her own.

(beat)

Sarah calls it Midwestern Grunge Privatism.

I call it a fucking movement.

---

EXEC \#2:

This all hangs on one analyst’s data modeling and a band that closes with a song called Come Inside Me?

(dry)

That’s a hell of a hill to die on.

**WYLER** (quiet, now deadly serious):

It is.

And I’m standing on it.

Because Malcom’s not just forecasting the fire—she’s fanning it.

She’s delivering tape-delayed chaos with receipts.

(hands out the data packet)

This is real feedback. Real airplay. Real audience response.

(beat)

We always say we want to find the future before it goes corporate?

Well, she already did.

And she’s living in a one-bedroom above a dry cleaner in Puyallup because she believes it matters.

---

EXEC \#1 (flipping through the data):

She’s either the next big thing…

Or you’re betting the house on some horny kids from Dayton.

**WYLER**:

I am.

(beat)

Because they’re connected.

To rage, to sex, to sorrow.

And she—Sarah—she knows how to package that in a way people don’t realize they’ve been waiting for.

---

He clicks off the projector.

The room goes still.

**WYLER** (final):

You want to be first?

You follow her.

Or we can wait to buy the rights back from Sub Pop in two years for triple the price.

(beat)

Your call.

---

The machine is turning. You decide where the gears grind next.

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – **WYLER**’S OFFICE – LATER THAT NIGHT**

The pitch meeting is over.

The slides are packed away.

But Wyler’s pulse is still racing.

He sits at his desk, sleeves rolled up, tie hanging like a white flag, staring at the glowing fax machine as it churns out a new memo from Seattle.

Sarah’s latest: a typed schedule, a hand-scrawled venue list, and a Post-it note that reads:

“You want Summer? You’ve got to pay for Winter.” — S.

---

He pours two fingers of bourbon.

Doesn’t drink yet.

Just leans back.

**WYLER** (to himself):

She wants post-production.

(He shakes his head, smirking at the absurdity)

She wants to take a barefoot blowjob performance on the Vegas Strip shot on shaky Hi8 and turn it into something MTV can’t ignore by June.

(beat)

That’s not confidence.

That's a delusion backed by momentum.

---

He opens his drawer, pulls out a budget folder.

Five figures. High five.

For what?

A maybe-viral VHS montage of an unsigned band screaming into a city that didn’t ask for them?

No. Not unsigned.

Signed by him.

---

**WYLER** (mocking her in a fond tone):

You want money to turn that guerrilla footage into something usable?

You want an editor, a colorist, someone to figure out how to frame Kathy on her knees in front of a fountain without setting off every red phone at Standards & Practices?

You want all that… for a band the suits still think is a novelty act?

(beat)

Goddamn you, Sarah.

You might be right.

---

He picks up the phone.

Calls Finance.

**WYLER** (into the receiver):

This is Wyler.

I need a hold on post-production discretionary.

Yeah. West Coast artist. No, not one you’ve heard of.

(smiles bitterly)

She hasn’t even shot the real footage yet.

But I’m betting she will.

Because I’d rather write a five-figure check today than watch MTV license this shit from Geffen in a year.

---

He hangs up.

Drinks.

Finally.

**WYLER** (to the empty office):

Novelties don’t start riots.

But this girl just might.

---

**INT. BELLINGHAM, WA – MAKESHIFT EDIT SUITE – NIGHT**

Rain taps against the cracked window.

Old CRT monitors flicker.

The room smells like solder, stale popcorn, and pre-viral ambition.

Kathy sits cross-legged on a broken couch, hair up, hoodie off one shoulder, eyes fixed on the edit screen.

The rough cut is paused.

Frame frozen:

Kathy, knees on the pavement, lips at the mic, gaze upturned—not pleading, not submissive—just… electric.

---

EDITOR (nervous, mid-20s, indie film dropout):

We can cut this sooner if it’s too much.

The kneel, I mean.

KATHY (without looking at him):

Why would you cut the moment everyone’s going to remember?

(beat)

That’s not what I felt.

---

She watches it again.

This time, from start to finish.

No overdub. No polish. Just raw tape: Vegas. Sunset. Her.

Kathy on her knees.

Kathy with a voice like broken glass and satin.

Kathy commanding the Strip without raising her volume.

---

KATHY (softly):

I didn’t feel…

Sexy.

(beat)

I felt dangerous.

But this— (gestures to the screen)

—this looks like I’m doing something for them.

Not to them.

---

She rewinds. Watches the same ten seconds again.

She studies her own body language.

The tilt of her head.

The way the mic cord wraps around her hand like it’s chained to her.

She sees sensuality, but also voltage.

And more than that—recognition.

---

KATHY (muttering, almost afraid of the words):

This is going to unsettle people.

(beat)

Especially women.

Especially the ones who know exactly what it feels like to be down there…

…but never got to do it on their own terms.

---

EDITOR (tentative):

You sure you want to keep it?

(beat)

Because this moment—it’s not just music anymore.
