GILLEY (with fake solemnity):

Thank you, Oklahoma.

You’ve been a dream.

---

KATHY (to Sarah, licking her last dot):

Next album?

Let him solo once.

(beat)

He earned it tonight.

---

**SARAH** (smirking):

Maybe.

If he promises to never use the word “onion” again.

---

They reach the van, still smiling.

Not rockstars.

Not legends.

Just three kids on fire in the middle of America.

---

**INT. COMMUTED VAN – OKLAHOMA CITY – PARKING LOT, OUTSIDE THE ARCADE – APRIL 7, 1992 – 10:03 P.M.**

The van doors slam shut behind them.

Kathy tosses her empty Dippin’ Dots cup into the footwell like a basketball shot she knows she’s going to miss.

She’s still grinning, post-pinball high, harmonica still rattling faintly in Gilley’s hand.

But then—

KATHY (half-laughing, half-serious):

I’m serious though.

Next album?

Let him solo once.

---

**SARAH** (not missing a beat, eyes forward in the passenger seat):

Kathy—

(turns to her, pointed)

You’re in the band.

I’m not.

(beat)

You want Gilley to blow some lungs on the record?

Take it up with the Evans brothers.

---

KATHY (mock gasp):

You’re deflecting.

---

**SARAH** (shrugs):

No.

I’m deferring.

(beat, smiling faintly)

You try wrangling Bill when he thinks someone’s touching his sonic landscape.

Or Jeremy when you mention adding “texture.”

---

GILLEY (from the back, harmonica between his teeth):

Texture? I am texture, baby.

---

**SARAH** (snorts, still focused on Kathy):

You got opinions?

You got power?

(beat, level)

Then speak up.

Or don’t.

(long pause)

But if you don’t?

(leans in, teasing but firm)

Then you’re godless.

---

KATHY (squinting):

Did you just weaponize blasphemy in a band meeting?

---

**SARAH** (smirking, settling back in her seat):

Only a little.

(beat)

Look, all I’m saying is: if you want him in the mix?

You own the mic.

Don’t hand it to me.

---

KATHY (after a beat, quietly):

Fair.

---

GILLEY (harmonica in lap, grinning):

Y’all can debate me later.

For now?

(he flicks on the radio, low volume)

Let’s get moving.

Tulsa ain’t gonna know what hit it.

---

The van pulls out of the lot.

Oklahoma fades into the dark behind them.

Ahead: miles of highway.

Inside: a band building its next myth.

---

**INT. COMMUTED VAN – SOMEWHERE BETWEEN OKLAHOMA CITY AND TULSA – APRIL 7, 1992 – 11:24 P.M.**

The van hums steady over cracked asphalt, headlights carving tunnels through the dark.

The others are quiet.

Kathy’s half-asleep, hood pulled up, headphones on.

Sarah’s in the passenger seat, flipping through the next day’s itinerary by the faint glow of a mini reading light, eyes focused, shoulders tight.

Gilley is in the back bench seat, sprawled out like he owns the night.

The harmonica rests on his chest, one hand lightly holding it.

He’s humming, low and rhythmic—an echo of “Whammer Jammer,” smoothed into something softer, dirtier, his.

---

He taps the harmonica once against his knee.

The melody drifts into a different key, a different mood—something lazy, humid, and hungry.

GILLEY (softly, in his head):

Maybe they will.

---

His perfect day’s plan?

Ice cream ✅

Pinball ✅

The crowd ✅

The myth? Growing ✅

Now?

He’s got one more checkbox.

---

He glances up front.

Kathy.

Tired.

Cooling down from the spotlight.

Her energy fading out like stage fog.

She’ll want a shower and sleep.

He can gently steer her that way.

---

Sarah.

Still tense.

Still electric.

Still too alert for someone running on no sleep.

She doesn’t know it, but he can read her tells.

She leaned in a little closer earlier.

Laughed longer than she meant to.

There’s something alive between them.

And Gilley?

He knows how to feed a fire without burning down the house.

---

GILLEY (to himself, eyes half-closed):

She’ll taste just like honey.

(beat)

Sweet.

Slow.

And earned.

---

The van rocks slightly with a bump in the road.

He closes his eyes again, the harmonica resting against his lips now, just the cool metal and a thought in his throat.

---

Tomorrow?

He’ll find his moment.

He always does.

And this time?

He wants both girls going opposite ways—so he can meet one behind closed doors, with nothing but time, charm, and heat on his side.

---

He plays one low, long note on the harmonica—

soft and haunting, like a promise he’s absolutely sure he can keep.

---

**INT. TULSA HOTEL – GILLEY’S ROOM – APRIL 8, 1992 – 2:03 A.M.**

The room is dark save for the dull gold glow of a lamp near the bed.

TV’s off.

Shades drawn.

Outside, the street hums with a few late cars and wind against old signage.

Gilley sits on the edge of the bed, legs apart, pen in hand, a crumpled notepad balanced on one thigh.

The harmonica rests nearby, silent for once.

He’s shirtless, still damp from a too-hot shower, hair curling at the edges.

The hotel keycard is tossed onto the dresser like he’s daring fate to use it.

---

On the notepad, across torn-out lines and abandoned couplets, something has started to take shape.

At the top, in his tight, all-caps handwriting:

SOMETHING SWEET AND UNSPOKEN

---

He’s not like Jeff—who builds lyrics like blueprints, structural and sacred.

And he’s definitely not Kathy—who bleeds her verses out raw like they’re carved from the inside.

Gilley writes like he flirts—careful, deliberate, hiding truth in timing.

He doesn’t enjoy it.

But he’s good at it.

---

He scrawls:

She walks like her silence has claws,  
Smiles like she’s got one lie left.  
But when she touches my wrist,  
She’s all sugar, no threat.

---

He stops.

Runs a hand through his hair.

Listens to the empty room.

No knock.

Not yet.

---

He writes again.

She doesn’t need me to mean it,  
Just to know what it meant.  
So I wait in the dark,  
Half honest, half bent.

---

He taps the pen against the page.

Then underlines the last line twice.

Hard.

Ink nearly bleeds through.

---

GILLEY (softly, into the quiet):

Come on, sugar.

(beat)

We’re both up.

---

But there’s only silence.

And the slow, ticking rhythm of time not yet chosen.

---

He stares at the door.

Waiting.

For the knock.

For her.

For permission.

---

**INT. TULSA HOTEL ROOM – GILLEY’S BED – APRIL 8, 1992 – 3:04 A.M.**

**The bedside lamp casts a low amber glow, dimmed now, reflecting off sweat on his collarbone and the notepad that’s grown fat with ink and adrenaline.**

**Eight pages.**  
 **Full lyrics.**  
 ***SOMETHING SWEET AND UNSPOKEN* now lives, breathes, and hits like a damn truck.**

**The room is dead quiet.**

**Still *no knock.***

---

**Gilley stretches, bones creaking, shoulders twitching from the grind of adrenaline and rejection.**  
 **But his grin?**

**Still there.**  
 **Weary. But proud.**

**He leans back against the headboard, notepad flat on his chest, skimming the last chorus again:**

***Velocity 100, every rule's broken***  
 ***Cherry gloss, electric cry***  
 ***Down in Ohio, we burn and fly***

---

**GILLEY (softly):**  
 **Yeah.**

**(*smirks to himself*)**  
 **We *do.***

---

**He reaches for his little tape recorder, clicks it on, and murmurs the title.**

***“Something Sweet and Unspoken. Draft one complete.***  
 ***Might be the best thing I’ve written since… hell, ever.”***

**(*beat*)**

***“Still alone. But damn, this’ll play loud.”***

---

**He hits stop.**  
 **Sets it on the nightstand.**  
 **One last look at the door.**

**Still nothing.**

**He exhales.**

**Not bitter.**

**Just *not surprised.***

---

**GILLEY (whispering, to no one):**  
 **It’s okay, sugar.**  
 **You missed your verse.**

**(*grinning, turning off the light*)**  
 **But I *nailed mine.***

---

**The room goes dark.**

**The pages still hum.**

**The song’s alive.**

**And tomorrow?**

***Everyone’s gonna hear it.***

---

**INT. TULSA HOTEL – **SARAH**’S ROOM – APRIL 8, 1992 – 8:27 A.M.**

**The sun’s already *too bright* through the thin hotel curtains.**

**Sarah jolts awake, tangled in her own sheets, mouth dry, head foggy with *regret and half-formed plans*.**  
 **The clock reads *8:27*.**  
 **She was up past 2, debating.**  
 **Her last clear memory is sitting on the edge of the bed, staring at her shoes and *trying to decide.***

**She *meant* to go to him.**

**She *was going* to go.**

**But she *fell asleep*.**

---

****SARAH** (groaning to herself):**  
 ***Dammit, Sarah.***

---

**She stumbles out of bed, still in yesterday’s blouse, grabs her bag, and notices—**

**A piece of paper.**

**Folded. Slid halfway under her door.**

**Her name is written on the outside in *Gilley’s handwriting.***

**She opens it fast, heart in her throat.**

---

**Inside:**

***Thought you might want to see what you missed.***  
 ***SOMETHING SWEET AND UNSPOKEN.***  
 ***Typed. 3:04 A.M.***

**Attached—a photocopy of eight handwritten pages.**  
 **Scanned from his notebook.**

**Full lyrics.**

**All of it.**

---

**She starts reading.**  
 **By the second verse, she sits down.**  
 **By the chorus, she’s gripping the side of the bed.**

***“Cherry bomb smile, heart’s unbroken***  
 ***Swallowing truths that go unspoken”***

***“Lips to lips, I’m losing control***  
 ***Ice cream kiss, swallowin’ soul”***

***“Down in Ohio, we burn and fly”***

---

****SARAH** (whispers):**  
 **You *wrote this last night?***

---

**She closes her eyes.**

***He didn’t wait.***

**He didn’t come knocking.**

**He *created.***

**And now she’s reading what *should’ve been shared between skin and sweat and something soft*—**  
 **but instead, it’s been *immortalized* without her.**

---

****SARAH** (fists the pages):**  
 ***Dammit, Sarah.***  
 ***Get your act together.***

---

**She stands fast.**  
 **Already pacing.**

**Because this isn’t *just about him.***

**It’s a *reminder.***

**These people?**

***These artists?***

**They’re *fucking dangerous.***

**They turn *every missed moment into art.***  
 **Every delay into *a detonator.***  
 **Every emotion into *something public and unforgettable.***

**And *she’s the one trying to manage that.***

---

****SARAH** (to herself):**  
 **You fall asleep once,**  
 **and they *write the hit single without you.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **Don’t *ever* do it again.**

---

**She folds the lyric pages with shaking hands, tucks them into her planner.**

**War-time.**

**No more missed moves.**

---

**INT. TULSA VENUE – BACKSTAGE GREEN ROOM – APRIL 8, 1992 – 2:12 P.M.**

**It’s loud—Jim’s tuning snare in the next room, someone’s amp is humming with impatience, and Gilley’s harmonica is mercifully quiet.**

**Sarah sits at a folding table, planner open, Gilley’s lyrics tucked between pages like a secret too heavy to carry in a purse.**

**But Kathy’s standing over her, cup of shitty venue coffee in hand, one eyebrow raised, reading the lyric sheet over her shoulder with a smirk forming as she goes.**

**By the first chorus, she’s nodding.**  
 **By the second, she’s whispering the lines under her breath.**

**By the end, she leans in and says—very clearly:**

---

**KATHY:**  
 ***Holy shit.***  
 **Is this about *you*?**

---

****SARAH** (instantly):**  
 ***No.***

**(*too fast, too sharp*)**  
 **Absolutely not.**

---

**KATHY (grinning):**  
 **Come on, “ice cream kiss” and “Ohio haze”?**  
 **You're *from New York* but you’re *burning in Dayton’s orbit.***

---

****SARAH** (snatching the pages, flushing):**  
 **It’s not about me.**

**It’s just… *him being poetic.***  
 **Wild, metaphor-loaded. You know Gilley.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **He *romanticizes vending machines*.**

---

**KATHY (leaning back, arms crossed):**  
 **Sure.**  
 **And he *accidentally* wrote the most *emotionally coherent* thing I’ve seen from him, ever?**

**(*beat*)**  
 **Nah.**  
 **This has *teeth.***

---

**Sarah tries to go back to her clipboard.**

**Fails.**

**Her pen hovers midair.**

---

**KATHY (tapping the lyrics):**  
 **This is *tight.***  
 **We’re getting this down when we hit *Dayton* again.**

**(*smirks*)**  
 **I don’t care if he wrote it with *his dick and a flashlight.***

**It *works.***

---

**She turns, shouts toward the hallway:**

**KATHY:**  
 ***GILLEY\!***

**Get your *mystery muse ass* in here.**

**We’re *cutting this.***

---

****SARAH** (muttering, too low to hear):**  
 **…Jesus.**

---

**KATHY (grinning, walking off):**  
 **Big shoutout to whatever *anonymous swirl cone* inspired this masterpiece\!**

---

**Sarah sighs, rests her head in her hands for a second, then pulls herself together.**

**Because now the song’s *alive*.**  
 **And she can’t kill it.**

**All she can do?**

***Control how it spreads.***

---

**INT. VENUE LOBBY – PAYPHONE ALCOVE – TULSA – APRIL 8, 1992 – 3:47 P.M.**

**The green paint on the wall is peeling in strips.**  
 **There’s a soda machine humming like it’s planning its own retirement.**  
 **The payphone cord is sticky.**

**Sarah stands with one arm braced against the wall, receiver cradled to her ear, holding her clipboard like a riot shield.**

**The line clicks.**

---

****WYLER** (on the other end):**  
 **Island.**

---

****SARAH** (measured):**  
 **It’s Malcom. I’m calling in from Tulsa.**

**I need to flag something that’s… in motion.**

**(*beat*)**  
 ***Do not panic.***

---

****WYLER** (instantly interested):**  
 **If you open with “do not panic,” I’m *already* panicking.**

---

****SARAH**:**  
 **We have… a new song.**

***Unscheduled.***

***Unapproved.***

***Unfiltered.***

---

****WYLER**:**  
 **From Kathy?**

---

****SARAH** (quiet):**  
 **No.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **From *Gilley.***

---

****WYLER** (dead silence):**  
 **…What?**

---

****SARAH**:**  
 **It’s called *“Something Sweet and Unspoken.”***  
 **He wrote it in his hotel room at 3 a.m.**

**Eight pages.**  
 **Power chords.**  
 **Blistering verses.**  
 **It’s *punk confession with sugar on top and sex underneath.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **Kathy read it this morning and immediately greenlit a *Dayton session.***

---

****WYLER** (still stunned):**  
 **You’re saying *Gilley* wrote the *next single?***

---

****SARAH** (tighter):**  
 **I’m saying *it’s happening.***

**With or without our coordination.**

---

****WYLER**:**  
 **Is it good?**

---

****SARAH** (quietly, honestly):**  
 **It’s *dangerous.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **And it might be *the most deranged romantic gesture* I’ve ever received in my *entire* life.**

---

****WYLER** (long pause):**  
 **Sarah…**

**(*slower, careful*)**  
 **Are you *involved*?**

---

****SARAH** (snaps):**  
 **I *manage the account.***

**(*pause*)**  
 **I *do not* date it.**

---

****WYLER** (calm now):**  
 **Okay.**  
 **Then manage this.**

**Make it look like *we planned it.***  
 **Spin it. Guide it.**  
 **And for God’s sake, don’t leave *any* paper trail.**

---

****SARAH** (quietly):**  
 **Understood.**

---

**She hangs up slowly.**

**Stares at the receiver for a moment.**

**Then writes at the bottom of her clipboard in small, hard letters:**

**\*This is how the job ends.**  
 **Not in failure.**  
 **But in a *hit single I didn’t see coming.***  
 **From a man who *saw me too clearly.***

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – **WYLER**’S OFFICE – NEW YORK CITY – APRIL 8, 1992 – 5:32 P.M. (EST)**

**Wyler’s pacing.**

**His tie’s off.**  
 **Rolodex open.**  
 **Three messages from legal flagged *URGENT*—ignored.**

**He’s got a copy of Sarah’s fax in his hand: a clean typeset of Gilley’s "Something Sweet and Unspoken" lyrics.**

**He reads it again, lips pursed, eyes narrowing.**

---

***“Cone in my hand, cold thrill in my grip / Tastes like trouble with a sugar-dipped tip”***

---

****WYLER** (to himself):**  
 **Where the *hell* was this hiding?**

---

**He drops into his chair, turns in a slow circle, then snaps upright and starts muttering like someone trying to undo a prophecy.**

---

****WYLER**:**  
 **Gilley was supposed to be *safe.***

**A *known variable.***

**Charisma on legs.**  
 **Smile like a switchblade, but *harmless* if you kept him off the creative leash.**

**(*points to air*)**  
 **The *thinking* was:**

* **Middling guitar player.**

* **Indifferent writer.**

* **Rides the *Jeff/Kathy combo*.**

* **Sits comfortably under *Jeremy’s riffs*.**

* **Gets *elevated* by *Bill’s synthscapes.***

**He *skates*.**

**He *winks*.**

**He *sells T-shirts.***

---

**He slams the lyric sheet down on his desk.**

---

****WYLER** (low, amazed):**  
 **And now he’s writing *like this?***

---

**He picks up the phone. Doesn’t dial. Just holds it.**

**Because now?**

**If this hits?**  
 **They *can’t* market him as the smile on the poster anymore.**

**Now he’s *dangerous.***

**Now he’s *credible.***

**Now he’s *a voice.***

---

**And that means:**

1. ***Creative leverage.***

2. ***Band dynamics shifting.***

3. ***Sarah, walking a razor blade without a net.***

---

****WYLER** (finally, with a grim smile):**  
 **We’re gonna have to *rewrite the whole narrative* around him.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **And *pray* to God he doesn’t figure out what that’s worth.**

---

**He leans back.**

**Looks at the ceiling.**

**Then picks up the lyric sheet again and whispers—**

****WYLER**:**  
 **Hell of a move, Gilley.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **I underestimated you.**  
 **Never again.**

---

**INT. TULSA VENUE – BACK OFFICE – APRIL 8, 1992 – 6:42 P.M.**

Sarah is on the venue’s landline, a beige Bakelite monstrosity mounted to the wall like a taunt from the 1950s.  
 The cord curls like a noose.

On the other end?  
 Island’s Legal Department.  
 Some junior counsel with the tone of a man who’s read one too many boilerplate contracts and not a single verse of *Come Inside Me*.

---

LEGAL (crisp, condescending):  
 Sarah, if Gilley’s now being positioned as a *primary lyricist*, we’ll need to begin *re-evaluating credit structures*.

Royalty splits. Trademark implications. We’ll have to draft provisional language. Possibly *retroactive attribution.*

---

**SARAH** (voice rising):  
 Are you *kidding me*?

---

LEGAL (calm, detached):  
 This could impact long-term IP valuation. The board needs to know who’s *actually writing the material.*

---

**SARAH** (exploding):  
 *Look at the fucking liner notes.*

All twenty tracks.

ALL. OF. THEM.

You know what every *single writing credit* says?

*Written by COMMUTED.*

Not Jeff.  
 Not Kathy.  
 Not Jeremy.  
 Not Bill.  
 Not Gilley.

*COMMUTED.*

---

LEGAL (quiet):  
 I mean… yes, but—

---

**SARAH**:  
 *This is why we fucking signed them\!*  
 Because they work like a *collective*.  
 Because they *agreed*—all of them—that every song comes from the band.

And you want to *shred that* because Gilley found a *pen and some balls for once?*

---

LEGAL:  
 I’m just saying—

---

**SARAH** (full throttle):  
 No.

*I’m saying.*

You want to *dismantle* the *only band in America* that still believes in *democracy*?

You wanna *fracture the myth* because you *got scared of a hot mic and a tight hook*?

*Then you deserve to lose them.*

---

*She slams the phone onto the receiver.*  
 *Paces.*  
 *Lifts it again—hesitates—then tries to rip it off the wall.*\*

It doesn’t budge.

The Bakelite glistens, smug. Indestructible. Immune.

---

**SARAH** (to the phone):  
 Oh, *you smug plastic son of a bitch.*

---

She tries to *slam it again.*  
 It *dings* like a bell in a boxing match.  
 Still doesn’t crack.

Sarah stands there, *breathing hard*.

And then it *hits her.*

This. This feeling.

This is why rock stars wreck hotel rooms.

---

Not because they’re spoiled.

But because *everything’s always in motion*.  
 Because *everyone wants to claim the crown without touching the throne.*  
 Because *one good night of lyrics can become a goddamn legal nightmare.*

---

**SARAH** (softly, to herself):  
 God help me…  
 I understand them now.

---

She smooths her blazer.  
 Picks up her clipboard.  
 Doesn’t look back.

Because now it’s war.

And the *plastic gods* won’t save anyone.

---

**INT. TULSA VENUE – BACK OFFICE – MOMENTS LATER – APRIL 8, 1992 – 6:47 P.M.**

**Sarah is still pacing.**

**Clipboard long forgotten.**  
 **Hands clenched.**  
 **Eyes blazing.**

**The Bakelite phone sits intact, smug, victorious on its wall mount like the last unbroken piece of the patriarchy.**

**And then—**

**Kathy steps into the room, still in her soundcheck flannel, water bottle in hand, sweat at her collarbones and heat in her eyes.**

**She sees Sarah.**

**Sees the rage.**  
 **Sees the phone.**  
 **Sees the tremble just under the control.**

---

**KATHY (dead calm):**  
 **Who do I kill?**

---

****SARAH** (doesn’t even look up):**  
 **Legal.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **And the *system* that thinks a man writing *one* song means he suddenly deserves to *own the band.***

---

**KATHY (soft, dangerous):**  
 **Let me guess—**

**They want to *split us.***

---

****SARAH**:**  
 **Already trying.**  
 **Retroactive credit clauses.**  
 **Royalty recalibration.**

**Like *Gilley* cracked open the world, and *we* just *helped*.**

---

**KATHY (quiet fury):**  
 **We bled.**  
 **We built.**  
 **We *birthed* this sound.**

**And now they want to *rewrite the history book* because he finally turned in his *homework?***

---

****SARAH** (finally looks at her):**  
 **Yeah.**

**And they’re scared.**  
 **Not of him.**  
 **Of *us.***

---

**KATHY (grins, savage):**  
 **Then let’s *burn something down.***

---

**They stand there, shoulder to shoulder.**  
 **Two women.**  
 **One clipboard.**  
 **One voicebox tuned to *hellfire*.**  
 **Both *done being polite.***

---

**KATHY (cool now):**  
 **They wanted a *frontwoman*.**

**They got *a firing squad.***

---

****SARAH** (nods, cold):**  
 **Let them try and rewrite us.**

**We *write louder.***

---

**Outside, the crowd is lining up.**  
 **Inside, the temperature is rising.**

**The band’s about to go live.**

**But *the women*?**

**They already are.**

---

**INT. TULSA VENUE – BACK OFFICE – SAME MOMENT – APRIL 8, 1992 – 6:49 P.M.**

**The fire’s still simmering behind Sarah’s eyes.**  
 **The rage from legal.**  
 **The *smug indestructibility* of the Bakelite phone.**  
 **The *reality* that one man’s late-night burst of brilliance just *threatened to upend the myth she built from blood and rhythm.***

**But Kathy?**

**She’s already flipping pages in Sarah’s clipboard, cool as a fuse waiting for spark.**

---

**KATHY (casual, dangerous):**  
 **So what’s the *agenda* for San Antonio?**

**(*beat, smirking*)**  
 **I assume there is one, since you’re the *field general with a vengeance spreadsheet.***

---

****SARAH** (tight, still fuming):**  
 **Three college radio drop-ins.**  
 **One surprise pop-up at a used vinyl dive off the River Walk.**  
 **Fan zine roundtable with the *We Bleed Loudly* girls—*bring your A-game.***

**(*flipping pages*)**  
 **I’ve got press for you with a *Latina music magazine* who *already thinks you’re bruja royalty.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **And a *private showcase* for a handful of indie labels circling like vultures in case Island screws the pooch.**

---

**KATHY (eyebrows raised):**  
 **Damn.**

**You plan revenge like it’s *war logistics.***

---

****SARAH** (flatly):**  
 **It is.**

---

**KATHY (grinning now):**  
 **What about sleep?**

---

****SARAH** (without flinching):**  
 **None scheduled.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **You *want myth?***  
 **You *live without comfort.***

---

**KATHY:**  
 **You’re mondo pissed, huh?**

---

****SARAH** (measured, voice low):**  
 **I’m not pissed.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **I’m *motivated*.**

---

**Kathy whistles, low.**

---

**KATHY (nods, folding the clipboard shut with respect):**  
 **Remind me not to *cross you.***

---

****SARAH** (turns to her):**  
 **Don’t worry.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **You’re *with* me.**

---

**Outside, the crowd starts chanting.**

**Inside, *a storm is forming.***

**And San Antonio?**

**It’s next in the *blast radius.***

---

**INT. SAN ANTONIO HOTEL – **SARAH**’S ROOM – APRIL 10, 1992 – 12:41 A.M.**

**The room is dim, her shoes are off, and Sarah is curled up on the edge of the bed, hair messy, clipboard on her lap like a lover she *trusts more than anyone else on Earth.***

**The air conditioner hums, drowning out distant street noise.**  
 **The TV glows faint blue, muted.**  
 **There’s a folder stuffed with local press clippings on the nightstand.**

**She’s flipping through her San Antonio master schedule, cross-referencing time stamps with locations, cross-checking personnel with promo plans, highlighting overlaps, scribbling notes in the margins.**

**Every cell of her brain is still in *go-mode*—even if her body is *screaming for mercy.***

**And then she pauses.**

**Stares at a block of time she *should* have filled.**  
 **Between the second radio drop and the quiet dinner with the zine girls.**  
 **A window.**

**A *four-hour window.***

**Unmarked.**

**Unused.**

**Untouched.**

---

****SARAH** (quietly, aloud):**  
 **I forgot.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **I *forgot* to schedule *Gilley.***

---

**She leans back against the headboard, closes her eyes, lets out a low, frustrated groan.**

**Not because of lust.**

**Because of *logistics.***

**Because for all the *military precision* she brings to this band’s conquest, for all her color-coded chaos and clipboard empire…**

**She *forgot to schedule her own pleasure.***

---

**Four hours.**

**Four golden, unclaimed hours.**

**A *perfect window for fire, skin, sweat, and silence.***  
 **For *finishing what they started.***

**For *tasting what he still hasn’t stopped offering.***

**And she *missed it.***

---

****SARAH** (muttering):**  
 ***Dammit.***

**This is a *conveyor belt of madness.***

---

**She grabs a pen and scribbles across the bottom margin of the page:**

***Next city: 4 hours. No excuses. Close the loop.***

**(*beat*)**

***If I’m going to command the war, I’m allowed one fucking ceasefire.***

---

**She sets the clipboard aside.**  
 **Turns off the lamp.**  
 **Curls into the quiet.**

**Tomorrow?**

**The machine spins again.**

**But tonight?**

**She mourns the *unwritten appointment.***

---

**INT. SAN ANTONIO HOTEL – GILLEY’S ROOM – APRIL 10, 1992 – 12:47 A.M.**

**The screen glows with sweaty bodies and fluorescent ropes—a PPV wrestling match halfway through the card.**  
 **Some dude in tassels just suplexed another through a table.**

**Gilley’s sprawled across his bed, half-dressed, a bowl of room service fries within reach, one boot still on, the other nowhere to be found.**

**The harmonica is on the nightstand.**

**He’s not watching the match.**

**Not really.**

**His eyes keep flicking toward the wall that separates his room from Sarah’s.**

---

**GILLEY (to himself, quiet):**  
 **Twelve-forty-seven.**

---

**He listens.**

**Hears *nothing.***

**No knock.**  
 **No footsteps.**  
 **No whispered invitation.**

---

**He leans back on his elbows.**  
 **Blankly watches a wrestler take a chair to the back.**  
 **Smirks a little.**

**Then sighs.**

**Hard.**

---

**GILLEY (muttering):**  
 **I wrote her a *goddamn song*.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **She *critiques it*.**  
 **Doesn’t *touch me*.**

**(*beat, softer*)**  
 **Maybe she *really doesn’t want this.***

---

**He pushes the fries away.**  
 **Sits up.**  
 **Runs a hand through his hair.**

**The swagger’s still there.**  
 **But the *certainty*?**

**Fading.**

---

**He glances at his wristwatch, then toward his phone.**

**Thinks about texting someone.**  
 **Anyone.**

**Thinks about *hooking up*—just to *feel wanted* again.**  
 **Someone at the venue had been obvious.**  
 **Someone local and *easy.***

---

**But he doesn’t pick up the phone.**

**Not yet.**

---

**GILLEY (quiet, to the wall):**  
 **Come on, sugar.**

**I *know* you’re in there.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **I *felt* it.**  
 **You *felt* it.**

**So why does it *feel gone now?***

---

**He stares at the harmonica.**

**Then the wall again.**

**Then turns the volume up on the TV.**

**Some guy screams, pile-drives another, and the crowd erupts.**

**Gilley?**

**He doesn't.**

**He just leans back, jaw clenched.**

**Alone.**

**Wondering.**

**If he *waits* again tonight…**

**Or if it’s time to *move on.***

---

**INT. SAN ANTONIO DINER – APRIL 11, 1992 – 8:02 A.M.**

**The place smells like scorched coffee, bacon grease, and yesterday’s decisions.**  
 **It’s already too bright.**  
 **The blinds are open too wide.**  
 **The tile floor too reflective.**

**Kathy’s in sunglasses, hoodie up, hunched over a plate of dry toast like it personally betrayed her.**

**Sarah, blazer crisp, hair pulled tight, is on her second cup of black coffee.**  
 **There are folders on the table beside her scrambled eggs—tour logistics, press clippings, *damage control notes from Island legal.***

**She’s been up since 6:00.**  
 **Because she had no choice.**

**And across from them?**

**Gilley.**

**Bright-eyed. Glowing. Shirt unbuttoned. Hair damp from a shower.**  
 ***Grinning like he’s already lived a full day and now wants brunch as a reward.***

---

**GILLEY (cheerfully):**  
 **God, I love *morning.***

**Smell of cheap coffee, sound of sizzling bacon, that *burnt-ass toast* smell—**

**(*gestures grandly*)**  
 **It's *America in her underpants.***

---

**KATHY (flat):**  
 **I will fight you.**

---

**GILLEY (ignores her, to Sarah):**  
 **And *you*—look at you.**  
 **All sharp edges and *business armor.***  
 **Ready to *slay a city* before the rest of the band finds their socks.**

**(*smiles, too clean*)**  
 **Did you sleep well?**

---

****SARAH** (without looking up):**  
 **I slept.**

**(*pause, deadpan*)**  
 **Which is more than *some of us* can say for our mouths this morning.**

---

**GILLEY (grinning):**  
 **Just trying to *lighten the room, sugar.***

---

**KATHY (muttering):**  
 **Lighten your *voice*.**

---

****SARAH** (burned at both ends, clipped):**  
 **Gilley, we’ve got a *radio interview at 10:15*, an *in-store signing* at noon, a *load-in at 2*, and *soundcheck at 3:30.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **So if you’re done *serenading the hash browns*, we need to go over call sheets.**

---

**GILLEY (mock offended):**  
 **Serenading hash browns is *part of my process*.**

**(*then, cooler, more measured*)**  
 **You burn both ends, Sarah.**  
 **Eventually, there’s *nothing left to hold.***

---

****SARAH** (meeting his eyes now):**  
 **Then *don’t let go* of me.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **And *stop making me wait.***

**(*turns back to clipboard*)**  
 **Because *I won’t stop moving.***

---

**Gilley stares at her a second longer.**  
 **Not grinning anymore.**

**Kathy watches them over her sunglasses.**

**No one says anything.**

---

**Waitress arrives with more toast.**

**No one touches it.**

---

**INT. KSYM-FM – SAN ANTONIO – COLLEGE STATION STUDIO – APRIL 11, 1992 – 1:03 P.M.**

**The booth is small, hot, and smells like pizza and plastic.**  
 **Posters of *The Smiths*, *Bauhaus*, and *Sonic Youth* curl at the corners on the walls.**  
 **A fan oscillates in the corner like it’s thinking about quitting.**

**Sarah is tucked into the corner, arms folded, watching from behind the glass.**

**Kathy is in the booth, headphones on, leaned into the mic with calm, predatory grace.**

**The DJ, Luis, is 20, nervously over-prepared, trying not to lose it as *Kathy Espich* sits across from him.**

---

**LUIS (into the mic, stumbling a little):**  
 **We’re here with Kathy from Commuted—thanks for coming to KSYM.**  
 **You, uh, picked a pretty bold track to spin.**

---

**KATHY (smirking, direct):**  
 **If it’s worth playing, it’s worth *feeling*.**

---

****SARAH** (behind glass, thinking):**  
 ***This station isn’t about reach.***  
 ***It’s about roots.***  
 ***We’re not playing to 1992\.***

**(*beat*)**  
 ***We’re playing to 1994\.***  
 ***To when these kids get jobs in labels, studios, publications.***

**(*beat*)**  
 ***Two steps ahead.***

---

**IN THE BOOTH, Luis is sweating.**

**KATHY leans in, voice low and deliberate.**

---

**KATHY (into mic):**  
 **This track’s called *“I’ll Own Your Moment.”***  
 **You might not hear it on daytime radio.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **But *after dark?***  
 **This is the song that makes people *take off their headphones and text their ex.***

---

**She nods. The track cues.**

**The opening guitar chimes.**

**Slow. Hypnotic.**

**The booth goes still.**

---

**Luis blinks as the first verse rolls out.**

**By the time Kathy sings:**

***“Anointing your member in my bed…”***

**Luis chokes on his water.**

---

**\*\*Behind the glass, Sarah just smiles coldly.**  
 **She *knew* it would hit like this.**

---

**By the final chorus, no one is moving.**  
 **Luis looks like he’s aged two years.**

**But he doesn’t stop it.**

**Not even the “shooting from your balls” line.**

**Because he knows:**  
 **This isn’t a gimmick.**

**It’s *art with claws*.**

---

**As the track fades out, Kathy takes off her headphones.**

---

**LUIS (quiet, dazed):**  
 **I think… I think we just broke the transmitter.**

---

**KATHY:**  
 **Or maybe *we fixed it.***

---

**She walks out into the control room, straight past Sarah.**

**KATHY (grinning):**  
 **If they won’t play it?**

**There’s always *KRTU*.**

---

****SARAH** (dead serious):**  
 **They’ll play it now.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **Even if it’s *under the table at midnight.***

---

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – SAN ANTONIO – APRIL 11, 1992 – 4:18 P.M.**

**Sarah is alone again, finally, back at her desk in the corner of her room, blinds drawn just enough to let the gold spill in.**  
 **She’s not tired.**  
 **She’s lit.**

**Clipboard out.**

**Map of the U.S. spread across the bed.**

**Red X’s mark stations that won’t play it.**  
 **Most of them.**  
 **The few unmarked are *pirate joints, overnight hosts with nothing to lose, or interns gone rogue.***

**She turns to a fresh page in her spiral-bound field journal.**

---

****SARAH** (writing, calm but fire-blooded):**

***“I’ll Own Your Moment” will never land on daytime U.S. radio.***  
 ***It’s not edgy—it’s eroticism with intent. Too smart to be pulp, too raw to be buried in metaphor.***  
 ***They don’t know where to file it.***  
 ***So they’ll refuse to shelve it at all.***

**(*pause*)**

***That’s fine.***  
 ***They’ll regret it in two years.***

---

**She flips the map.**

**Europe.**

**Draws a hard circle around London.**  
 **Then Dublin.**  
 **Then Belfast.**

---

****SARAH** (writing faster now):**

***BBC Radio 2*** **— after 10 p.m.**  
 ***NME* — find a young critic who’s jaded enough to love it and reckless enough to say so.**  
 ***U2 infrastructure in Ireland* — leverage old Island contacts.**  
 ***They like big guitars and sexual politics.***  
 ***This is both.***

**(*pause*)**

***Go where they still know that music is supposed to challenge, seduce, and scare the hell out of you.***

---

**She underlines it twice:**

***“Invade Britain.”***

---

**And below that, in smaller handwriting:**

***Let the Americans wonder why they missed it while the UK burns it into their bloodstream.***

---

**She leans back.**

**And just for a second?**

**She *smiles.***

**Because the doors are *closing* in the States.**

**Which means it’s time to *kick them open across the Atlantic.***

---

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – SAN ANTONIO – APRIL 11, 1992 – 4:26 P.M. CDT / 10:26 P.M. GMT – INTERNATIONAL CALL IN PROGRESS**

**Sarah’s sitting cross-legged on the bed, receiver pinched to her shoulder, notes scattered like war maps.**  
 **The *long-distance static* crackles faintly over the line.**

**Finally—**

**CALL CONNECTED.**

---

**TIERNAN (groggy, very Irish):**  
 **Sarah?**

**(*beat*)**  
 **Do you realize what the *bloody hell time* it is here in Dublin?**

---

****SARAH** (perfectly calm):**  
 **Yes.**

**That’s why I knew you’d be home.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **Alone.**  
 **Sober.**  
 **And *grateful to hear from me.***

---

**TIERNAN (grumbling):**  
 **Christ. You still run like a** *Provo* and **flirt like a *knife*.**

**(*yawns*)**  
 **What is it?**

---

****SARAH**:**  
 **I have a song.**

**A *problematic* one.**

**It’s called *“I’ll Own Your Moment.”***

**(*flipping pages*)**  
 **Shoegaze. Erotic. Slow-burn.**  
 **Explicit to the point of *ineligibility* on American radio.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **But in your country?**  
 **It’s *art with heat.***

---

**TIERNAN (clearly intrigued now):**  
 **Oh, so *BBC Two* then, yeah?**

**Or *Midnight Rotation* on *XFM*?**

---

****SARAH**:**  
 **Yes.**

**And I need one critic, young and full of cum. One *gatekeeper* who doesn’t flinch at *lyrics that make people clench their asshole.***

---

**TIERNAN (snorts):**  
 **Christ alive.**

**(*mock horror*)**  
 **This is *another Commuted track*, isn’t it?**

---

****SARAH**:**  
 **You *know* it is.**

---

**TIERNAN (low whistle):**  
 **You’re not looking for buzz.**

**You’re *laying the foundation for a colonic.*** 

---

****SARAH** (coolly):**  
 **Correct.**

**(*pause*)**  
 **You owe me, Tiernan.**  
 **I kept your *name* off the *misconduct report* at the ’89 Island holiday party.**

**(*smiles*)**  
 **Time to *pay up.***

---

**TIERNAN (beat, groaning):**  
 **I’ll make some *calls tomorrow.***  
 **Sleep is for *people who didn’t bet their futures on a band that sings about balls and glory.***

---

****SARAH**:**  
 **Love you for it.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **But if I *don’t* get airplay?**

**I’m sending Kathy.**  
 **With *intent.***

---

**TIERNAN (laughs nervously):**  
 **Message received.**  
 **God save Ireland.**

---

****SARAH** hangs up, clicks the pen twice, and circles one line again:**

***Invade Britain.***

---

**INT. TIERNAN’S FLAT – DUBLIN, IRELAND – APRIL 12, 1992 – 9:08 A.M. GMT**

**Tiernan is slouched in a worn jumper, bare feet on cold tile, mug of tea going cold next to the massive stack of demo tapes, press sheets, and open notebooks covering his kitchen table.**

**He’s got a *faxed lyric sheet from Sarah spread in front of him*, annotated and underlined like *it’s evidence in a criminal case*.**

**The title *“I’ll Own Your Moment”* is circled three times in black ink.**  
 **One phrase is scrawled at the top: *“Too Hot for America.”***

---

**TIERNAN (muttering, eyes scanning):**  
 ***Shooting from your balls… white ropes cascade…***

**(*leans back*)**  
 **Holy *God.***

---

**The phone is cradled under his chin, ringing through to his *BBC Radio contact in London—Nadine.***

**She picks up on the fifth ring.**

---

**NADINE (half-bored):**  
 **Yeah?**

---

**TIERNAN:**  
 **You awake?**

---

**NADINE (sighing):**  
 **Barely. What’s on fire now?**

---

**TIERNAN:**  
 **I’ve got something *American.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **But *actual American.***  
 ***Not* grunge-lite or safe radio paste.**  
 **Not *Nirvana’s baby cousin* singing about static and skate parks.**

**This is *filthy.***

**(*grins*)**  
 **And *gorgeous.***

---

**NADINE (dry):**  
 **I work for the *Corporation*, Tiernan.**  
 **You think I can air *gorgeous filth*?**

---

**TIERNAN (cutting in):**  
 ***Yes.***  
 **If *you’re the one* to put it *front and centre.***

---

**He stands, walks to the window, stares out at a *grey Dublin sky thick with possibility and pent-up weather.***

---

**TIERNAN:**  
 **The BBC can’t smell something this *fresh.***  
 **Their *instincts are rubbish.***

**They’ll bury it under *Rod Stewart reissues* and *whatever Bowie’s not touring.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **Unless *you* put it in the *Midnight Reel.***

---

**NADINE (sighs, curious now):**  
 **Alright, what is it?**

---

**TIERNAN:**  
 **A track called *“I’ll Own Your Moment.”***

**(*beat*)**  
 **It’s *shoegaze meets sex magic.***  
 **Written by a *girl with a guitar, no fear, and zero interest in being polite.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **One listen, Nadine.**  
 **You’ll *never un-hear* it.**

---

**NADINE (pause):**  
 **If this gets me *banned from day rotation* again, I’m *personally posting your address in the breakroom.***

---

**TIERNAN (grinning):**  
 **If they don’t play it, \*\*\*I’m catching a ferry across the Irish Sea with a *spanner* and *kneecapping half the lads in Programming.***

---

**NADINE (laughing now):**  
 **That’s the Tiernan I remember.**

**Send the reel.**

**(*click*)**  
 **Call ends.**

---

**Tiernan leans back, victorious.**  
 **Lights a cigarette.**

**TIERNAN (softly, to himself):**  
 **Alright, Sarah.**  
 **Let’s *turn this island inside out.***

---

**INT. BBC BROADCASTING HOUSE – LONDON – STUDIO 7 – APRIL 13, 1992 – 12:03 A.M. GMT**

**The building hums like a church after hours—quiet halls, red lights above studio doors, low conversation in late-night voices.**  
 **Outside, London is silver and silent, streetlamps flickering through fog and drizzle.**

**Nadine, BBC producer, sits alone in the booth, lights dimmed, a cup of Earl Grey cooling beside the console.**

**Her headphones are on.**

**She presses play.**

---

**Track: *“I’ll Own Your Moment” by Commuted***

---

**The *chiming guitars begin—slow, layered, velvet-soft like breath across bare skin.***

**Kathy’s voice comes in:**

***“I remember the summer, you and me…”***

---

**Nadine sits back slowly, her fingers off the faders.**

**At first, it’s just mood.**  
 **Intimate.**  
 **Dreamlike.**  
 **Like a confession in a candlelit room.**

**Then—**

***“Anointing your member in my bed…”***

**Nadine’s eyes widen.**  
 **She doesn’t stop it.**

**The booth feels smaller.**

**Not claustrophobic.**  
 ***Intimate.***

**Like the *track is pulling the walls closer to listen too.***

---

**By the second pre-chorus, her pen has fallen from her hand.**

**By the bridge, she’s leaning forward, elbows on the console, entranced.**

***“With every hard on, every longing sigh…”***

---

**And then, the *final chorus.***

***“Shooting from your balls, white ropes cascade…”***

---

**Silence.**

**For *five full seconds.***

**Only the soft hiss of the booth.**

---

**NADINE (softly):**  
 **Jesus *Christ.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **It’s *Joyce.***  
 **But *electric.***  
 ***Erotic confession as cathedral.***

**(*beat, eyes wide*)**  
 **Commuted just *communed with James Joyce’s ghost.***

---

**She doesn’t hit “stop.”**  
 **She doesn’t *cut it*.**

**She lets it fade, all the way to the outro:**

***“Together forever, let’s open that door…”***

**And when it ends?**

**She exhales like she’s just walked out of a confessional in stilettos.**

---

**NADINE (grinning to herself):**  
 ***We’re airing it.***

**(*reaches for the programming log*)**  
 **They can *fire me after.***

---

**INT. FLAT – BRISTOL, ENGLAND – APRIL 13, 1992 – 12:43 A.M.**

**The tiny studio flat is dim.**  
 **Curtains drawn.**  
 **A single lamp buzzing quietly next to a pile of open sketchbooks and ashtrays.**

**The radio is on, low, tucked between stacks of records and ramen packets.**

**BBC Radio 2\.**  
 **Late night segment.**  
 **Nadine’s voice just faded.**  
 **The track is over.**

**And *every molecule of air* in the room still feels like it’s vibrating.**

---

**STACEY, 23, art student, bleary-eyed, barefoot, covered in charcoal dust and wearing her ex’s hoodie, is sitting cross-legged on the floor, frozen.**

**She stares blankly at the radio like it just confessed to a murder.**

**She’d only turned it on for background noise.**  
 **Maybe a Sade track.**  
 **Maybe Bowie.**

**But *that*?**

---

***“Shooting from your balls, white ropes cascade…”***

**Still echoing in her skull like the lyrics had been branded onto her *brainstem.***

---

**STACEY (soft, stunned):**  
 **For *fuck’s sake*…**

**(*beat*)**  
 **Wot the *hell* did I just *hear?***

---

**She stands up slowly, walks over to the radio like it might need medical attention.**

**There’s a pause.**  
 **A soft jingle from BBC’s overnight programming.**

**Then Nadine’s voice:**

***“That was ‘I’ll Own Your Moment’ by Commuted—an import you’ll be hearing a lot more of if we have anything to say about it.”***

---

**STACEY (muttering):**  
 **That wasn’t *music.***  
 **That was *intercourse with reverb.***

**(*beat, blinking*)**  
 **And I *liked* it?**

---

**She grabs the nearest pen, writes “COMMUTED” in all caps across the back of a utility bill.**

**Underlines it.**  
 **Twice.**

**Stares at it.**

**Then slowly smiles.**

---

**STACEY (to herself):**  
 **God, this is *filthy.***

**(*beat*)**  
 ***When’s the album out?***

---

**INT. BBC BROADCASTING HOUSE – LONDON – PROGRAMMING OFFICE – APRIL 13, 1992 – 3:17 P.M. GMT**

**A room filled with suits and smug mid-afternoon certainty.**  
 **The kind of space where *art is discussed like accounting and panic always wears a smile.***

**Nadine walks in holding a fax.**

**No clipboard.**  
 **No apologies.**

**She drops the page on the table with the quiet finality of someone about to *upend a room full of men*.**

---

**NADINE:**  
 **You wanted to talk about my *programming choices*?**

**Fantastic.**

**Let’s *start with facts.***

---

**She taps the paper.**

**SALES NUMBERS – *69 Reasons***  
 **491,232 UNITS SOLD (as of yesterday)**

---

**NADINE (flat):**  
 **That is a *cunt’s hair shy of going gold.***

**(*beat*)**  
 ***Zero* commercial radio play in the States.**

---

**EXEC \#1 (blinking):**  
 **Yes, but the *content*, Nadine—**

---

**NADINE (cutting in):**  
 ***Content?***

**(*laughs once, cold*)**  
 **We *aired Madonna’s "Justify My Love"* at full rotation.**

**We *played "Relax"* for *five years.***

**But *a shoegaze ballad with anatomical honesty* makes you clutch your pearls?**

**You can *play Commuted now*—**

**Or wait until *Boxing Day* and look like *nobs who missed the boil*.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **And *the kettle’s name is Kathy.***

**And \*\*\*she’s *whistling.***

---

**EXEC \#2 (quietly):**  
 **It’s a good track…**

---

**NADINE (smirking):**  
 **It’s *more than good*.**  
 **It’s *inevitable.***

**(*leaning in*)**  
 **Now the question is—**  
 **do we *lead*?**

**Or do we *chase the echo*?**

---

**She collects the fax, turns on her heel, and walks out.**

**No response.**

**Just the sound of *a paradigm shifting behind closed doors.***

---

**INT. TIERNAN’S FLAT – DUBLIN – APRIL 13, 1992 – 10:33 A.M. GMT**

**The phone’s still warm from his morning call with Nadine when NME’s features editor rings.**

**Tiernan’s half-dressed, scribbling with one hand and eating cold toast with the other, surrounded by empty teacups, cigarette stubs, and a printout of the *69 Reasons* tracklist annotated like scripture.**

---

**NME EDITOR (crackly, sharp):**  
 **Tiernan, you’re the only Irish bastard we trust to write about this Ohio filth like it matters.**

---

**TIERNAN (deadpan):**  
 **You mean *art.* You meant *art.***

---

**NME EDITOR:**  
 **Call it what you want, but it’s *moving units and moving thighs.***  
 **We need *500 words*, *exclusive angle*, *Commuted in Europe*.**  
 ***600 Irish pounds.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **We go to press at *fourteen hundred.***

**(*sharp inhale*)**  
 **That gives you *three hours and change.***

---

**TIERNAN (grinning):**  
 **I’m *thirty minutes ahead* of you.**

**I *already started writing* this when I heard the *ball line.***

---

**NME EDITOR:**  
 **Then *best be about it, lad.***

---

**CLICK.**

**Tiernan tosses the toast. Grabs a cigarette. Pulls his old typewriter closer with a screech.**

**Types the title, hard:**

**COMMUTED OWNS THE MOMENT, AND YOU JUST MISSED YOURS**  
 ***By Tiernan O’Dowd***

---

**He’s in the zone now, hammering keys like he’s *exorcising the prudish demons from all of British music journalism.***

**He writes:**

***They said America wasn’t ready, but they meant America was afraid.***  
 ***Afraid of women who don’t ask. Afraid of hands that touch back. Afraid of a band that uses guitars like confessions and lyrics like loaded weapons.***

**\*“I’ll Own Your Moment” doesn’t seduce—it *claims.***  
 **It isn’t trying to flirt with radio. It’s *grinding against it until the transmitter begs to be turned off.***

---

***In 500 words or fewer:***  
 ***This band didn’t cross the ocean to ask permission.***  
 ***They came to plant a flag in your imagination, unzip your shame, and play the guitar solo while you cried about it.***

---

**By 12:13 P.M., he’s done.**

**Faxes the copy to London with *ink on his fingers and a devil’s grin.***

---

**INT. NME EDITORIAL OFFICE – LONDON – APRIL 13, 1992 – 12:26 P.M. GMT**

**A storm of *clacking keyboards, crumpled cans of Irn-Bru, and punk vinyl on the office turntable* fills the air.**  
 **It smells like *ink, hangovers, and hard-earned deadlines*.**

**The *newest fax from Tiernan* arrives on the *old thermal paper roll machine* with a high-pitched whine like a prophecy being spat into reality.**

**Tom, a deputy features editor in a *threadbare Buzzcocks shirt*, tears it off the roll, scans the headline—**

**“COMMUTED OWNS THE MOMENT, AND YOU JUST MISSED YOURS”**

**—and starts *cackling.***

---

**TOM (to the room):**  
 ***He fookin’ did it\!***

---

**ZARA (layout designer, rolling a cig):**  
 **Did what?**

---

**TOM (waving the fax):**  
 ***Dropped the single greatest opening line I’ve read since we let that gobshite write about Primal Scream on ketamine.***

---

**OWEN (senior editor, glancing up):**  
 **It’s *Tiernan,* innit?**

**(*grins*)**  
 **Of *course it is.***

---

**TOM:**  
 **He’s *thirty minutes ahead of the rest of the bloody industry* and *six hours ahead in filth.***

---

**OWEN (snatching the sheet):**  
 **Let’s see—**

**(*reads aloud*)**  
 ***"They said America wasn’t ready, but they meant America was afraid…"***

**(*chokes on his coffee*)**  
 ***Christ on a fuckin’ Vespa.***

**(*yelling to the back of the room*)**  
 **PHIL\!**  
 **GET THIS ON PAGE FOUR\!**

---

**PHIL (from layout):**  
 **Already mocked it up, mate\! It’s *beautiful*. I put the Commuted promo photo over a *Union Jack* like it’s a war poster\!**

---

**TOM (still reading, eyes wide):**  
 **Listen to this:**  
 ***"They didn’t cross the ocean to ask permission. They came to plant a flag in your imagination, unzip your shame, and play the guitar solo while you cried about it."***

---

**ZARA (genuinely impressed):**  
 **That’s *not writing.***  
 **That’s *holy fuck poetry.***

---

**OWEN (grinning):**  
 **Can we *afford* him?**

---

**TOM:**  
 **We’re *paying him in Irish pounds.***  
 **It's basically *glorified Monopoly money.***

---

**Suddenly, GAVIN (music editor, Irish-born) walks in with his arms crossed.**

**He hears the laughter, sees the fax, and deadpans:**

---

**GAVIN:**  
 ***Sod off, lads.***

**Ireland is a *fookin’ republic.***

**(*grabs the fax from Owen*)**  
 ***You want war copy like this? Go back across the Sea and learn to write with teeth, you soft-palmed English tossers.***

---

**EVERYONE:**  
 **Ooooooooooooh\!**

**(*laughter erupts*)**

---

**OWEN (laughing):**  
 **Alright, alright—give the man his Guinness and *get it to print.***

---

**TOM (to Zara):**  
 **You put this on the shelf next to anything about the Stones, and *Commuted’s gonna blow the wrinkles off Mick Jagger.***

---

**ZARA:**  
 **They already *own the moment.***

---

**Presses roll.**  
 **Layout finalizes.**  
 **And across the office, someone shouts—**

***"Oi\! Add ‘white ropes cascade’ to the pull quote\!"***

---

**INT. GOGARTY’S PUB – TEMPLE BAR, DUBLIN – APRIL 13, 1992 – 7:18 P.M. GMT**

**The wood floors creak.**  
 **The ceiling's low.**  
 **And the smell of *Guinness, pride, and permanent ink* hangs in the air.**

**Tiernan O’Dowd pushes open the pub door, NME folded under his arm, worn satchel slung over his shoulder like he just *toppled an empire and popped out for a pint.***

**The Monday crowd’s light—locals, students, a few tourists trying to blend in.**

**But as soon as *Seamus* behind the bar catches sight of him?**

**He shouts.**

---

**SEAMUS (grinning):**  
 ***Well, if it isn’t Ireland’s dirtiest export\!***

**(*louder*)**  
 **Oi\! \*\*\*Make room, ya wankers—\*\*\*the *man* just turned *masturbation metaphors into poetry\!***

---

**APPLAUSE breaks out.**  
 **Genuine.**  
 **Loud.**  
 **A little rowdy.**

**A regular at the corner table actually *raises his glass*.**

---

**TIERAN (grinning, mock-modest):**  
 **Christ. All I did was *report the truth.***

**(*slides onto a stool*)**  
 **The *orgasmic, guitar-drenched, scandalous truth.***

---

**SEAMUS (pouring a Guinness):**  
 **You didn’t write an article, Tiernan—**

**You *set fire to the BBC and called it weather.***

**(*slides pint across*)**  
 **On the house. *And the next one.***

---

**TIERAN (raising his pint):**  
 **To *Commuted.***  
 **And to *Kathy Espich,* who may or may not *summon spirits through amplifiers.***

---

**REGULAR \#1 (winking):**  
 **And to *white ropes cascading\!***

---

**The whole pub *erupts with laughter.***

**Tiernan takes a long sip.**  
 **Sets the pint down.**  
 **And pulls the NME copy from his satchel, folding it open to page four.**

**He taps his byline.**  
 **Then grins wider.**

---

**TIERAN (to Seamus, smug):**  
 **Cheque’s in the post.**  
 ***600 quid.***

---

**SEAMUS (nodding approvingly):**  
 **Not bad for something that’ll probably *get you banned in five countries.***

---

**TIERAN:**  
 **Make it *six.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **I’ve got *a call from Rolling Stone* to return in the morning.**

---

**The jukebox kicks in—*The Jesus and Mary Chain*.**  
 **Glasses clink.**  
 **Laughter rolls.**

**And Tiernan?**

**He leans back, beer in hand, *king of the filth-stained literary frontier.***

**Tonight?**

**He *owns his moment.***

---

**INT. SAN ANTONIO HOTEL – GILLEY’S ROOM – APRIL 14, 1992 – 11:41 P.M. CDT**

**The AC rattles.**  
 **The mini-fridge hums louder than it should.**  
 **The room smells like stale takeout, cigarette ash, and missed connections.**

**Gilley lies on the bed, one boot still on, a crumpled copy of the NME spread resting on his chest.**  
 **The headline:**

**COMMUTED OWNS THE MOMENT, AND YOU JUST MISSED YOURS**  
 ***By Tiernan O'Dowd***

**He’s read it *three times already.***  
 **But the line that keeps sticking, the one that *won’t let him go*—**

***“…They didn’t cross the ocean to ask permission. They came to plant a flag in your imagination, unzip your shame, and play the guitar solo while you cried about it.”***

---

**GILLEY (quietly, to himself):**  
 **It’s *not just about her.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **It’s *me.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **I’m *in this.***

---

**His fingers trace a paragraph where Tiernan waxes about *"unexpected voices rising mid-album, men who smirked their way into legitimacy with lyrics sharpened in silence."***

**Gilley shuts his eyes.**  
 **Feels the weight of it now.**

**The *truth*.**

**He wrote something *real*.**  
 **And it *hit.***  
 **And *still*—he’s *alone* in his hotel room, lying under *words that mattered* and *a silence that doesn’t.***

---

**GILLEY (gritting his teeth):**  
 **She’s not coming.**

---

**He sits up, throws the NME onto the floor.**  
 **Runs a hand through his hair.**

**His phone buzzes—**  
 **Kathy texting a band meme.**  
 **Jeff asking about load-in tomorrow.**

***Not Sarah.***

**Still not Sarah.**

---

**He pulls on the other boot, grabs his denim jacket, and checks the mirror.**

**That *classic smirk* returns, barely.**

---

**GILLEY (to his reflection):**  
 **Fuck it.**

**Next *brunette that smiles* at me tonight?**

**She’s *coming back here.***

---

**Not because he’s lonely.**  
 **Not because he needs a distraction.**  
 **But because *someone* should want to be near the man *who just got name-dropped in the NME* for *blowing the lid off modern sex rock.***

**And *if Sarah doesn’t?***

**Then *someone will.***

---

**He flicks off the lamp, grabs his key, and walks out into the *Texas heat*.**

**Because if he can’t *own the moment with her*—**

**He’ll *own it with someone.***

---

**INT. SAN ANTONIO HOTEL – LOBBY BAR – APRIL 14, 1992 – 11:58 P.M. CDT**

It’s dim, lit like a *whiskey bottle left open too long.*  
 A low hum of conversation.  
 A dying jukebox in the corner plays *Mazzy Star* like it’s apologizing for the world.

Sarah sits at the bar, blazer off, sleeves rolled, stirring her drink more than sipping it.  
 The NME is folded beside her, open to Tiernan’s piece.

She hasn’t looked at it in 20 minutes.  
 But it’s there.  
 Like a *challenge.*  
 Like *a receipt.*

Then—

Kathy slides onto the stool next to her, her own drink already half gone, smirk in place, fire burning low behind the eyes.

---

KATHY (quietly):  
 If you don’t *fuck him soon*, I *will.*

(*pause*)  
 *For morale.*

---

Sarah chokes slightly on her sip.  
 Doesn’t laugh.  
 Doesn’t flinch.

Just turns and meets Kathy’s eyes.

Dead calm.

---

**SARAH** (even):  
 Really?

---

KATHY (shrugs, nonchalant):  
 Nah.

(*beat*)  
 Not *really*.

(*beat*)  
 We had a thing. *Back then.*

It was… *fine*.

(*beat*)  
 No orchestras.  
 No fireworks.

(*sips*)  
 But I learned a *lot.*

(*smirks*)  
 Like how to *stop faking things for boys who think they’re the event.*

---

Sarah (quietly):  
 You ever tell him?

---

KATHY (shaking her head):  
 Nah.  
 Would’ve just *shattered his little cowboy myth.*

(*leans in*)  
 But *you?*

You’d *wreck him proper.*  
 You wouldn’t *worship the swagger*.  
 You’d *match it.*

(*beat*)  
 That *scares him.*  
 Which is why *he’s out right now looking for less.*

---

**SARAH** (looks away):  
 You think I *want* him?

---

KATHY (matter-of-fact):  
 I think if you didn’t *want* him, you’d have *told him* that song was *about you.*

(*smirks*)  
 Instead of *pretending you didn’t read every goddamn word three times.*

---

Sarah’s silent.  
 Her fingers tighten around the glass.  
 Then loosen.

---

**SARAH**:  
 I don’t have time for chaos.  
 I’m *managing a revolution.*

---

KATHY (laughing softly):  
 Sweetheart…

You’re *starring in it.*

---

The jukebox shifts.  
 The bartender wipes a glass without caring who’s watching.

Sarah sips.  
 Kathy leans back.

No more need for truths tonight.

Just *possibility.*

---

**INT. SAN ANTONIO DIVE BAR – APRIL 14, 1992 – 11:59 P.M. CDT**

The bar glows in that *familiar amber haze*—all neon Budweiser signs and duct-taped barstools.  
 The jukebox is somehow *grinding out its third playthrough of “Sweet Memories in a Dive Bar,”* like someone’s pressing repeat just to make sure the walls memorize it.

Gilley leans at the bar, boots up on the rail, *half-empty beer in one hand, cracked pool cue in the other.*

He’s not *thinking* about the song.  
 Not really.

But it’s inside him anyway.  
 Because that voice, those words, that *thrust* of chaos and sex and power—

That’s *Kathy’s voice.*

But *tonight?*

It’s coming from Anna, seated two stools down.  
 Brunette.  
 Red lipstick.  
 A look in her eye like *she’s already picked her poison—and he’s pouring it.*

---

ANNA (grinning, tipsy but in control):  
 You ever *been* to New Orleans?

---

GILLEY (grinning back):  
 Been *run out of it.*

---

ANNA:  
 This track’s *filthy.*

(*laughs*)  
 I love it.

It’s *me and my girls, five years ago.*

(*leans closer*)  
 *Maybe me tonight,* if you’re lucky.

---

Gilley laughs, raises his beer.

But his eyes flick—again—to the door.

Just a second.

Just a *check*.

Just in case *Sarah*…

No. Still nothing.

---

ANNA (noticing):  
 Waiting for someone?

---

GILLEY (masking it with charm):  
 Not if you’re here.

---

She smiles.  
 He drinks.  
 The jukebox croons:

*“To wild dreams and daring flights…”*

---

He leans in.

But something’s still *off*.

Because *every time that horn sample hits?*  
 Every time Kathy’s voice slices through the haze?

He remembers who’s *not* in this bar.

And *what it would mean if she was.*

---

**EXT. SAN ANTONIO DIVE BAR – PARKING LOT – APRIL 15, 1992 – 12:04 A.M. CDT**

The night air is humid, thick with cigarette smoke and tequila sweat leaking out the bar door.  
 Neon reflections shimmer across cracked asphalt like fractured promises.

Sarah stands across the street, heart punching in her chest, wearing *that yellow floral print dress*—the one that *doesn’t hide anything.*

No bra.  
 No panties.  
 Nothing between her and the night but the thrum of her own *fury and fear*.

---

She sees him.

Gilley.  
 At the bar.  
 Grinning.  
 Anna leaning in close.  
 Laughing.  
 Lipstick too red.

And he doesn’t look sad.

He looks *available.*

---

**SARAH** (furious whisper):  
 *Goddammit, Sarah.*

---

She balls her fists.

Because this?

This was supposed to be *her night.*

Her *four-hour window.*

Her *moment*.

And now he’s in there, letting someone else fill the *slot* she *booked but never showed for.*

---

And worse?

She *knows* how this story plays out if she doesn’t move:

He goes home with *someone*.

Writes *another* song.

Gets *stronger* for it.

And *she*?

She stays *stuck in strategy*, *scheduling regret* like it’s a boardroom appointment.

---

**SARAH** (growling through clenched teeth):  
 Put your *ass* in the *firing line*…

(*beat*)  
 And *commit.*

For the *big win*.

---

She steps off the curb, fast.

Crosses the street like it’s a *battleground.*

The door’s open.  
 The jukebox is fading into the outro:

*“With sweet memories left in the dark…”*

---

She pushes through.

The heat hits her.  
 The smell.  
 The *weight* of the bar.

And then—  
 *Gilley turns.*

Eyes meet.

The *entire room drops out.*

---

His eyes scan the dress.

The flushed cheeks.

The hair half-undone.

And in one flicker of hesitation, *Sarah tells him everything:*

*“I’m late, but I’m here.*  
 *I want this.*  
 *I’m ready.*  
 *Let’s go.”*

---

Gilley blinks.  
 Anna notices.  
 Steps back, confused.  
 She sees the shift.  
 She knows she’s been replaced.

She shrugs.  
 Flicks her cigarette.

Walks away.

---

Sarah walks up.  
 No words.

Just guts.  
 Eyes.  
 Nerves on fire.

---

GILLEY (quiet, stunned):  
 Sarah…

---

**SARAH** (whispers):  
 I *own this moment.*

(*beat*)  
 Let’s *go.*

---

He downs the rest of his beer without breaking eye contact.

Drops the tip on the bar.

And follows her *out the door like gravity just remembered what it was for.*

---

**INT. SAN ANTONIO HOTEL – **SARAH**’S ROOM –  APRIL 15, 1992 – 12:38 A.M. CDT**

The door clicks shut behind them like a countdown starting.

Sarah doesn’t wait.

She grabs his shirt and drags — not leads, drags — Gilley into the room like she’s storming a stage. Their mouths meet before logic can catch up. Tongues clash, teeth scrape, fingers already undoing buttons like it’s a demolition job.

Clothes go flying — jacket to the lamp, boots to the wall, his shirt ripped, her dress yanked over her head like she’s molting a former life.

The bed hits the wall with a crack like a starter pistol.

And they start fucking.

Fast. Hard. Loud. The mattress squeals. The frame moans. The rhythm builds into something primal — a tempo born from too many rehearsals and not enough release.

Sarah’s laugh cuts through the air — wild, hungry.

Gilley growls back, lifting, shifting, pinning — as if he’s afraid she’ll vanish if he doesn’t leave marks.

Then

SLAM.

CREAKCREAKCREAKCREAKCREAK.

THUD.

Laughter.

**Gasps.**

Skin hitting skin with unapologetic rhythm.

Down the hall, guests check their watches.

Next door, Kathy blinks awake.

**INT. KATHY’S ROOM – SAME TIME**

Kathy’s lights are off.  
 She’s in bed, one leg out from under the blanket, trying to find the cool spot on the pillow.

She’s been reading *Anaïs Nin* by lamplight.

And she’s just flipped the page when—

*SLAM.*

The door next to hers.  
Sarah’s room.  
Or more specifically now—Sarah and Gilley’s room.  
Now.

Kathy blinks.  
Waits.

One beat.  
Two.

Then—

*Creak.*  
*Creak-creak.*  
*Creak-creak-creak-creak-creak.*

The unmistakable rhythm of a shitty hotel mattress doing its damndest to survive the night.

---

KATHY (deadpan):  
Well then.

---

She rolls onto her back, book open across her chest, staring at the ceiling like it’s a confessional booth.

*creakcreakcreakcreakcreakcreakCREAK*

She winces.

---

KATHY (muttering):  
Jesus Christ, Gilley.  
 *Pace yourself.*

Kathy stares at the ceiling, frozen.

It’s not just creaking anymore.

It’s a performance. Unchained. Percussive. Damn-near orchestral.

She hears Sarah scream — not in pain, not in fear — but like something inside her just snapped free and sprinted into the wild.

*CREAK-CREAK.*  
 *creak… creak…*  
 *CREAK.*

Then a muffled laugh. A gasp.  
 Then?

*Bang.*  
 (Headboard or knees, she’s not sure.)

KATHY (soft):

Holy shit.

Another thud. Another gasp. A headboard cracking like thunder.

She laughs — hands behind her head, face lit by the war drums next door.

KATHY (shaking her head):

If there’s anything left of that bed in the morning, I’ll buy it dinner first.

Back in Sarah’s room?

One last yell.

One last slam.

Then — silence.

Not quiet.

Charged silence.

Like the air after a concert, still vibrating with everything that just happened.

Then?

KATHY (shaking her head):  
 Girl waits *weeks* for the moment and then *goes zero to demolition in sixty seconds.*

(*beat*)  
 *Respect.*

---

She grabs a pen from the nightstand.

Pulls a napkin from under her tea mug.

Writes:

*About. Fucking. Time.*  
*Literally.*

Folds it.  
 Tucks it under Sarah’s door when things finally go quiet.

---

KATHY (smirking as she slips back into bed):  
 Welcome to the *real band.*

---

**INT. SAN ANTONIO HOTEL – **SARAH**’S ROOM – APRIL 15, 1992 – 1:04 A.M. CDT**

The room is a wreck of sheets, sweat, breath, and history.

The yellow dress is somewhere—*maybe* on the lamp.  
 Maybe *under the dresser.*

It doesn’t matter.

Because Sarah’s where she was supposed to be.

Exactly where she’s been *denying herself for three goddamned nights.*

Naked.  
Alive.  
Fucking.

Flat on her back, legs locked around him, lips parted not for talking but for the kind of breathing that can’t wait.

Gilley’s above her, inside her cunt, hands buried in her hair like he’s scared it’ll all vanish if he lets go.

Her *head’s swimming.*

His *hips are unforgiving.*

And the *only thing she hears louder than the squeaking mattress* is the *sound of herself moaning like she just unzipped her own restraints.*

---

GILLEY (hoarse, low):  
*Why* did you *hesitate?*

---

Sarah doesn’t answer right away.

She *gasps.*  
 He doesn’t stop.  
 Won’t stop.  
 Not until she answers.\*\*

He slows just enough to bring her face to his, foreheads pressed.

---

GILLEY (again, quieter now, almost a whisper):  
 Why, Sarah?

*Why’d you wait?*

You’re *right here.*  
 Where you *should’ve been* for *three fucking nights.*

---

Her nails rake down his back.

Not out of rage.  
 But release.

She *hated* waiting too.

---

**SARAH** (panting, finally):  
 Because if I *had* this then—  
 I wouldn’t have *controlled anything.*

---

GILLEY (breathless laugh):  
 You still *don’t.*

---

And then he *kisses her*—  
 rough and deep,  
 as if trying to undo every night she spent *managing instead of wanting.*

---

They collapse into it again.  
Hot.  
Hard.  
No lies left.  
No clipboard in sight.

Just *sweat and skin and jism*.

And *every moment she didn’t take…*  
*finally being taken.*

---

**INT. SAN ANTONIO HOTEL – **SARAH**’S ROOM – APRIL 15, 1992 – 1:51 A.M. CDT**

The room has finally gone quiet.

Just the slow rise and fall of breathing, the occasional creak of the settling bed, and the distant hum of the hallway ice machine down the corridor.

Sarah lies on her side, pressed against Gilley’s chest, her leg draped over his thigh, her fingers tracing soft lines across his ribs.  
It’s intimate.  
Deliberate.

She’s not smiling.

Not glowing.

She’s *processing.*

But her body is warm in the way only real aftermath delivers.

His arm’s around her back.

One hand tangled in her hair, like he doesn’t quite believe she’s there.

He finally exhales a long breath and murmurs:

---

GILLEY (soft):  
That was…

(*beat*)  
Really good.

---

**SARAH** (even quieter):  
Yeah.

---

She lifts her head, just enough to look him in the eye.

There’s no armor in her voice.  
But there’s *steel beneath it.*

---

**SARAH**:  
We’re not telling anyone.

---

GILLEY (a pause):  
I figured.

---

**SARAH** (serious):  
Not Kathy.  
Not Jeff.  
Not the label.  
*No one.*

---

GILLEY (nods once):  
Okay.

---

She lays her head back on his chest.

Fingers still tracing.

---

GILLEY (after a pause):  
You gonna regret this?

---

**SARAH** (no hesitation):  
No.

(*beat*)  
But I’ll *hate myself* if it *costs me control.*

---

GILLEY:  
Then we *don’t lose control.*

---

He doesn’t say more.

Doesn’t make promises.

Just tightens his arm around her, and they fall back into the stillness—

Not lovers.  
Not enemies.

But *co-conspirators*.

In *something private.*  
*Something powerful.*  
*And absolutely theirs.*

---

**INT. SAN ANTONIO HOTEL – KATHY’S ROOM – APRIL 15, 1992 – 2:37 A.M. CDT**

The lamp's on low.  
The bedsheets are kicked halfway off.  
The ceiling fan turns, lazy and useless.

And Kathy?

Kathy’s *wide awake.*

Because through the wall?

It’s *round two.*

---

*“FUCK me hard—uhhh\! UH\!—God, yes\!”*

*CreakcreakcreakCREAK—* *thump.*

---

She stares at the ceiling like it owes her money.

---

KATHY (dry):  
Jesus *Christ, Sarah.*

---

Ten minutes of rhythmic chaos later, she throws off the sheet, grabs a pencil, and yanks her notepad from the nightstand like a general reaching for a battle map.

She *writes furiously.*  
 Words flowing faster than she can filter them.

But this time?

It’s not revenge.  
 It’s not smirk.  
 It’s *ambition*.  
 It’s *awakening.*

---

Because if Sarah can wail that loud, that *uninhibited*?

Then *why the hell not her?*

---

She taps the pencil against the page, thinking.

*Maybe acoustic trance…*  
 *Just a touch of funk in the bass?*  
 *Something breezy but charged…*

She hums a melody that climbs and *hangs on the edge of something impossible*—

High.  
 Strong.  
 *Free.*

Can she *hit that note?*

She *hears Sarah again.*

*“YES\! YES—oh my GOD—”*

---

KATHY (quiet, determined):  
 If *that babe* can *do* it…

*So can I.*

---

She circles a line she’s written three times already:

*I’m ready for sex, to kindle my dreams.*

Then underlines it once.  
 Hard.

*This isn’t jealousy.*

It’s *fuel.*

---

**INT. 97X (THE FUTURE OF ROCK AND ROLL) – OXFORD, OHIO – APRIL 16, 1992 – 10:56 A.M. EDT**

The station smells like bad coffee, vinyl sleeves, and twenty years of passionate defiance.  
 Posters of *Pixies*, *R.E.M.*, and *Patti Smith* line the soundproof walls.  
 There's a *buzz in the building*—not just the signal.

The *PD (program director), Lynn*, is pacing with a clipboard and a barely-hinged smile.

She got the call yesterday:  
 Commuted. In her booth.  
 Live. Acoustic.  
 Kathy and Gilley.

She said *yes* so fast she dropped her office chair.

---

LYNN (to the engineer, trembling):  
 They’re gonna play something *original.*

(*beat*)  
 I didn’t even *ask.*

---

In the booth:  
 Gilley’s got his guitar—no strap, boots scuffed.  
 Kathy holds a single lyric sheet, folded into thirds, *fresh. Raw. Possibly written in a hotel bed hours ago.*

They’ve barely spoken to each other.

But something’s coiled tight between them.

Not tension.

*Readiness.*

---

LYNN (on mic):  
 Listeners, *brace yourselves.*  
 We’ve got *Commuted.*  
 Live.  
 Stripped down.  
 Just Kathy. Just Gilley.

(*grinning*)  
 And they’ve promised *something original.*

---

Sarah is still in the parking lot.  
 She thinks they’re doing *Sweet Memories in a Dive Bar*.

She’s *totally wrong.*

---

GILLEY (to Kathy, under his breath):  
 You sure?

---

KATHY (quiet fire):  
 Start with A minor.  
 Follow me.

---

GILLEY nods.

Plays the first chord.

It’s *not Sweet Memories.*

It’s *this new thing.*  
 *Her* thing.

From *last night.*

---

Kathy breathes once.  
 Then sings.

*“I checked into the hotel, a perfect escape…”*

---

LYNN (off mic, mouthing):  
 *Oh. My. God.*

---

And by the time Kathy hits the first chorus—

*“‘Baby\!’ she cried, her desire laid bare…”*

the engineer’s mouth is open,  
 the intern at the soundboard has stopped blinking,  
 and Lynn’s ovaries have straight-up quit the building.

---

It’s raw.  
Funny.  
Candid.  
Sexy as hell.

But most of all?

It’s *brilliant.*

---

Outside, Sarah walks in with her clipboard.  
Stops cold.  
Hears Kathy’s voice.  
Hears the lyrics.

*“‘Fuck me hard, oh UHH UHH,’ her passion rang out…”*

Her eyes go wide.

---

**SARAH** (whispers):  
…You *have* to be fucking kidding me.

---

She steps into the booth just as the bridge hits:

*“So I reflected, on slumber I’ve lost…”*

Kathy sees her.

*Doesn’t flinch.*

Just *locks eyes* and *sings louder.*

---

**INT. 97X STUDIO – ON AIR – APRIL 16, 1992 – 11:08 A.M. EDT**

The last chords hang in the air like *perfume and danger.*

Gilley strums a final shimmering harmonic and leans into the mic, all sweat and mischief.

---

GILLEY (deadpan, charming):  
 Inspired by *walls that ain’t quite thick enough.*

---

The room ERUPTS.

Lynn’s laughing so hard she nearly knocks over her coffee.  
 The intern slaps the desk.  
 The engineer wheezes.

Phones? *Lighting up.*

---

LYNN (wiping tears):  
*Thank GOD* for *base morals* and \*\*\*paper-thin hotel walls—\*\*\*again.

(*grinning wide*)  
I haven’t felt this *naughty* playing daytime radio since we spun Liz Phair’s *Flower* at 11:59 a.m.

---

KATHY (cool as a glacier, hot as a fuse):  
Leonard Cohen was the *point of departure.*

(*beat*)  
But the *inspiration*?

(*looks directly at Sarah, who is still frozen just inside the doorway*)  
Was *friends.*

---

Sarah blinks once.  
Twice.

Clipboard loose in her hand.

Mouth parted in silent disbelief.

The *plan*?  
The *schedule*?

*Shredded by a chorus and a confession.*

---

LYNN (pointing at Kathy):  
 This is *going* into *rotation*.

Midnight, drive time, fuck it—we’re playing this *on Valentine’s Day* until the transmitter melts.

(*to Kathy*)  
 You want to come back and do *Volume Two*?

---

KATHY (grinning):  
 Give me *another thin wall and a bad decision.*

---

**INT. 97X STUDIO – REQUEST LINE – APRIL 16, 1992 – 11:14 A.M. EDT**

The red *request line light blinks* like it’s on fire.

Lynn waves it through—*line one*.

Engineer taps the button.

---

LYNN (on air):  
 97X—The Future of Rock and Roll.  
 You're live, go ahead.

---

JOSIAH (caller, 21, University of Cincinnati, dazed voice):  
 Uh… yeah, hey.

(*nervous laugh*)  
 This is *Josiah* from UC.  
 I was just… I mean—

(*beat*)  
 Who *was that?*

---

LYNN (grinning):  
 That was *Kathy Espich* of *Commuted.*  
 And the song was *brand-fucking-new.*

---

JOSIAH (still catching his breath):  
 Okay, because, like…

(*beat*)  
 I don’t know *who* she is, but I want her to *narrate my next hookup.*

(*pause*)  
 Or *read me poetry.*  
 Or *start a cult.*  
 Or *whatever.*

---

LYNN (laughing):  
 Careful, Josiah.  
 Those *thin hotel walls* might be contagious.

---

JOSIAH:  
 Let ‘em be.

(*beat*)  
 That song made me *rethink my entire approach to foreplay.*

---

LYNN:  
 And *that* is why *we play the real shit.*

Stay tuned, Josiah.  
 *She’s not done yet.*

---

Engineer fades the call.  
 Lynn mouths *"Holy shit"* to the room.  
 Phones keep blinking.

Kathy?

Still calm.  
 Still glowing.

Sarah?

Still watching.

Commuted?

*Now officially banned in four states and climbing.*

---

**INT. UNIVERSITY OF CINCINNATI – DORM ROOM – SCHNEIDER HALL – APRIL 16, 1992 – 11:42 A.M. EDT**

Josiah, barefoot, hair wild, still holding a piece of toast he forgot to bite, paces back and forth like *a man possessed by poetry and lust*.

The *portable radio’s still on the windowsill*, 97X crackling faintly.

The *last notes of Kathy’s live track* hang in the air like perfume after a bomb went off.

His *roommate, Trey*—button-down shirt, pocket protector, textbook open to “Statics and Materials”—watches in disbelief.

---

JOSIAH (raving):  
 I’m *serious.*  
 She was *channeling erotic transcendence* and *reckoning with sleep deprivation and modern loneliness* through *acoustic trance.*

(*waving the toast*)  
 That was *feminist spirituality with chorus hooks.*

---

TREY (not looking up):  
 Dude.

You’re an *engineering major.*

---

JOSIAH (turning on him):  
 And *Newton wrote love letters* in the margins of his mechanics notes, so don't *box me in, Trey.*

---

TREY (still unfazed):  
 You tutor Calculus II.

---

JOSIAH (pointing at the radio):  
 I’m *rethinking Calculus* now.  
 That song had *rhythm.*  
 That *bridge modulation?*  
 It was *structured like a cantilever under tension.*

(*beat*)  
 *Sexy tension.*

---

TREY (putting his pencil down):  
 Are you… *hard* right now?

---

JOSIAH (without shame):  
 Emotionally.

---

He grabs a legal pad from the floor and writes:

*Kathy Espich Thesis Title:*  
 *“Moaning Through the Wall: Acoustic Eroticism and the Echo Chamber of the Feminine Self.”*

---

TREY:  
 What class is that even for?

---

JOSIAH:  
 Life.

---

**EXT. 97X STATION PARKING LOT – OXFORD, OHIO – APRIL 16, 1992 – 11:26 A.M. EDT**

The air smells like spring and radio static.  
 The trees are blooming.  
 The sun is just *mocking Sarah at this point.*

She strides out the front door of the station, her heels clicking like gunfire on pavement.  
 Clipboard under her arm, jaw clenched, hair pulled back just tight enough to *hide the chaos.*

Kathy’s already outside, leaning against the band van like *she owns the sky*, sipping from a Styrofoam cup like *she didn’t just detonate Commuted’s brand image live on FM radio.*

---

**SARAH** (low and furious):  
 That was *sabotage*.

---

KATHY (calm, amused):  
 No, Sarah.

(*turns to her, slow and smug*)  
 That was a strategic *surprise.*

---

**SARAH** (sharp):  
You were supposed to play *Sweet Memories in a Dive Bar.*  
You know, *the song I cleared with the promo packet, the acoustic plan, the FCC safe list—*

---

KATHY (interrupting, sipping):  
Yeah, but I *wrote this one at 2:37 a.m.* while your *orgasm cracked the drywall* like thunder in a condemned church.

(*beat*)  
It felt… *relevant.*

---

**SARAH** (fuming):  
You ambushed *me.*  
You ambushed the *label.*  
You ambushed *Gilley.*

---

KATHY (shrugs):  
He *loved it.*  
I gave him *two chords and a signal*. He *followed*.

---

**SARAH** (quiet now, deadly):  
You put me *on display* in front of *a live audience*.

---

KATHY (gently):  
You put *yourself* on display.  
I just *hit record.*

(*beat*)  
And let’s not pretend *97X* didn’t *eat it alive.*

---

**SARAH** (staring hard):  
This was *personal.*

---

KATHY (holding the stare, then softens):  
No, Sarah.

This was *proof.*

(*beat*)  
You’re *not just the clipboard.*  
You’re *the moment*.

(*smiles, soft and criminal*)  
I just wrote it down first.

---

Sarah doesn’t answer.  
Can’t.

Because *she’s not wrong.*

And worse?

Sarah *felt it too.*

The room.  
The wetness.  
The way the song *hit*.

She hadn’t heard Kathy sound *that alive* in months.

---

KATHY (heading for the van):  
Get in, General.  
We’ve got *more stations to conquer.*

(*grins*)  
And *walls to test.*

---

Sarah exhales.  
Once.  
Hard.

Then follows.

Because *strategy’s great*.

But *momentum*?

That’s *everything.*

---

**INT. 103.9 THE EDGE – DAYTON, OHIO – STUDIO A – APRIL 17, 1992 – 2:03 P.M. EDT**

The walls are lined with cracked eggcrate foam and *graffiti'd posters from every edge band that’s ever mattered in Dayton*.

This is Commuted's hometown battlefield.

Every damn one of them grew up with this station blaring from car stereos, boomboxes, and basement speakers.
