This isn’t just another live radio set.  
This is *coming home.*

---

Sarah is ten feet from the booth, hands on her hips, holding her clipboard like a holy text.  
She *knows what’s coming this time.*

She *didn’t authorize it*.

But *she’s not stopping it, either.*

---

Kathy stands between Jeff and Jeremy, eyes burning bright, *hushed and razor-sharp with intent.*

She *taps the lyric sheet* she just wrote at 2:37 A.M., now creased and fingerprinted from rehearsals in hotel rooms.

---

KATHY (to Jeff, whispering):  
Give me *Bootsy.*

(*taps his chest*)  
But *quiet Bootsy.*  
*Bedroom Bootsy.*

---

JEFF (grinning):  
That’s *a dangerous request.*

---

KATHY (smirking):  
I *know*.

---

KATHY (turning to Jeremy):  
Jer—this one’s *not a solo.*  
 It’s *foreplay.*

(*leans in, softer*)  
Dance with me.  
Like you’re *watching from the next room.*  
If you breathe too loud, *you ruin it.*

---

JEREMY (half-laughing):  
Got it.  
*Voyeur settings: activated.*

---

She turns to Bill, already waiting by the mixer with his arsenal of synths muted, headset on, calm as a monk.

---

KATHY (dead serious):  
Bill?  
No pads.  
No fills.

Just…

(*she lifts her hand and SNAPS—crisp, sharp, right into the air*)

KATHY:  
*That.*

Right *into the mic.*

(*beat*)  
Every eight bars.

---

BILL (nods):  
Minimalist *funk priest.*

I live for this.

---

Inside the booth, DJ Marnie, dyed hair, Doc Martens, and eyeliner like warpaint, leans into the mic:

---

MARNIE (on air):  
We’ve got *Commuted* in the building.  
And folks—this isn’t a replay.  
 This isn’t a remix.

This is *a homecoming.*

(*beat*)  
Brand-new track.  
Wrote it at *2:37 A.M.*

So it’s called…

(*glancing back through the glass at Kathy, who smirks and nods*)

“2:37 A.M.”

Live.  
Raw.  
Only on *The Edge.*

---

Jeremy’s fingers hit the strings.  
Jeff’s bass slides in like silk dipped in bourbon.  
Bill’s first SNAP echoes like a match being struck.

And then…

Kathy sings.

---

*“I checked into the hotel, a perfect escape…”*

---

The studio goes still.

Even the *recording engineer* stops moving.

Out in the hallway, *two saleswomen freeze* in place like they’ve been caught eavesdropping on sin.

---

Sarah closes her eyes, just for a moment.

She *feels it.*

Right here.

Where they were *all born*.

Where *this myth started.*

And now?  
They’re writing *a new one.*

---

**INT. HOTEL LOBBY BUSINESS CENTER – COLUMBUS, OHIO – APRIL 17, 1992 – 6:22 P.M. EDT**

Sarah sits hunched at a dot matrix printer, one sneaker pressed against the leg of the chair, a cold Diet Coke sweating beside her.

She’s just faxed off her latest status update—bolded, bullet-pointed, *strategically triumphant*:

*OHIO HAS BEEN CONQUERED.*  
 *Push the signal east. NYC next. Let’s move.*

She leans back.  
 Satisfied.  
 Smug.

The fax machine whirs to life again.

One page.  
Top to bottom.  
All bold.

---

FROM: **WYLER**  
TO: **SARAH** MALCOM

*OHIO IS A GODDAMNED BIG STATE.*

(*underlined twice*)

*It’s not “conquered” just because one college kid wants Kathy to narrate his next orgasm.*

*THREE major media hubs: CLEVELAND, COLUMBUS, CINCINNATI.*  
 *And at least FIVE more that matter to retail, syndication, and grassroots tour-building.*

(*pause*)

*You want to conquer the Midwest?*  
 *Don’t scoot your ass to the Big Apple.*  
 *You haven’t earned the skyscrapers yet.*

*CLEVELAND ROCKS.*

*Go prove it.*

(*signed in scrawl: **WYLER***)

---

Sarah stares at it.

Sips the Diet Coke.

Exhales.  
 Laughs.  
 *Once.*

---

**SARAH** (to herself):  
 Fine.

(*pulls out her clipboard*)  
 Then *we take Cleveland.*

(*beat*)  
 With *fire.*

---

She flips to a blank page and writes across the top in all caps:

**OPERATION: ROCK CITY.**

---

**INT. TOUR VAN – SOMEWHERE ON I-71 NORTH – APRIL 17, 1992 – 8:46 P.M. EDT**

The van hums along the highway, moonlight slipping across the windows.  
 Empty fast food wrappers.  
 A half-used map of Ohio on the dash.  
 Jeremy asleep with headphones. Jeff sketching setlists. Kathy scribbling god-knows-what in the margin of a Gideon Bible.

Gilley turns to Sarah, riding shotgun.  
 He’s got that half-smile, one-leg-up cockiness she *usually wants to strangle—or ride.*

---

GILLEY (grinning):  
 Why are we doing *Cleveland* next?

(*beat*)  
 I mean, we just *leveled* Dayton.

Shouldn’t we be *celebrating*?

---

**SARAH** (not looking at him):  
 Because it’s *where gods are tested.*

(*then, deadpan*)  
 And it’s *less than four hours away.*

---

GILLEY (laughs):  
 That the *only* reason?

---

She turns her head.  
 Finally looks at him.

Cool. Calm. *Lethal.*

---

**SARAH** (low, direct):  
 You get *two hours* tonight.

---

GILLEY (eyebrow lifts):  
 Just two?

---

**SARAH**:  
 *I’ll be on top.*

---

Gilley’s smirk widens into something *close to reverence.*

---

**SARAH** (leaning closer):  
 And you. Will. *Not.* Write. A. *Song.* About. This.

(*pause*)  
 This isn’t *material*.  
 This is *therapy.*

---

GILLEY (hands raised, mock innocence):  
 No song.

(*beat*)  
 *Probably.*

---

**SARAH** (warning glare):  
 *Gilley.*

---

GILLEY (grinning):  
 Fine.  
 No lyrics.  
 No verses.  
 No bridges.

(*beat*)  
 Maybe… *an instrumental.*

---

**SARAH** (muttering):  
 I swear to God I’ll leave you at a *Love’s Travel Stop* in Wooster.

---

Outside, Cleveland looms on the horizon.

Inside the van?

The fuse is *burning* again.

---

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – DOWNTOWN CLEVELAND – APRIL 17, 1992 – 11:53 P.M. EDT**

The *city pulses outside*—streetcars, halogen halos, the wind off Lake Erie rattling the old windows.

Inside?

Sarah is straddling Gilley, sheets kicked off, dress somewhere near the minibar, hair clinging to her shoulders like battle streamers.

She’s in full control.

*Deliberate. Rhythmic. Ruthless.*

Each movement is *strategy and indulgence* fused together.

Gilley’s hands are on her hips, tight, as if letting go would break the spell.

He’s breathing in short bursts, but his eyes never leave hers.

This isn’t *just* sex.

It’s *her victory lap.*

---

**SARAH** (low, breathless, but focused):  
 So…

(*leans forward, skin sliding over his*)  
 What do you *think* of *life on the road?*

---

GILLEY (voice ragged, laughing softly):  
 Right now?

(*gasps, clutches harder*)  
 I think it’s *glorious.*

(*beat*)  
 And *dangerous.*

---

**SARAH** (grinning, slow):  
 Dangerous because you might *fall in love*?

Or because you might *write something dumb and make me leave you in Toledo?*

---

GILLEY (groaning):  
 I’m trying *very* hard not to do *either.*

---

**SARAH** (leaning down to his ear):  
 Try *harder.*

(*she moves down his shaft again—deeper, slower, a little cruel*)

Because *I’m not here for dreams.*

I’m here for *conquest.*

---

GILLEY (laughing through his teeth):  
 Well… *General Malcom.*  
 Consider my penis *occupied.*

---

She presses her mouth to his, devours the grin.

And as they move again—her body dictating pace, his hands submitting freely—  
 it’s clear:

This isn’t *romance*.

This is *command.*

And Sarah?

Sarah’s *winning*.

---

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – DOWNTOWN CLEVELAND – EARLY MORNING – APRIL 18, 1992 – 1:27 A.M. EDT**

The heat has broken.

The storm has passed.

The room is dark, lit only by the blinking red light on the smoke detector and the slow crawl of car headlights across the ceiling.

Sarah lies face-down on the bed, one leg hooked over the sheets, hair tangled, skin glowing with sweat and victory.

Gilley lies beside her, equally wrecked, hand tracing slow, idle lines down the curve of her spine.

Not possessive.

Just *curious.*

*Studying.*

---

GILLEY (softly):  
 What happens when the *Gauntlet Tour* ends?

---

Sarah’s eyes stay closed.  
 She doesn’t flinch.  
 She’s prepared.

Of course she is.

---

**SARAH** (quiet, but sure):  
 I’ll catch the *Eastern time zone shows.*

(*beat*)  
 Fly in for the *important ones.*

(*another beat, almost nothing*)  
 And I’ve *just moved into my fiancé’s house.*  
 *Long Island.*

---

The silence after is thick.  
 Not cruel.  
 Just *real.*

Gilley’s hand stops moving.

---

GILLEY (after a long pause):  
 Oh.

He says it like someone trying *not* to say *fuck.*

Or *I knew it.*

Or *why didn’t you tell me sooner.*

**SARAH** (finally opening her eyes):  
 Because it didn’t *matter* until it *might.*

GILLEY (quiet):  
 And now?

**SARAH** (flat, decisive):  
 It *still doesn’t.*

She rolls over to face him.  
 Eyes locked.

**SARAH**:  
 This is *the road.*  
 We *burn things here.*

(*beat*)  
 Then we *leave the ashes behind.*

Gilley exhales.

Nods once.

Then looks up at the ceiling and says nothing.

Because *what is there to say?*

He’s *not the ending.*

He’s *part of the fire.*

And *that*?

That’s the job.

---

**INT. JFK AIRPORT – TERMINAL 5 – MAY 2, 1992 – 8:41 A.M. EDT**

Sarah steps off the Jetway, sunglasses on, *diamond flashing subtly* on her left hand.  
 She’s in *neutral tones, a flawless travel blazer, low heels—not the yellow dress.*

This is *New York Sarah.*  
 *Home-field Sarah.*  
 Where *she doesn’t blink.*

But her mind is already *spinning with risk vectors.*

Because tomorrow?

Commuted hits WFMU.

And there’s *no room for chaos.*

Not Kathy.  
 Not Gilley.  
 *Not in her city.*

---

**INT. TAXI – MIDTOWN BOUND – MOMENTS LATER**

She flips through her leather planner.

Underlined twice:

*WFMU – LIVE STUDIO SET – 1 HR BLOCK*  
 *Experimental slot. Art crowd. No filter.*  
 *DO. NOT. RISK. GILLEY OR KATHY.*

---

Her pen hovers.

Then, she writes:

*JEFF.*

(*underlined once. Then again.*)

He’s the *dark horse.*  
 The *steady one.*  
 Not flashy.  
 Not unpredictable.

But *musical*.

*Witty* in the right context.  
 And, crucially?

*Doesn’t fuck up when given the mic.*

---

**INT. LONG ISLAND HOUSE – LIVING ROOM – THAT NIGHT**

She stands near the window, wine in hand.  
The skyline’s distant.  
Safe.

Fiancé watching TV behind her.  
Clueless.

She flips open the *Village Voice*.  
Headline jumps:

"COMMUTED’S BEST TRACK WAS WRITTEN BETWEEN WALLS"  
*Subhead: WFMU’s Ready for the Whispered Revolution*

She smiles.

Closes it.

Dials Jeff from the landline.

---

**SARAH** (into phone):  
 Pack a clean shirt.  
 **Leave the rest of them in Jersey.**

**You’re coming to *New York.***

**(*pause*)**  
 **And you’re gonna *talk for us.***

**JEFF (on the other end, stunned):**  
 **Wait, me?**

**(*nervous chuckle*)**  
 **You’re unleashing *me* on *WFMU?***

****SARAH**:**  
 **I don’t trust Kathy with *restraint***  
 **And I don’t trust Gilley with *a live mic anywhere within fifty blocks of my address.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **But you?**

**You’ve been *waiting for a moment.***

**(*smiles*)**  
 ***Here it is.***

---

**INT. JEFF’S MOTEL ROOM – ROUTE 22, NEW JERSEY – MAY 2, 1992 – 9:47 P.M. EDT**

Jeff is standing in the middle of his room, barefoot, shirtless, phone pressed to his ear, *shocked.*

Outside, a fluorescent sign blinks *“VACANCY”* like a dare.

The *dial tone hums* in his ear like a moral failing.

---

JEFF (to the dead line):  
 Did she just… *hang up on me?*

(*pause*)  
 She *hung up on me.*

He stares at the phone like it personally insulted his mother.

He sets it down gently, like it might explode.

Then mutters to the *beige motel wallpaper*:

JEFF:  
I *can’t sing.*  
That’s *not self-doubt.*  
That’s *fact.*  
That’s *biological science.*

(*beat*)  
*Jim Brown?*  
You want *Jim Fucking Brown dulcet baritones*?

Lady, I *run a flanger pedal through a bass amp and grunt at 120 BPM.*

He looks down at his suitcase.

Then at the *folded Commuted lyric sheet* on the nightstand.

Then sighs.

Hard.

---

JEFF (resigned):  
 Port Authority bus stop.  
 Newark.  
 Eight A.M.

(*beat*)  
 Cool.

Just… *sell my soul on air, why don’t we.*

---

He begins to *pack*.  
 *Button-up shirt.*  
 *One pair of clean socks.*  
 *Notebook full of lyrics he never expected to read aloud.*

And beneath it all?

A *tiny smile.*

Because *she called him.*

Because *this is his shot.*

Because *Sarah Malcom doesn’t bet on people lightly.*

---

**INT. MOTEL ROOM – ROUTE 1, NEWARK – MAY 2, 1992 – 10:41 P.M. EDT**

**The ceiling fan rattles like it's about to eject a blade.**  
 **The walls are thin enough that someone’s watching *Red Shoe Diaries* on max volume next door.**

**Jeff paces.**

**He’s down to boxers and a threadbare Commuted tour shirt from the *Dayton VFW gig that got shut down.***  
 **In his hands: a notepad.**  
 **On the bed: his bass.**  
 **On the dresser: *the lyrics to “Tangled Up.”***  
 **Next to them? *Panic.***

---

**JEFF (muttering):**  
 **I’m a *bassist.***  
 **Jim does *drums.***  
 **Kathy *sings.***  
 **Gilley *smirks in rhythm.***  
 **I *exist below the melody line* like a polite shadow.**

**(*he flips the notebook*)**  
 **How the *heckfire* am I supposed to *pull off this caper?***

---

**His pacing stops.**  
 **He stares at the lyrics again.**

***Feel the squirt, hear your sound…***

**Jeff exhales like someone bracing to walk into a hurricane with a paper umbrella.**

---

**Then it clicks.**

**A *brilliant, terrible idea*.**

**He reaches for the hotel phone.**

---

**INT. MOTEL ROOM – ELSEWHERE – JIM’S ROOM**

**Jim answers after two rings. Sounds like he’s mid crunch on a vending machine Snickers.**

---

**JIM (muffled):**  
 **Y’ello?**

---

**JEFF (fast):**  
 **Jim.**

**I can’t do *Tangled Up* as written.**

---

**JIM:**  
 **Well, no shit.**

---

**JEFF:**  
 **But I *can subvert it.***  
 **Flip the framing. Change the energy.**  
 **Instead of a *blowjob metaphor*…**

**(*beat*)**  
 **…It’s *cunnilingus.***

---

**There’s a beat.**

**Then:**

**JIM (grinning):**  
 **I *love* this.**  
 **You just *flipped the polarity of the song.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **I'll roll with you.**  
 **You and me, we’ll *blow their minds.***

**(*snickers*)**  
 **And make Kathy *hella jealous.***

---

**JEFF (deadpan):**  
 **I’m not saying it.**

---

**JIM:**  
 **Say it.**

---

**JEFF (smiling now):**  
 **…*Infamy awaits.***

---

**JIM (dead serious):**  
 ***WFMU* can *handle* us *subverting our most subversive song.***

---

**JEFF (correcting, grinning):**  
 **Most subversive… *to date.***

---

**He hangs up.**  
 **No panic now.**  
 **Just purpose.**

**Tomorrow?**

**The quiet guys are *bringing fire.***

---

**INT. MOTEL ROOM – ROUTE 1, NEWARK – MAY 3, 1992 – 12:08 A.M. EDT**

**The room has gone quiet.**  
 **TV off.**  
 **Bass gently resting on the chair like a sleeping animal.**  
 **The “Tangled Up” lyrics are folded, set on the nightstand beneath a half-drunk bottle of water and a cough drop he’s been meaning to throw away for three days.**

**Jeff lies in bed, wide-eyed, staring at the popcorn ceiling like it’s going to write the WFMU set for him.**

**Blankets tangled.**

**The kind of insomnia reserved for men who *don’t usually speak first in a room,* now about to be the *voice of the band* for an hour *on live radio in New York City.***

**His stomach twists.**

**Because tomorrow?**  
 **He’s *way out over his skis.***

---

**He sits up.**

**Swings his legs over the edge of the bed.**

**Grabs the *motel pad* and a *pen with weak ink.***

**He writes:**

***Don’t hold back.***  
 ***You’re the pulse now.***

---

**He tears it off.**

**Sticks it to the lampshade where he’ll see it first thing.**

**Stares at it.**

**Then adds, beneath in smaller print:**

***Jim’s with you.***  
 ***Sarah picked you.***  
 ***And if you don’t fumble this?***  
 ***You change your story.***

---

**He climbs back into bed.**

**Not calm.**

**But committed.**

**Tomorrow?**

**The bassist *becomes the beat.***

---

**INT. WFMU STUDIO – JERSEY CITY – MAY 3, 1992 – 10:58 A.M. EDT**

**The air smells like warm vinyl and solder, old headphones and the dust of decades of weird, glorious sound.**

**Posters for *Suicide, Sonic Youth, Nico, and The Fugs* are duct-taped to the walls like punk wallpaper.**  
 **The turntables are older than most interns.**  
 **The producer’s wearing *Birkenstocks and a minor hangover.***

**This is *WFMU.***

**This is *church.***

---

**Jeff stands behind the guest mic, bass in his lap, pick in his palm, *sweating through a pale blue Oxford.***

**He’s already asked the intern three times if it’s hot in here.**

**The red *“ON AIR”* light glows like *a silent dare.***

**And just behind him, calm as *a Zen arsonist*, stands Jim Brown, drumsticks in one back pocket, *paper cup of black coffee in hand.***

**Jim walks up beside him.**

**No mic yet.**

**Just presence.**

**Leans in, nods once.**

---

**JIM (soft):**  
 **Let’s go rewrite this.**

---

**\*\*Jeff exhales like it’s his first breath of the day.**

**He nods.**

**But he can’t help it.**  
 **He whispers—\*\***

---

**JEFF:**  
 **God, I hope the *interview crap* goes well.**

---

**JIM (grinning):**  
 **Just *do you*.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **This place?**  
 **They have *Jeff Buckley* on all the time.**

**(*leans in*)**  
 **And you can *whip his ass* *every day of the week*—**  
 ***and twice before dinner.***

---

**Jeff blinks.**

**Then snorts.**

---

**JIM (dead serious):**  
 **And if the *voice inside your head* tells you to *stop talking*?**

**Ignore it.**

**They *don’t play commercials* here, man.**

**So *indulge.***

---

**The red light flares brighter.**

**The host’s voice rolls in, cool and smooth:**

**“Live in studio this morning—Commuted’s *Jeff Evans and Jim Brown.***  
 **They've brought something *special.***  
 **You might want to… turn it up.”**

---

**Jim slides onto his drum throne with zero flair.**  
 **Just confidence.**

**Jeff breathes once more.**

**Then leans into the mic.**

**And says—**

---

**JEFF (into mic, steady):**  
 **We’re Commuted.**

**We’re *reversing polarity.***

**This is *Tangled Up.***

***Differently.***

---

**Bass hits.**

**Kick drum follows.**

**Something \*\*\*low, sensual, masculine, subversive—\*\*\*rises up.**

**And Jeff?**

**He *doesn’t hold back.***

---

**INT. WFMU STUDIO – OUTSIDE THE BOOTH – MAY 3, 1992 – 11:03 A.M. EDT**

**Sarah stands frozen behind the glass, headset tilted, clipboard untouched at her side.**  
 **She had walked in expecting awkward banter, maybe a little musical vamping, *some polite filler.***

**But what she’s hearing?**

**Is *Jeff.***

**And *Jim.***

**Doing *Tangled Up.***

**And doing it *completely inside out.***

---

**The *bass is smooth and low*, pulsing like breath against skin.**

***Jim’s kit is minimal but precise—***  
 **kick, rim taps, feathered cymbal, *all heat, no excess.***

**And Jeff?**

**He’s speaking the lyrics like *prayer and poetry* mixed with *dirty confidence*.**

**Reversed roles.**  
 **New tempo.**  
 **New power.**

---

***“Run my tongue up and down your soul…”***

***“Mmm, I love the way we begin…”***

***“Feel the squirt, hear your sound…”***

---

**Sarah’s mouth slowly opens.**

**She *doesn’t blink.***

**Then?**

**She starts to grin.**

---

****SARAH** (half-laughing, under her breath):**  
 ***GOD. DAMN.***

**The boys *did what?***

---

**She turns to the producer standing beside her, whose jaw is *slightly unhinged.***

**He shrugs helplessly, still mouthing *“holy shit”*.**

---

****SARAH** (laughing now):**  
 **OOOOOO, *somebody’s* gonna get her *panties in a bunch.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **And *it ain’t me.***

---

**Because Jeff and Jim?**

**They just *picked Kathy’s purse.***

**Right on *public broadcast*.**

**In *New York City.***

---

****SARAH** (giddy):**  
 **This is *better than sabotage.***

**This is a civil *war with taste.***

---

**INT. WFMU STUDIO – CONTROL ROOM – MAY 3, 1992 – 11:07 A.M. EDT**

**The song winds down like a *slow sigh in a candlelit room*—Jeff’s final bass note fades under *Jim’s gentle rimshot,* like the punctuation at the end of a whispered confession.**

**The *booth is dead silent*.**

**No outro music.**

**No commercial.**

**Just one stunned *human pause.***

**Then—**

**DJ RANDALL, iconic WFMU host, leans back from the mic, eyes wide behind round glasses, ponytail fraying like his sense of protocol.**

**He turns toward the producer behind the glass, mouth half open, and then just speaks—*on air, raw, unfiltered:***

---

**DJ RANDALL (live):**  
 **I’m sorry…**

**(*leans closer to the mic*)**  
 **Was that your *bassist* just *seducing New York*?**

---

**\*\*Behind the glass, Sarah grins like *a fox at the chicken wire.***

**She leans forward, presses the talkback button to the host mic, and with zero hesitation:**

---

****SARAH** (smooth, wicked):**  
 **Uh… *yeaaaah.***

**(*grinning*)**  
 ***Wasn’t it delicious?***

---

**Randall throws up his hands, laughing.**

---

**DJ RANDALL (live, delighted):**  
 **Ladies, gentlemen, and *everyone with a pulse*—**

**That was *Jeff motherfucking Evans* of *Commuted*, assisted by *the prophet of restraint himself, Jim Brown.***

**They just turned *Tangled Up* into *something filthy, divine, and 100% legally unfit for AM radio.***

---

**Phones light up.**  
 **The soundboard intern *pumps a fist.***

**Sarah?**

**Already pulling out her *notebook*, flipping to a fresh page marked:**

**DEPLOY JEFF**  
 **(*when Kathy gets too comfortable*)**

---

**Because *now*?**

**The *quiet ones* are no longer *just support.***

**They’re *weapons.***

**And Sarah?**

**She’s *armed to the teeth.***

---

**EXT. WFMU STUDIO – PARKING LOT – JERSEY CITY – MAY 3, 1992 – 11:28 A.M. EDT**

**The door swings open.**

**Jeff and Jim step into the sunlight, both squinting—partly from the brightness, partly from the afterglow of *total artistic theft executed in front of a live radio audience.***

**A *station intern bolts out after them*, clutching a paper coffee cup in each hand, breathless with reverence.**

---

**INTERN (starstruck, offering cups):**  
 **One for *Baritone God*…**  
 **One for *Rhythm Prophet.***

**(*grinning*)**  
 **You *wrecked it.***

---

**Jeff raises a brow.**  
 **Jim freezes.**

---

**JIM (blinking):**  
 **Wait… *Baritone*?**

**(*beat*)**  
 **You mean *me*?**

**(*scoffs*)**  
 ***Bro.***

**(*hands go up*)**  
 **Ever *hear of Phil Collins?***

---

**JEFF (trying not to laugh):**  
 **Shh…**  
 **I think they’re *on our side, Jim.***

---

**JIM (still hyped):**  
 **I *have range.***  
 **I *choose* to stay behind the kit.**  
 **It's *aesthetic.***

---

**Sarah walks out behind them, clipboard casually tucked under her arm, hair pinned, *expression smug and glowing like a general post-victory.***

**She hears Jim’s rant, and without breaking stride:**

---

****SARAH** (flatly):**  
 **He used to moonlight two summers ago in a *barbershop quartet.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **Funded half his college tuition singing *bass harmonies at ice cream socials and weddings.***

---

**JIM (turning beet red):**  
 **That’s *not public knowledge.***

---

****SARAH** (grinning):**  
 **It is *now.***

**(*sips coffee*)**  
 ***Baritone God.* Own it.**

---

**JEFF (to Jim, with a smirk):**  
 **You want to take *lead* next time?**

---

**JIM (smiling now, shrugging):**  
 **Maybe.**  
 **But only if I can *sing about dairy and longing.***

---

**They all laugh.**

**Because they *did it.***

**And no one *saw it coming.***

---

**INT. PAYPHONE ALCOVE – HUDSON STREET, JERSEY CITY – MAY 3, 1992 – 12:03 P.M. EDT**

**Sarah grips the payphone receiver, one foot propped against the booth wall, coffee in one hand, a smirk blooming beneath her sunglasses.**

**Across the street, Jim and Jeff are still basking like war heroes in a record store parking lot.**

**She dials.**

**Two rings.**  
 ***Wyler picks up.***

---

****WYLER** (curt, Midtown bark):**  
 **Talk.**

---

****SARAH** (cool and surgical):**  
 **The *bassist and the drummer* just made *national radio blush.***

**(*pause*)**  
 **Your move.**

---

**There’s a silence on the line.**

**That rare Wyler beat when *information outruns expectation.***

**Then—**

---

****WYLER** (calm):**  
 **I *heard.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **Is that *going out in syndication* nationwide?**

---

****SARAH** (grinning now):**  
 ***Already is.***

**WFMU’s *pushing the segment to affiliates tonight*—experimental slot syndication.**  
 **From *Philly to Berkeley.***

---

****WYLER**:**  
 **Goddamn.**

**(*pause*)**  
 **And this was *Jeff and Jim.***  
 **No Kathy.**  
 **No Gilley.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **No nudity?**

---

****SARAH** (smirking):**  
 ***None visible.***

**Just *aural seduction.***

**(*leans into the mouthpiece*)**  
 **We *reversed Tangled Up.***  
 ***Cunnilingus perspective.***  
 **Jeff led. Jim harmonized.**

**You *owe me* for this one.**

---

****WYLER** (long pause):**  
 **I’m gonna need *tapes.***  
 **I’m gonna need *quotes.***  
 **I’m gonna need *time to figure out how the hell to sell this.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **Also?**

**Tell Jeff he’s *not allowed* to get mysterious and disappear now.**  
 **He *belongs* to me.**

---

****SARAH** (sipping coffee):**  
 **He belongs to *the myth*.**

---

****WYLER**:**  
 **Same thing.**

**(*pause*)**  
 **Alright.**  
 **Push Cleveland hard.**  
 **Then we *circle back* and drop this like a *live grenade on morning radio.***

---

****SARAH** (clicks tongue):**  
 **Already ahead of you.**

**She hangs up.**

**Not cocky.**  
 ***Victorious.***

**Because today?**

**The *quiet ones* took the mic.**

**And *everyone heard.***

---

**INT. **SARAH**’S HOTEL ROOM – CLEVELAND – MAY 3, 1992 – 9:11 P.M. EDT**

**The city is humming outside.**  
 **She’s just started unwinding—halfway through washing her face, *one earring off, one still on.***

**The room phone rings.**

**Line 1: *Wyler.***

**She answers, expecting more strategy, maybe an “atta girl.”**

**Instead—**

---

****WYLER** (low, clipped):**  
 **Sarah.**

**Get them in *New York City* by the *tenth.***

---

****SARAH** (instantly alert):**  
 **What's going on?**

---

****WYLER**:**  
 **I’ve got *some shit to say.***

***Bad news.***

**Come to the *office.***

---

**(*pause. beat. quieter now.*)**

---

****WYLER**:**  
 **I want to *tell you to your face.***

---

**CLICK.**

**He hangs up.**

**No room for questions.**  
 **No clues in his voice.**  
 **Just the kind of finality that *makes your stomach go cold.***

---

**Sarah stands in silence.**

**Staring at the phone.**  
 **Drip of the bathroom faucet ticking like a clock.**

**She wipes her face with the towel, slow.**  
 **Then reaches for her clipboard.**

***Flight plans.***

***Hotel rebookings.***

***Band logistics.***

**But mostly?**

**A note scribbled at the top of the page:**

**“What does he know that I don’t?”**

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – **WYLER**’S OFFICE – MIDTOWN MANHATTAN – MAY 3, 1992 – 10:37 P.M. EDT**

**The skyline glows outside like a slow-burning fuse.**  
 **The windows are shut.**  
 **The door is locked.**

**Inside, *Wyler is pacing like a caged animal*—tie off, sleeves rolled, eyes burning with *pure, nuclear-grade fury.***

**On his desk:**  
 **A fax from *MTV Standards and Practices*.**  
 **Top page highlighted in yellow:**

**RE: “Come Inside Me” Music Video Submission**  
 ***At this time, we cannot approve the content for scheduled airing on July 4th or any future date under our current broadcast policy.***

***Visual implication \+ lyrical content deemed in conflict with audience standards.***  
 ***We encourage artist to consider editing for re-submission.***  
 ***(Internal note: “This is fire, but we’re not ready to die on this hill.”)***

---

****WYLER** (snarling):**  
 **“Not ready to die on this hill”?**

**You *spineless, Nickelodeon-adjacent, beige-couched cowards.***

---

**He picks up the fax.**

**Tears it.**

**Twice.**

***Then carefully smooths it out.***  
 **Because he *needs* the proof.**

---

**He turns to the stereo.**  
 **Blasts the final chorus.**

***“Come inside me… come inside me…”***

***NOW\!***  
 ***NOW\!***  
 ***NOW\!***

---

****WYLER** (shouting over the speakers):**  
 **It’s *art*, not *porn*\!**  
 **It’s *truth*, not *titillation\!***

**It’s *going Platinum* by *Saturday* and you *just flinched\!***

---

**He slams a fist onto the desk.**

**Hard.**

**Startles himself.**

**Then laughs—low, ugly.**

---

****WYLER** (to himself):**  
 **They just *branded themselves.***  
 **Not with a *no.***

**With a *whimper.***

**MTV just said:**  
 ***“We’re pussies.”***

---

**He grabs the phone.**  
 **Dials HR.**

**Doesn’t wait for pleasantries.**

---

****WYLER**:**  
 **Effective *immediately*—Sarah Malcom’s title is *Account Representative.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **Backdate it to *March 1st.***

**Add *8% to her salary.***  
 **Yes. *Retroactive.***

**(*pause*)**  
 **Because she *earned it* when she *dragged this band to the gates of hell and made people dance in the fire.***

---

**He hangs up.**

**Stands there.**

**Breathing.**

**The fax on the desk.**

**The stereo still humming.**

**And *a storm building behind his eyes.***

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – **WYLER**’S OFFICE – MIDTOWN MANHATTAN – MAY 6, 1992 – 9:08 A.M. EDT**

**The morning light slices through the blinds like judgment.**

**Sarah steps inside.**

**Clipboard. Blazer. *Prepared.***

**But she’s never walked into Wyler’s office with this kind of tension riding up her spine. Her instincts—so finely tuned by now—are *screaming*.**

**Wyler doesn’t offer coffee.**  
 **Doesn’t look up at first.**

**Just stands at the window, a fax curled in one hand, *veins in his neck like tension wires.***

---

****WYLER** (without turning):**  
 **You know what *today* was supposed to be?**

---

****SARAH** (quietly):**  
 **Final post-prod for the *"Come Inside Me"* video.**  
 **Approval for Fourth of July.**  
 **Launch day. Syndicated spin coverage.**  
 **National lift-off.**

---

****WYLER** (turns now, voice low and *dangerous*):**  
 ***That’s right.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **Except *MTV*?**

***Took. A. Fucking. Walk.***

**(*waves the fax*)**  
 ***Standards and Practices.***  
 ***Declined.***

**They didn’t even *say* it outright, Sarah.**

**Didn’t say *“too sexy.”***

**Didn’t say *“inappropriate.”***

**What they *did* say?**

**(*reads from the page*)**  
 ***“We are unable to accommodate a broadcast schedule under our current policy environment.”***

**(*crumples it*)**  
 **They *pussed out.***

---

**Sarah doesn’t move.**

**She’s been in *plenty of heat* before.**

**But *this?***

**This is *Wyler enraged at the system.***  
 **Not her.**  
 **Not the band.**

**The *system.***

---

****WYLER** (walking straight at her):**  
 **Do you know what it means when *Come Inside Me* hits *Platinum* this *weekend*…**

**(*voice sharpens*)**  
 **…and *MTV* says *no?***

---

****SARAH**:**  
 **It means *we beat them.***

**And they’re *too scared* to admit it.**

---

****WYLER** (grinning, fuming):**  
 ***Exactly.***

**And I’m done *waiting* for them to get their *courage back.***

**So here’s *your new mission.***

**(*steps in close, voice low, brutal*)**  
 ***FUCKING MAKE THEM PAY.***

---

**Sarah stares at him, jaw tight.**

**And then—*she exhales.***

**Not fear.**

***Fire.***

**She’s *right behind him.***

---

****SARAH** (quietly):**  
 **Okay.**

---

****WYLER** (sits at his desk, already scribbling):**  
 **Effective today?**

**You’re no longer “junior anything.”**

***Account Representative.***

**(*beat*)**  
 ***Eight percent raise.***

**Backdated to *March 1st.***

**Because you *carried this band like a bayonet.***

**Now?**

***Take New York.***  
 ***Break something.***  
 ***And when you’re done—***  
 ***Make them beg to re-air this video.***

---

**Sarah nods.**

**No clipboard.**

**No hesitation.**

**Just *purpose*.**

**She turns.**

**Walks out.**

**Ready.**

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – **WYLER**’S OFFICE – MIDTOWN MANHATTAN – MAY 6, 1992 – 9:27 A.M. EDT**

**The door swings shut behind Sarah with a crisp *click.***

**Wyler’s already grabbing the phone.**

**Not the office line.**  
 **Not for staff.**

***His direct line.***

**The *one* that rings *overseas.***

**He scrolls to "DUNNING, R." – *BBC2 programming director, fellow media predator,* and a *savage five-iron* on weekends in Surrey.**

**He dials.**

---

**RUPERT DUNNING (groggy, across the pond):**  
 **Christ, Wyatt… it’s not even *bloody tea time.***

---

****WYLER** (flat):**  
 ***America flinched.***

---

**RUPERT (instantly alert):**  
 **MTV?**

---

****WYLER**:**  
 ***Punted.***

**“Come Inside Me.”**  
 **Their *Fourth of July flagship video.***  
 **Gone. *Declined.***

**No public statement.**  
 **Just *cowardice* by fax.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **Your turn.**

---

**RUPERT:**  
 **You want BBC2 to… *run it raw?***

---

****WYLER**:**  
 ***Air the uncut video.***

**Midnight block.**  
 **European syndication.**  
 **Push the *performance version* too—the one we’re packaging for Glastonbury press.**

---

**RUPERT (smirking now):**  
 **And *what’s in it for me, Wyatt?***

---

****WYLER** (leans back, voice cold):**  
 ***Legacy.***

**The Brits aired *Come Inside Me* when *MTV hid behind their khakis.***

---

**RUPERT:**  
 **Let me guess. You’ll send me a copy labeled *“Not Fit for America.”***

---

****WYLER** (grinning):**  
 **Already did.**

**It’s in your *private box* marked *Fore\!***  
 **The one your assistant pretends not to know about.**

---

**RUPERT (low whistle):**  
 **Well, hell.**  
 ***Let’s make the colonies squirm.***

---

****WYLER**:**  
 **That’s the spirit.**

**(*hangs up without goodbye.*)**

---

**Wyler leans back.**

**Cracks his knuckles.**

***Two continents.***

***One band.***

***No mercy.***

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – MAIN CONFERENCE ROOM – MAY 7, 1992 – 10:16 A.M. EDT**

**The fax machine chirps like it’s smug.**  
 **Sarah pulls the sheet straight from the tray, eyes scanning before it’s even cooled.**

**THIS WEEK’S DEBUTS: US TOP 40 SINGLES – WEEK ENDING MAY 9, 1992**

**There it is.**

**\#29 — AFTER HOURS –•– Commuted – 1 (29)**

**She stares at it.**

**Doesn’t blink.**

**Then—slowly—she smiles.**

**A small one.**  
 **Tight.**  
 **Triumphant.**

**The kind of smile you get when *the universe finally admits you were right all along.***

---

****SARAH** (to herself):**  
 ***Twenty-nine.***

**No payola.**  
 **No favors.**  
 ***No MTV.***

**Just *after-hours girls with torn jeans and big feelings.***  
 **Just *college radio and guerilla field ops and DJ seduction cookies.***

***And it worked.***

---

**She circles the number in red pen.**

***Commuted.***  
 ***Top 40\.***  
 ***No gimmicks.***

---

**She walks straight to Wyler’s office, opens the door without knocking, holds the page up like a *warrant.***

---

****SARAH**:**  
 **We *cracked* the *Top Forty.***

***After Hours.***

**Number *twenty-nine.***

**First week.**

---

****WYLER** (glancing up from paperwork, deadpan):**  
 ***And Billy Ray Cyrus is \#83.***

**(*leans back, smirking*)**  
 **This… is gonna be *fun.***

---

**INT. NME EDITORIAL OFFICE – LONDON – MAY 8, 1992 – 3:19 P.M. GMT**

**The print room is a mess of ink fumes, takeaway curry wrappers, and *disgust*.**

**Tiernan O'Dowd is pounding the keys of his typewriter like it personally insulted his ancestors.**

**The new piece?**

***Pure fire.***

**The *headline* is already done—scrawled in black marker on the top of the page:**

**NEVER MIND THE BOLLOCKS, MTV – THE PEOPLE ALREADY DID**

---

**The rest of the piece reads like a man exorcising *decades of pent-up transatlantic rage* in under 500 words.**

---

**TIERNAN (reading aloud as he types):**

***MTV, once the so-called arbiter of taste, now stands in full coward’s bloom—refusing to air Commuted’s “Come Inside Me,” a song with more heart, heat, and art than the last decade of their rotation combined.***

***They call it “too provocative.” Too much. Too suggestive.***

**(*slams spacebar*)**

***TOO GOOD, they mean.***

**\*Because it turns out when women write about *pleasure* with *precision* and *power*, the men in suits—those gobshite assholes—go looking for *editing notes and comfortable silence.***

---

**TIERNAN (sharper now):**

***Meanwhile, “After Hours”—the band’s nocturnal confessional—enters the US Top 40 at No. 29\.***

***No major video. No late-night MTV rotation. No gatekeepers.***

**\*Just *airplay, tape sharing, and truth.***

**(*slams return key*)**

***These langers may run American television, but they do not run culture. Not anymore.***

**(*another beat*)**

***Let them die without a priest.***

---

**TIERNAN (softly, satisfied):**  
 **That’ll land like a hammer in a porcelain toilet.**

---

**He signs it:**

**TIERNAN O’DOWD – STILL LISTENING TO REAL MUSIC, YOU COWARDS**

**And shouts toward layout:**

---

**TIERNAN:**  
 **Oi, Phil\!**  
 **Print this *on the centre spread* in *bold black ink.***  
 ***We’re going to piss off a continent.***

---

**PHIL (from across the room):**  
 **As per usual?**

---

**TIERNAN:**  
 ***Damn right.***

**And then he lights a cigarette like it’s a victory cigar.**

**Because it is.**

---

**INT. NME EDITORIAL OFFICE – LONDON – MAY 8, 1992 – 3:31 P.M. GMT**

**Tiernan’s just handed the carbon-smudged pages to Phil, who’s now squinting at the draft with a copy editor’s eye and the skepticism of a man who’s seen too many rants, not enough revolutions.**

**Phil sets the paper down, lifts his mug of tea like a peace offering, and deadpans—**

---

**PHIL:**  
 **Do ya think the *Yanks* are gonna *understand any of your insults?***

**“Gobshite”?**  
 **“Langer”?**  
 **“Die without a priest”?**  
 **You’re *fluent in holy war* and they’re over there choking on *Achy Breaky Heart.***

---

**TIERNAN (lighting a cigarette, unfazed):**  
 **They’ll *feel it*.**

**(*exhales*)**  
 **You don’t need to *understand a curse word* when it’s hurled *like a brick through your telly.***

**(*smirks*)**  
 **Besides, the *right Americans* will *get it*.**

**The *Commuted ones.***  
 **The *college radio kids.***  
 **The ones *MTV’s afraid of.***

---

**PHIL:**  
 **And the rest?**

---

**TIERNAN:**  
 **They can *look it up.***

**Or *feel the burn.***  
 **Either way, *message delivered.***

---

**PHIL (grinning):**  
 **Jesus, you’re insufferable when you’re right.**

---

**TIERNAN (blowing smoke):**  
 **That’s why I write.**

---

**INT. NYC SUBWAY – 6 TRAIN TO 51ST – MAY 10, 1992 – 10:24 A.M. EDT**

**The band rides in silence, mostly.**

**A couple of commuters glance up from their papers, side-eyeing Gilley’s mesh shirt, Kathy’s flannel and leather combo, and Jeff’s well-worn notebook resting across his lap like it’s a holy text.**

**But no one recognizes them.**

**Yet.**

**They're *\#29 on the Billboard charts*, but *underground in every way that counts.***

**Even *anonymous*.**

**Which, frankly, *Cremeans loves*—because he doesn’t have to *herd egos* through Penn Station this time.**

**He sits near the door, sipping a Dunkin’ coffee like it’s victory champagne.**

---

**CREMEANS (to himself):**  
 ***Everyone’s ridden the subway now.***  
 **Look at us.**  
 ***Regular New Yorkers.***

---

**GILLEY is three seats down, grinning behind his sunglasses, nudging Jeremy.**

---

**GILLEY (low):**  
 **I got *plans* tonight.**

---

**JEREMY (not even looking up):**  
 **Sarah?**

---

**GILLEY (smug):**  
 **She *knows we cracked the Top 40*.**

**We’re *number twenty-nine*.**  
 **I *didn’t even bring condoms to New York.***  
 ***That’s how confident I was.***

---

**KATHY (from across the aisle, without looking up):**  
 **Say it ain’t so.**

---

**JEFF (smirking):**  
 **Gilley, you’re on the *charts.***  
 **Not *Inside Edition.***

**Calm down.**

---

**GILLEY:**  
 **I’m *just saying*—debuting *at twenty-nine*?**

**MTV passed.**  
 **America *didn’t.***

**This is *legend-building stuff.***

---

**CREMEANS (deadpan):**  
 **Try not to *build your legend* in Sarah’s bed *before* we hit the conference room.**

---

**The subway *rattles into 51st*.**

**Doors open.**  
 **Band rises.**

**They’re headed *uptown.***

**To *Island Records.***

**To *Wyler.***

**To *whatever the hell comes next.***

---

**And tonight?**

**Gilley’s still hoping he comes inside Sarah.**

***Figuratively.***

***Maybe literally.***

**Depends on the wine.**

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – 6TH FLOOR LOBBY – MAY 10, 1992 – 11:03 A.M. EDT**

**The elevator dings open with a sterile chime.**  
 **The doors part.**

**And the band steps into *a surreal fever dream of validation.***

**There, plastered across a *massive stretch of wall behind glass*, is a *poster-sized printout* of the *Billboard Top 40*.**

**Big, bold red Sharpie ring around:**

**\#29 — AFTER HOURS –•– COMMUTED – 1 (29)**

**Under it, in Wyler’s unmistakable scrawl:**

***“THIS IS WHAT A WARHEAD LOOKS LIKE.”***

---

**They freeze.**  
 **No one speaks for a second.**

**Because it’s *them.***  
 **On a *chart* they’ve read since *junior high.***

**And it’s *real.***

---

**JEREMY (soft):**  
 **Holy shit.**

---

**JEFF (blinking, pulling out a disposable camera):**  
 **Jim.**

**Please.**

**You *have to* take a picture of us with that.**

---

**JIM (already grinning):**  
 **You want *a vertical* or *a horizontal* for the fridge?**

---

**JEFF:**  
 **This is *for Mom and Dad.***  
 **Send it with *handwritten captions.***  
 ***Frame it.***  
 **Wrap it in *Christmas.***

---

**Jim lines them up in front of the display.**  
 **Jeremy adjusts his collar.**  
 **Jeff’s too stunned to pose right.**

**Flash.**

**Click.**

**Another.**

**And they’re *laughing.***

---

**KATHY (arms crossed, smirking):**  
 **Hey—does *Mr. Evans* still drive *Silver Bullet One*?**

**(*mock gasp*)**  
 **Please tell me *he finally fixed the headlight wiring.***

---

**JEREMY (grinning):**  
 **You mean *the world’s loudest 1982 Cutlass Supreme?***

---

**JIM:**  
 **Tell him *I’m unavailable* to work the *Dayton Air Show* this summer.**

**I’m *otherwise detained.***

**(*beat*)**  
 ***Charted.***

---

**They *crack up.***

**The kind of *insider, dirt-under-the-nails, Midwestern garage-band laughter* that *no magazine will ever capture correctly.***

**It’s *inside jokes.***  
 ***Rustbelt glory.***  
 **And the *sudden, sharp smell of possibility.***

**They’re still *just kids from Dayton*—**

**But now?**

**They’re *Dayton with a bullet.***

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – CONFERENCE ROOM – 6TH FLOOR – MAY 10, 1992 – 11:26 A.M. EDT**

**The long glass table is already set.**  
 **Legal pads.**  
 **Cans of Diet Coke.**  
 **A plate of slightly stale biscotti someone tried to make look intentional.**

**In the corner stands a *life-size cardboard cutout* of Commuted’s band logo—gritty, iconic, flammable.**

**And on the wall?**

**A barely-mounted 32" plasma TV, clearly not the standard issue.**

**An intern with a clipboard paces near the door, checking bets with professional detachment.**

---

**CHUCK THE INTERN (muttering):**  
 **Okay, official tally…**

**(*ticking boxes*)**

* **Kathy: *Drink toss*.**

* **Jeff: *Standee arson*.**

* **Gilley: *TV ejection.***

**(*beat*)**  
 ***Odds:***  
 **Gilley’s rage: *\+110***  
 **Kathy’s hand-eye coordination: *\-125***  
 **Jeff’s inner chaos: *wild card.***

---

****WYLER** walks in, tosses a $20 into the intern’s cup like it’s church tithe.**

---

****WYLER**:**  
 **My money’s on *Jeff.***

**He’s quiet.**

**Too quiet.**

**That *standee* is *toast.***

**(*nods toward it*)**  
 **We *swapped it in from an old lobby display.***  
 **That thing *wants to burn.***

---

****SARAH** (entering behind him):**  
 **Please.**

***Kathy*** **will *fling a drink* in my face *before* Jeff even registers the news.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **That’s not *fear* talking.**  
 **That’s *historical precedent.***

---

**CHUCK:**  
 **Y’all brought in *a backup plasma TV*?**

---

****WYLER**:**  
 **From the *break room.***  
 **That *Sony Bravia* in here?**

**Yeah, *no*.**  
 **It’s *too nice* to die for art.**

---

**CHUCK (scribbling):**  
 **If Gilley goes *full linebacker* again, I’d say 22 feet easy.**

---

**The energy is *nuclear.***

**Outside the room, you can *hear the band approaching.***

**Laughter.**  
 **Bootsteps.**  
 **Bass cases being banged into corners.**

**Everyone inside the conference room *tenses.***

**Bets are placed.**  
 **Eyebrows are raised.**  
 **The *camera is metaphorical,* but everyone knows—**

**This is the shot before detonation.**

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – CONFERENCE ROOM – 6TH FLOOR – MAY 10, 1992 – 11:29 A.M. EDT**

**The door swings open.**

**Kathy walks in first, black espresso in hand, shades on, fresh off a sidewalk cigarette and a killer pair of boots that somehow still whisper when she walks.**

**She stops.**

**Immediately.**

**The room is wrong.**

**No agenda printed.**  
 **No coffee carafe.**  
 **No post-it marks on Sarah’s clipboard.**

**And Sarah?**

**Standing at the far end of the table—**  
 **hair pulled back too neatly,**  
 **white blouse buttoned too high,**  
 **and under it?**

**A plain white bra.**

**Visible enough through the thin cotton that Kathy’s eyes land on it like radar.**

**It is *the most un-Sarah thing she’s worn all spring.***

**No lace.**  
 **No strategic cleavage.**  
 **No power move cami.**

**Just *white.***  
 **Unremarkable.**  
 **Unflirty.**

---

**KATHY (slowing her walk, suspicious):**  
 **You wore *that?***

**(*sips her espresso*)**  
 **You *de-tuned* your entire *sex frequency.***

---

****SARAH** (even, clipped):**  
 **I didn’t come here to seduce.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **I came to *tell you something.***

---

**KATHY (quietly, peeling off her sunglasses):**  
 **Oh *shit.***

---

**She turns to Jeff, who just stepped in with Jim.**

**They clock the silence.**

**Jeremy mutters, “Something’s wrong.”**

**Gilley walks in, freezes.**  
 **Eyes flick to the *plasma TV*.**

**Back to Sarah.**

**Then to the *standee*.**

**Then *back to Sarah.***

---

**KATHY (to the room):**  
 **Nobody sit.**

**(*beat*)**  
 ***She’s not smiling.***  
 ***And she’s not dressing to win.***

---

**The entire band goes still.**

***Battle-trained still.***

**Even *Cremeans* stops chewing his gum.**

---

****SARAH** (voice steady, eyes locked on Kathy):**  
 ***MTV passed.***

**(*beat*)**  
 ***BBC aired it.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **The *people*?**

***Already chose.***

---

**Gilley lets out a slow exhale like a fuse just lit behind his teeth.**

**Jeff adjusts his collar.**

**Jeremy’s fingers twitch toward an invisible fretboard.**

**Kathy?**

**She sips her espresso.**

**Then tilts her head.**

---

**KATHY (calm):**  
 **How *bad* is the fallout?**

**(*beat*)**  
 **And *which one of us* is going to *break something first?***

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – CONFERENCE ROOM – MAY 10, 1992 – 11:32 A.M. EDT**

**Everything breaks *all at once.***

**There’s *no warning.***

**There’s *no slow boil.***

**Just:**

***GILLEY,*** **eyes glassy with restrained chaos, grabbing the *32-inch plasma TV* off its mount like it’s a piece of overgrown LEGO and *hurling it* across the room—**

***CRASH\!***

**It *explodes against a potted plant* in the corner. *Soil everywhere.* A *fern dies.***

---

**At the same moment—**

***JEFF*** **walks to the *Commuted standee*, quiet as a funeral… and then *flicks his Zippo.***

**A *fwoosh* of flame curls up from the cardboard logo like it’s *meant to burn.***

***“Symbolic,”*** **he mutters.**

---

**Then—**

***KATHY.***

**She just gives Sarah *that giggle.***

**The *one* that sounds like *a dare wrapped in perfume.***

**And as the TV smolders and smoke begins to curl toward the ceiling vent—**

**KATHY (smirking):**  
 ***Dodge this.***

**She *tosses the remaining espresso* right at *Sarah’s chest.***

---

****SARAH** (stepping aside like she’s reading choreography):**  
 **Nope.**

**(splat — the drink misses, splashes on the wall beside the door)**

---

****WYLER** barges in at the sound of chaos, holding a folder and yelling like this is exactly what he expected:**

****WYLER** (shouting):**  
 ***I JUST HAD THIS FLOOR REPAINTED\!***

---

**CHUCK THE INTERN, grinning ear to ear, tallying notes on his betting pool clipboard:**

**✔ Gilley \= TV massacre**  
 **✔ Jeff \= Firestarter**  
 **✔ Kathy \= Beverage-based assault**  
 **✔ Sarah \= Untouchable**

---

**CREMEANS (sipping his coffee, cool as hell):**  
 **Yep.**

***That’s a band at \#29.***

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – CONFERENCE ROOM – MAY 10, 1992 – 11:34 A.M. EDT**

**Smoke.**  
 **Glass.**  
 **Burnt cardboard curling into ash.**  
 **The smoldering TV carcass lying in a ruined potted plant like the last casualty of a corporate war zone.**

**Kathy’s espresso stain still drips down the drywall.**  
 **Wyler’s screaming into a folder.**  
 **Gilley’s pacing like a lion post-impact.**  
 **Jeff’s watching the standee dissolve like he just baptized the future.**

**And then—**

**Cremeans unzips his duffel bag.**

**Real calm.**

**Real quiet.**

---

**CREMEANS (deadpan):**  
 **I *knew* one of these *New York debriefs* would go sideways eventually.**

---

**From the bag he pulls…**

***A bright orange canister.***  
 **Bold black letters: UDAP BEAR REPELLENT**  
 ***2.0% major capsaicinoids.***

---

****WYLER** (alarmed):**  
 ***Cremeans, what the holy hell is that?***

---

**CREMEANS:**  
 ***Control.***

---

**CHUCK THE INTERN (wide-eyed, clipboard still in hand):**  
 **Wait, is that—**

**(*brain short-circuits*)**  
 **I wonder what *bear spray* smells li—**

***TSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSHT\!\!\!***

---

**Cremeans *unleashes a short burst.***

**Wide cone.**  
 **Center mass.**  
 **Chuck.**

**The clipboard clatters to the ground.**

**Chuck’s final coherent thought before reality *detaches from his sinuses* is exactly:**

***Oh. Pepper and death and broken promises. Got it.***

---

**CHUCK (screaming):**  
 **OH GOD IT’S IN MY EARS**  
 **IT’S IN MY *LIFE***  
 **WHY WOULD BEARS NEED THIS MUCH PAIN**

---

**KATHY dives under the table, coughing through laughter.**  
 **Jeff backs toward the window, eyes watering, muttering “what the actual fuck.”**  
 **Jim rips open the conference room door to ventilate.**  
 **Gilley’s trying to fan himself with a laminated copy of their press kit.**

---

****WYLER** (coughing, furious):**  
 ***CREMEANS.***

**WHY.**

---

**CREMEANS (cool, spritzing the can once more into the empty air):**  
 ***Because I love these kids.***

**And sometimes?**

**You gotta *keep the wild things in line.***

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – CONFERENCE ROOM, ZONE A4 – MAY 10, 1992 – 11:36 A.M. EDT**

**The air’s still thick with pepper spray.**  
 **Chuck is somewhere in the corner whimpering in Sanskrit, or maybe just coughing in Morse code.**

**Then—**

***BEEP BEEP BEEP BEEP BEEP***

**The *fire alarm explodes to life*.**

**Above the smoke detector, a *red strobe* flashes in rapid rhythm, like a rave for panic.**

**Then?**

***PSHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHT***

**A hiss.**  
 **A thud.**

**And suddenly?**

***THIRTY-EIGHT HIGH-PRESSURE SPRINKLERS ERUPT.***

**The ceiling *vomits cold, institutional water* in all directions.**  
 **Over Gilley.**  
 **Over the burning cardboard.**  
 **Over Sarah’s white blouse.**  
 **Over Wyler’s now-ruined conference folders.**

---

**AUTOMATED VOICE (from intercom):**  
 **"FIRE DETECTED – ZONE A4.**  
 **EVACUATE THE BUILDING.**  
 **EVACUATE THE BUILDING."**

---

****SARAH** (under her breath):**  
 **I *hate being right.***

---

**KATHY (laughing as she wrings out her flannel):**  
 ***Wooo\! Zone A4, baby\!***

***WE DID IT\!***

---

**GILLEY (looking up, arms outstretched):**  
 ***WE’RE CLEANSED IN GLORY.***

---

****WYLER** (yelling into a sopping legal pad):**  
 **I *will fire* every single *sprinkler technician* in *midtown Manhattan.***

---

**JEFF (to Jim, as they shuffle toward the door):**  
 **Did we just get *baptized or expelled?***

---

**CREMEANS (holding the bear spray like a staff):**  
 ***Yes.***

---

**The team pours out into the hallway—*soaked, coughing, chaotic.***

**Secretaries screaming.**  
 **Security scrambling.**  
 **Phones ringing.**  
 **An intern tripping and yelling *“The band did it again\!”***

**Chuck limps out like a war poet.**

---

**Outside, on the sidewalk, the *Island Records fire doors slam shut behind them.***

**Steam rising.**  
 **Alarms echoing down the block.**  
 ***Sirens incoming.***

**Gilley removes his shirt, spins it in victory like it’s a rally flag.**

---

**KATHY (to Sarah, grinning):**  
 **So… do we *still* have a meeting?**

---

****SARAH** (without missing a beat):**  
 **Nah.**

***We just turned in the album notes for our lives.***

---

**INT. MTV NEWSROOM – 1515 BROADWAY – MAY 10, 1992 – 3:44 P.M. EDT**

**Kurt Loder’s office is a mess of manila folders, marked-up scripts, and a steaming mug of espresso strong enough to reboot a cardiac arrest.**

**He’s standing—*not sitting*—reading a typed-up page from a very trusted source at Island Records, half-grinning like a *man who's just been handed poetic justice with a headline.***

---

**KURT (to himself):**  
 **Fire suppression.**

***Bear spray.***

**TV *ripped* off the wall.**

***Standee combustion.***

**Espresso-based *assault and evasion.***

**(*chuckles*)**  
 **And *they charted this week.***

---

**He turns to his producer—a kid named Miles, who’s way too green for what’s coming.**

---

**KURT (snapping fingers):**  
 **You got tape rolling?**

**Because if my source is right?**

**We’re not just *covering* this.**  
 **We’re *immortalizing* it.**

---

**MILES:**  
 **Wait—you're going *on air* with it?**  
 **Even after Standards iced the “Come Inside Me” rollout?**

---

**KURT:**  
 **Exactly.**

**(*waves paper*)**  
 **Because *MTV blinked* at a *perfectly-tuned, stadium-level sexual anthem* and *BBC2 ran it uncut.***

**(*points to the ceiling*)**  
 **And *our audience knows.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **Time to own the *cowardice.***  
 **Time to *acknowledge the carnage.***  
 **And time to *tell one of the greatest goddamn band stories in rock history.***

---

**He leans into the desk, pacing now.**

---

**KURT:**  
 **Not quite *Mud Shark-level Zappa chaos*…**

**(*smirks*)**  
 **…but this?**

**This is *modern.***

**It’s *horny.***

**It’s *flaming logo meets strategic espresso fury.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **It’s *Commuted*. At *\#29.***

**And *burning everything down* on their way to *\#1.***

---

**MILES:**  
 **You’re gonna zing the network *on air*?**

---

**KURT (grinning):**  
 **Oh, not *by name.***

**But let’s just say…**

***“While others passed on the flames, we’re here to fan them.”***

**(*clicks pen*)**  
 **Let’s go make *MTV history* the old-fashioned way—**

**By *pretending we meant to do this all along.***

---

**INT. MTV NEWS STUDIO – LIVE TAPING – MAY 10, 1992 – 6:00 P.M. EDT**

**Kurt Loder sits at the anchor desk, sleeves rolled up, one eyebrow perpetually raised, reading off the teleprompter with a gleam that says *“I’ve waited my whole damn career for this one.”***

**A \*bold chyron flashes across the bottom of the screen:**

**MTV NEWS EXCLUSIVE — COMMITTED CHAOS: COMMUTED SETS FIRE (LITERALLY) TO THE INDUSTRY**

**Behind him, *rotating B-roll* shows:**  
 **• Stock footage of Island Records HQ**  
 **• BBC2 footage of the banned "Come Inside Me" video**  
 **• Still images of Commuted’s “After Hours” hitting \#29**  
 **• And finally: a *smoking conference room photo* quietly leaked from a fire chief’s Polaroid.**

---

**KURT (on air):**  
 **Well, folks—**

**It’s not every day we have to *call the fire department* to verify a story about a *Top 40 band.***

---

**Cue dramatic pause.**

---

**But in the case of *Commuted*?**

**We’ve got *eight sources*—and yes, *one of them* is a *lieutenant from FDNY Ladder 21* who responded to *a triggered fire suppression system at Island Records earlier today.***

**(*eyebrows up*)**  
 **Apparently, the \*\*building’s Zone A4 conference room was engulfed in bear spray, cardboard flame, and a Top 40 band’s *live reaction to getting censored by us.***

**(*pointed beat*)**  
 ***Allegedly.***

---

**Studio cuts to a quick clip of Ladder 21 on the scene, one firefighter saying to camera:**

**“Yeah… conference room was torched. Some intern had chemical burns in his soul. That’s not even in the training manual.”**

---

**Back to Kurt:**

***“Kathy threw an espresso.”***  
 ***“Gilley threw a TV.”***  
 ***“Jeff lit the logo on fire.”***  
 ***“And Cremeans deployed bear repellent like it was Beirut in ’83.”***

**This, by the way, *after* the BBC aired *Come Inside Me*—a video *MTV passed on.***

**(*leans in*)**  
 **And yet?**

**That same week?**

**Commuted debuts at *\#29.***

**(*slow nod*)**  
 **Let that math teach itself.**

---

**KURT (final note, deadpan):**  
 **MTV may not have had the *spine* to air the video.**

**But *we’ve got the cameras ready* if they burn down *another* boardroom.**

**(*smiles*)**  
 **We’ll be right back.**

---

**MTV bumper rolls.**

**The moment is *instant legend.***

**And somewhere in Manhattan?**

***Commuted just became folklore.***

---

**INT. THE BACK ROOM – 102 NORFOLK STREET – LOWER EAST SIDE, NYC – MAY 10, 1992 – 7:02 P.M. EDT**

**The oldest speakeasy in Manhattan is barely lit—velvet couches, vintage lamps, bookshelves hiding real liquor, teacups brimming with gin, and *ghosts of roaring twenties debauchery* in every shadow.**

**This place survived *Prohibition* and somehow *looks less damaged than Island’s conference room.***

---

**At the center of it all?**

***Wyler.***  
 **Pressed shirt. Black tie.**  
 ***Dry. Sober. Calculating.***  
 ***The only one sensibly dressed.***

**He stands beside a table full of mismatched teacups filled with *high-end bourbon* and *whiskey tumblers full of irony.***

---

**The band?**

**Drenched in a cocktail of fire, foam, caffeine residue, and adrenaline.**

**Kathy’s jacket *still faintly smells like pepper spray.***

**Gilley is *holding court in suspenders he didn’t wear this morning.***  
 **No one knows where he got them.**

**Jeff and Jeremy have already *claimed an armchair each* and are trying not to let anyone *see them smiling too hard.***

**Jim’s tapping his fingers on the rim of his cup like it’s a snare.**

**Sarah?**

**Stands with a Manhattan in one hand, *phone off*, *hair damp*, and *high on chaos.***

---

**MTV News plays on the bar’s mounted TV.**  
 **No sound—just captions.**

***“Commuted: Band Sets Fire to Industry Norms—Literally.”***

**Wyler raises his glass.**

---

****WYLER**:**  
 ***You maniacs.***

**You *plotted a coup, executed a media spectacle, destroyed a conference room, and still hit the goddamn Top 40\.***

---

**GILLEY (toasting):**  
 ***To destruction with purpose\!***

---

**KATHY:**  
 ***To espresso warfare\!***

---

**JEFF (softly):**  
 ***To Mom and Dad’s fridge.***

---

**JIM (raising his glass):**  
 ***And to Chuck… who got baptized in bear mace so the legend could live.***

---

****SARAH** (locking eyes with Wyler):**  
 **And to *making cowards flinch.***

**(*a toast*)**  
 ***Because we didn’t.***

---

**They clink.**  
 **The bar crowd watches like *they know they’ll never be in a room like this again.***

**The *smoke has cleared.***  
 ***The city’s listening.***  
 ***And history just bought its second round.***

---

**EXT. NORFOLK STREET – OUTSIDE THE BACK ROOM – MAY 10, 1992 – 7:38 P.M. EDT**

**The Lower East Side air is thick with post-rain steam, exhaust, and old ambition.**  
 **The city hums behind them—*unaware that two people on the sidewalk just declared an armistice neither plans to honor.***

**\**Sarah lights a cigarette with the same poise she used to convince radio stations to spin “Come Inside Me” before noon.***  
 ***Gilley leans against the speakeasy’s brick wall, damp hair falling across his forehead.***  
 ***He’s still wearing the grin of a man who knows he caused property damage and still got a drink paid for by the victim.***

---

****SARAH** (exhaling smoke, voice cool):**  
 **So…**

**Are we still *pretending* we’re not *sleeping together?***

---

**GILLEY (shrugs, eyes twinkling):**  
 ***Yes.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **But only *because I respect the illusion.***

---

**(*he straightens, brushes something off his sleeve that might be soot or victory.*)**

---

**GILLEY (sincere):**  
 **Sorry about the mess, *Ms. Malcom.***

**I… *apologize.***

---

**(*pause*)**

---

***BUT.***

**(*hands go up, no defense—just clarity*)**

**I *was mad.***

**Not at *you.***  
 **At *injustice.***  
 **At *art being told to turn down the volume.***  
 **At *men in ties* who *fold at a little heat.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **At *a goddamn TV screen* that flinched *harder than we ever did.***

---

****SARAH** (smiling faintly):**  
 **You know, for a *horny chaos engine* with no verbal filter?**

**You give *one hell of a mission statement.***

---

**(*she flicks her cigarette to the curb, crushes it under her heel, voice dropping*)**

---

**I’m *amenable* to a *rendezvous.***

**Your hotel.**

**Three minutes.**

**Slip out the back.**

**I’ll grab a cab.**

---

**GILLEY (straightening, voice lower now):**  
 **Do I need to bring *anything*?**

---

****SARAH** (walking away):**  
 **Just *your mouth shut* and *your stamina intact.***

---

**She disappears around the corner.**

**And Gilley?**

**Gilley counts to ten.**

**Then follows, *grinning like a man who’s about to lose sleep and gain a memory.***

---

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – UPPER MANHATTAN – MAY 10, 1992 – 8:12 P.M. EDT**

**The room is *dimly lit by the city’s bleed-through glow.***  
 **Not elegant, not fancy—just *private.***  
 **A *clean bed.***  
 **A *bottle of water half-finished.***  
 **Clothes half-off.**  
 **Shoes in a heap.**

**\*\*Sarah stands at the window in her blouse, now unbuttoned, catching her breath from laughter, or maybe adrenaline, or maybe *the sheer velocity of the last 48 hours.***

**Gilley sits at the edge of the bed, shirtless, tracing the rim of a whiskey glass with one callused finger.**  
 **He looks up at her—not cocky, not flirtatious.**  
 ***Clear.***

---

**GILLEY (quietly):**  
 **You know…**

**(*beat*)**  
 **I think this is gonna be *the last time we have sex* on *Manhattan.***

---

**Sarah turns, raising a brow.**  
 **She doesn’t answer.**  
 **Not yet.**

---

**GILLEY (sincere):**  
 **Because I’m gonna be *recognizable soon.***

**People are *gonna see me.***

**And if *we* get caught together?**  
 **If *anyone* catches a whiff of *this?***

**They’ll *twist* it.**  
 **They’ll *drag you* into *my storm.***

---

**He sets the glass down.**

**No theater in it.**  
 **Just *truth.***

---

****SARAH** (after a pause):**  
 **I *understand* your point now.**

---

**She steps toward the bed.**  
 **Kneels across from him.**  
 **Her hand on his chest.**

---

****SARAH** (low, grounded):**  
 **So *let’s make this one*…**

***memorable.***

**(*leans in*)**  
 ***Undeniably.***  
 ***Unrepeatably.***  
 ***Memorable.***

---

**He leans forward, forehead to hers.**

**Neither of them *smiling.***  
 **Because *it’s not that.***

**This is *the last breath before legacy.***  
 **Before they *aren’t ghosts anymore.***

---

**Their clothes vanish in silence.**

**Their mouths speak *everything their careers won’t allow.***

**And when they move, it’s *not about pleasure.***

**It’s about *burning something into the floorboards.***

---

**So when the story’s told—when someone writes about that *May night before they were household names*—**

**they’ll never guess…**

**That this was *the truest chapter.***

**And *no camera caught it.***

---

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – UPPER MANHATTAN – EARLY MORNING – MAY 11, 1992 – 6:09 A.M. EDT**

**The room is still.**  
 **Dim light peeks through the cracked curtain, outlining the *soft wreckage* of the night.**

**Gilley sleeps on his side, one arm curled where someone else used to be.**

**The *bedsheets are warm, but empty.***

**His breathing slows as consciousness stirs.**

**He reaches—**

***No Sarah.***

**But there is a *note*.**

**Folded.**  
 **Plain hotel stationery.**  
 **Placed carefully on the pillow beside him.**

**He sits up, eyes still puffy with sleep, and reads:**

---

**Don’t speak of this until I say so.**

**You’re beautiful. And dangerous.**

**I needed it.**

**Now I need to be gone.**

**I’ve got a train to catch.**

**Long Island calls.**

**Retreat isn’t surrender—it’s cover.**

**— S\*\***

---

**He stares at it.**

**Blank for a moment.**

**Then he smiles.**  
 ***Wry. Heartbroken. Grateful.***

**He doesn’t crumble the note.**  
 **Doesn’t fold it again.**

**He slides it into his guitar case—beneath the *lyrics to “Tangled Up.”***

**Then lies back.**

**Eyes open.**

**City humming outside.**

**And for once?**

***He doesn’t rush.***

**Because *she’s gone.***  
 **And *he doesn’t have to pretend otherwise.***

**Not yet.**

---

**INT. LIRR TRAIN – EASTBOUND TO LONG ISLAND – MAY 11, 1992 – 7:18 A.M. EDT**

**Sarah sits alone, pressed against the window, hair tied back in a loose knot, sunglasses on even though the train is still cutting through city tunnels.**

**The ring on her left hand catches the early morning light as the train emerges from underground, revealing a streaked blue sky over Queens.**

**Her briefcase is closed.**

**She hasn’t touched it once.**

**Because *she can’t think like a strategist right now.***

**She’s stuck between two lives—*and both are winning.***

---

**In her mind, she sees:**

***Michael.***  
 **Always *calm*.**  
 **Always *brilliant*.**  
 **The *kind of man who controls combustion at a molecular level* and still brings her tea when she’s having a bad day.**

**And he’s *safe.***  
 **He’s *solid.***  
 **He *commands without chaos.***

**She thinks:**

***Michael is the man I could trust with a mortgage.***  
 ***A dog.***  
 ***A child.***  
 ***My real name in a will.***

---

**But then her mind flashes:**

***Gilley.***  
 ***Last night.***  
 ***His hands.***  
 ***His fire.***  
 ***His unpredictability.***

***The band. The fame. The ride. The goddamn thrill.***

---

**Sarah exhales.**

**Too sharp.**

**Her head pulses.**

---

****SARAH** (quietly):**  
 **Jesus, I’m going to *give myself a migraine.***

---

**She presses her temple.**  
 **Sinks deeper into the seat.**

**Outside, the suburbs begin to blur past.**  
 **Lawns. Minivans. Tennis courts. Promise.**

**And inside?**

**She’s a *spy in her own life.***

---

**INT. LONG ISLAND – Michael’S HOUSE – UPSTAIRS BATHROOM – MAY 11, 1992 – 8:42 A.M. EDT**

**Sarah closes the door gently.**  
 **Not softly.**  
 **Just *controlled.***  
 **Like everything she’s ever done when it hurts too much to feel, and she doesn’t want anyone to hear the sound of her unraveling.**

**She turns the lock.**

***Clicks it with precision.***

**The mirror is too clean.**  
 **The light too honest.**

**Her reflection?**

***Not helping.***

---

**She sits on the closed toilet seat.**  
 **Still in the blouse she left Gilley’s hotel room in.**  
 **Same bra.**

**The white one.**

**The *deliberate one.***  
 **The *warning flag she raised before the bomb dropped.***

**Her face goes still.**

**Then—**

***The tears come.***

**No noise.**

**Just water.**

**Like the *fire suppression system* that doused the chaos hours ago.**

**Silent.**  
 **Necessary.**  
 **Too late.**

---

**She lets it all out.**

**Five minutes.**  
 **Not more.**

**Because *five minutes is all she’ll allow.***

**Not for guilt.**

**But for the *ache* of *knowing*.**

**Knowing that *if this was France*?**

**No one would *bat an eye.***

**If she was *a woman in Paris* with a fiancé and a lover?**

**She’d be *normal.***

**She’d be *free.***

---

**But this is *Long Island.***

**And *America.***

**And the *early '90s.***

**And *it’s not fair.***

---

****SARAH** (whispers):**  
 **So *he* gets to *fuck* his way across a tour map—**

**And *I* have to *cry in a bathroom*?**

**Because *I* have the *good man?***

**Because *I’m the woman?***

**That’s—**

**(*wipes her eyes, furious now*)**

**That’s *crap.***

---

**She stands.**  
 **Straightens her shoulders.**

**Wipes off the mascara streaks.**

**Reapplies *deep plum lipstick.***

**Stares at her reflection again—this time *not flinching.***

---

****SARAH** (softly, like a vow):**  
 **Are *women* allowed to do the same things *men* do?**

**(*beat*)**  
 **Doesn’t *seem* like it.**

**(*long pause*)**

**But *maybe it’s time we stop asking.***

---

**She unlocks the door.**

**And steps back into the *perfect house.***

**To the *perfect man.***

**With the *perfect mask* on.**

**And *fire* still smoldering behind her eyes.**

---

**INT. LONG ISLAND – Michael’S HOUSE – KITCHEN – MAY 11, 1992 – 8:57 A.M. EDT**

**The *ceramic tile is warm from the morning sun.***  
 **The *kettle whistles softly.***  
 **The *coffee smells like domestic tranquility and compromise.***

**Sarah walks in.**

**Calm.**  
 **Composed.**  
 ***Mask sealed like lacquer.***

**Michael’s at the counter in his robe, pouring two mugs.**  
 **Turns, smiles.**

---

**Michael:**  
 **Morning, beautiful.**

**(*offers her the mug she always takes—the one with the faded bluebirds*)**

---

****SARAH** (accepting it smoothly):**  
 **Thanks.**

---

**She sips.**  
 **Smiles.**

**And inside?**

**She’s *sifting through fire and algebra.***

---

**Because *she’s decided.***

**She can *have her cake.***

**And *eat it too.***

**It’s just going to take:**

* ***Incredible discipline.***

* ***A low profile.***

* **And *Gilley* understanding *the stakes.***

---

**Because *if* she can pull it off?**

**If *she* can maintain *this sub-layered arrangement* with *clarity, professionalism, and boundaries*?**

**This isn’t scandal.**

**This is *strategy.***

**This is *power-sharing.***

**This is *brand-building.***

---

**All she has to do is *treat him with generosity and respect.***

**Like she *already is.***

**Or…**

**Is she?**

---

**She blinks.**

**Because *maybe* it’s *not generous* to keep sleeping with someone *under contract.***

**Maybe it’s *dangerous.***

**Maybe it’s *exploitative.***

**Or *mutual.***

**Or *inspired.***

**Or *illegal.***

---

****SARAH** (in her head):**  
 **Maybe I should *consult a lawyer.***

---

**Then—**

**She clenches her jaw.**

**Pain *spikes behind her eyes.***

**She grips the mug a little too hard.**

---

****SARAH** (muttering):**  
 **Oh god.**

**I’m *really* going to give myself a *migraine.***

---

**Michael (from across the counter):**  
 **What was that?**

---

****SARAH** (snaps out of it, smiling instantly):**  
 **Just… *caffeine hitting wrong.***

**(*cheerfully*)**  
 **Could you pass the honey?**

---

**Michael (smiling):**  
 **Anything for you.**

---

**She stirs her tea.**  
 **Calm.**  
 **Precise.**

**And wonders *how far she can bend this world before it breaks.***

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – LEGAL DEPARTMENT – PRIVATE LINE – MAY 11, 1992 – 2:13 P.M. EDT**

**Sarah sits in a quiet corner of the Island satellite office on Long Island, tucked behind a filing cabinet, voice low, tone measured.**

**She’s got a notepad in front of her with only one thing written on it:**

***Dual roles – personal entanglements – contractual exposure?***

**She’s on hold.**  
 **Light jazz playing.**

**Then—**

**CLICK.**

---

**LEGAL COUNSEL (male, neutral tone):**  
 **Island Records Legal Affairs, this is Evan.**  
 **How can I assist?**

---

****SARAH** (even, diplomatic):**  
 **Hi Evan, this is Sarah Malcom.**

**I have a *hypothetical scenario* involving *personal proximity and contractual oversight.***

---

**EVAN:**  
 **Go on.**

---

****SARAH**:**  
 **Let’s say someone on *Commuted’s account team* has *entered a personal relationship* with a *band member.***

**Not officially disclosed.**

**Not public.**

**Not interfering with duties.**

**But… there.**

**Would this present *a conflict of interest* under current company policy?**

---

**EVAN (pause):**  
 **That would be…**

**(*clears throat*)**  
 **A *Chris Blackwell matter.***

---

****SARAH** (raising her eyebrows):**  
 **That high?**

---

**EVAN (flat):**  
 **That *personal.***

---

****SARAH** (tightly):**  
 **So if someone wanted *clarity* or *guidance* on this?**

**You’re suggesting they *take it up with the founder of the company?***

---

**EVAN (carefully):**  
 **That would be the *most appropriate channel.***

---

****SARAH** (sharply):**  
 **Do *you* know the answer?**

---

**EVAN (after a beat):**  
 ***No comment.***

**(*pause*)**  
 **Have a nice day, Ms. Malcom.**

**CLICK.**

---

**Sarah slowly puts down the receiver.**

**Stares at it.**

**And grits her teeth.**

**Because now?**

**It’s *not just about morality.***

**It’s *politics.***

***Power.***

**And *visibility.***

---

**And she’s no longer worried about *crossing a line.***

**She’s worried about *who’s watching her color outside the margins.***

---
**INT. SARAH’S PERSONAL JOURNAL – HANDWRITTEN ENTRY – MAY 11, 1992 – 3:47 P.M. EDT**

Her pen scratches slowly across the page.  The header is clean. Firm. Unmistakable: 
**BLACKWELL CONVERSATIONS – NEVER CASUAL**

Below it:  Shit just got real.

I asked Legal a question I didn’t think would raise alarms.  I thought I’d get a paragraph.  Instead, I got *Blackwell.

She presses the pen harder now.

He doesn’t run the show anymore.   Not *technically.*   The PolyGram sellout pulled some of the teeth out of the lion.  But he's still here. Every day.  Every meeting that matters. He doesn’t swing the gavel—but people still look at his hands when it falls.

She pauses. Breathes. Writes faster.

If I speak to him about this…It’s not legal. It’s not ethical.  It’s *chess.*** And he already knows every move.  This man built a label on chaos and intuition.  He signed Bob Marley. He can smell a lie through two walls and a scarf.  And he knows where every body is buried. He *buried half of them.*

The ink trails off for a moment.

Then: What do I want? Do I want his blessing? Or do I want his silence?

She underlines the next line twice:  I can’t let him see me sweat.

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – EXECUTIVE SUITE – CHRIS BLACKWELL’S OFFICE – MAY 11, 1992 – 4:11 P.M. EDT**

Chris Blackwell stands by his window, hands clasped behind his back, watching the city like it owes him an explanation. His office smells like paper, patience, and leather. It’s lined with gold records and *trophies of past revolutions.*** He’s been expecting this conversation. Not just for two days. But for eighteen months.

**NICK STEWART’S** offhand remark still echoes: “Saw her coming out of Gilley’s room at the hotel in Chicago. Northwestern show. Her blouse was backwards. They were laughing like kids who knew the world was about to call.”

Blackwell didn’t say a word at the time.  Just nodded.  Filed it away.  Because Sarah Malcom was always headed here. And sooner or later? She’d need to answer something he already knew the answer to.

**He turns to his assistant.**

**BLACKWELL (quiet, deliberate):**  
Summon Ms. Malcom.

(*beat*)
 The assistant nods and picks up the phone.  Blackwell walks back to his desk.  Sits. Crosses his legs. Opens the folder marked simply:**“Malcom”**

Inside?  Clippings. Tour receipts. A BBC2 transcript.  A fax from Wyler. And a grainy photo of Sarah standing outside a venue, Gilley’s hand on her back.

**BLACKWELL (to himself, softly):**  
Let’s see if she’s ready to be powerful.  Or *just another story.***

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – 9TH FLOOR EXECUTIVE SUITE – MAY 11, 1992 – 4:19 P.M. EDT**

**The hallway is *too quiet.***  The carpets are too thick.  The lighting is *moodier* than anything Sarah’s ever authorized on a promo shoot.  She walks behind the assistant, clipboard clutched tight to her chest even though she knows she doesn’t need it* here.

This part of the building?  She figured it would be a decade or more before she’d earn this hallway.  Ten, maybe twelve years.  After three promotions. After a Grammy win or a trade feature or a New Yorker profile with her name in full serif.  But now?  Now she’s being summoned.  And not to *pitch*.  To *explain*.

The artwork gets nicer the closer she gets. More gold leaf. More Bob Marley originals. A signed Compass Point photo she once printed off the internet and pinned over her desk during grad school.  And it *scares the fuck out of her.*  Because this hallway isn’t a pipeline.  It’s a threshold.

**ASSISTANT (stopping):**  
Here we are.

(nods toward the door)

He’s expecting you.

Sarah nods.  Doesn’t speak.  She watches the assistant leave.  Then she stands there, alone, in front of the dark walnut double doors with a single brushed gold plaque:

**CHRISTOPHER BLACKWELL**

She swallows.  Then knocks.

---

**INT. BLACKWELL’S OFFICE – ISLAND RECORDS – MAY 11, 1992 – 4:20 P.M. EDT**

The walnut doors swing open.  Chris Blackwell doesn’t stand.  He sits behind a massive desk of African hardwood, half-hidden in the shadow of towering windows and the weight of empire.

No music plays.  No assistants linger.  Just him, crisp in a black button-down, a pair of round glasses perched low on his nose, one hand resting atop a manila folder.  He looks at her once. Eyes like warm water poured over razors.

**And he says, simply—**

**BLACKWELL:**
Close the door behind you.

Sarah obeys.  CRUMP. She stands just inside. Not quite frozen, but too aware of her own body. Of how her breath sounds in the silence.  Of how every inch of this room was built for power.

**BLACKWELL (still calm):**  
You didn’t expect to be here this soon.

**(*beat*)**  
But let’s not waste time pretending you weren’t on your way.

---

He gestures to the chair across from him.  She walks forward and sits. No notes. No planner. No performance. Just Sarah Malcom. Brilliant.  Exhausted. Exposed. And *ready*. She hopes.

---

**INT. BLACKWELL’S OFFICE – ISLAND RECORDS – MAY 11, 1992 – 4:22 P.M. EDT**

Blackwell doesn’t make a show of it.   Doesn’t lean forward.   Doesn’t frown.  He simply opens the folder.  It’s labeled in all caps: *MALCOM*.

Inside:
* Printouts of *BBC syndication data.
* Press clippings—*NME, MTV News, internal memos.*
* A fax from Wyler marked URGENT.
* A grainy still of *Sarah and Gilley in Chicago, 1991*.
* And, on the top, a *short typed memo from Nick Stewart.

He skims it once.  Then looks up at her. His eyes are glacier calm.

**BLACKWELL (quiet, firm):**  
I expect my *line managers* to tell me the *truth.

(*beat*)
 So *start.*

Sarah doesn’t blink.  But inside?  Her pulse thunders.  Line managers?  Come again?  She just got three promotions in a sentence, without the HR paperwork or the parade.  
Her next paycheck will have zeroes she’s only seen on executive forecasts. This isn’t her boss Wyler.  This isn’t a radio station. This is *Chris Blackwell.* And the next sentence might define the rest of her career.

---

**INT. BLACKWELL’S OFFICE – ISLAND RECORDS – MAY 11, 1992 – 4:24 P.M. EDT**

Sarah holds her breath for a beat, staring at the man who discovered legends and still walks like he invented trust and betrayal in equal measure.  She folds her hands in her lap.  Looks him directly in the eye. And chooses *neither fear nor denial.*


**SARAH (quiet, even):**  
Do you want the *truth*…Or the *explanation*?

Blackwell says nothing.  Which means *explanation it is.* She leans forward, voice steady—not acting. Just unburdening.

**SARAH**
 The explanation’s simple. I’m spying on the band.  I’m having a sexual affair with a member of Commuted. And yes—*it’s thrilling.* It’s *fun.
