It’s *rewarding.* It’s dangerous.* It’s stupid.* It’s *rock and roll.* But most of all?  It’s *informational.* I know *everything.* What they’re *feeling.*  What they’re *thinking.* *Where they’re scared.* Where they’re *lying.*
 Where they’re *not* lying.

**(*exhale*)**  
I know what they’ll do before they do it. Because I’m in their bed, their van, their nerves.

She pauses. Not breaking eye contact. 

**SARAH**:
So yes. I’m spying on the band. But I’m *doing it for us. For *Island.* For *you.*

Blackwell closes the folder.  Very slowly.  His face unreadable. But *he doesn’t look away.***

---

**INT. BLACKWELL’S OFFICE – ISLAND RECORDS – MAY 11, 1992 – 4:26 P.M. EDT**

The silence after Sarah’s confession could fill a blocked off subway tunnel. Blackwell closes the folder with a gentle *thump*. Then sits back. Calm. Controlled. Like *someone who’s already finished the novel* but enjoys watching others struggle through the plot. He lifts his eyes to her.  And finally speaks.

**BLACKWELL (measured, almost amused):**  
Sarah…I’ve *known for seventeen months.*

Sarah flinches—just slightly.

**BLACKWELL:**  
I knew before we signed them.  Before *Wyler* even drew up the budget. Before *Ric Ocasek’s* plane ticket was booked.

(*leans in, voice harder now*)
Nick Stewart told me.  Chicago. Northwestern’s Fall Festival.

**(*tilts head*)**  
Said you came out of Gilley’s hotel room with your blouse inside-out and the look of a woman who knew a revolution was under her skin.

He lets that hang in the air.  Then:

**BLACKWELL:**  
So now—Tell me something I don’t know. Because Nick only gave me so much.  And if you’re going to *report to me*—Not Wyler. Not PR. ***Me.*** Then you’re going to tell me *the truth.***  The whole truth. ***Nothing but the truth.***

He leans back again. Eyes cold. Voice like a blade.

**BLACKWELL:**  
And if I *ask* for your *soiled panties* in the *mail*?  You FedEx them straight off your ass.

(long pause)
 **Do you *understand* how *short a leash* you’re on?**

The silence that follows isn’t from fear.  It’s from *clarity.*  He has *all the cards.* But *she’s still at the table.*

---

**INT. BLACKWELL’S OFFICE – ISLAND RECORDS – MAY 11, 1992 – 4:28 P.M. EDT**

**The room is still, heavy with the weight of truth in transit.**

**Blackwell leans back, arms folded.**  
 **He’s invited the storm, and he’s *ready to listen like a god absorbing prophecy.***


**BLACKWELL:**  
 **Tell me *something I don’t know.***

---

**Sarah doesn’t blink.**  
 **Doesn’t posture.**

**She just thinks—*for one second.***

**And then begins.**

---

****SARAH** (measured, clinical):**  
 **How about this?**

**Gilley isn’t the *slacker* we thought he was.**

**He plays it cool, loose, *horny frontman swagger*—**  
 **But *he works*.**

**He’s *tactile* with the crowd.**  
 **He *reads rooms* like a touring magician.**  
 **And *he rewrites lyrics in his head when no one’s looking.***

---

**(*beat*)**

---

***He bears watching.***

**Not because he’s *lazy.***

**Because he’s *evolving.***

---

**BLACKWELL (nods slowly):**  
 **Go on.**

---

****SARAH**:**  
 **Jeff is *trying to get back in Kathy’s pants.***

**Kathy is *trying to get back in Jeff’s pants.***

**They *won’t admit it.***

**They *won’t act on it.***

**They *just circle* each other like *two dogs too proud to hump in public.***

---

**(*Blackwell chuckles once. Not warm.*)**

---

****SARAH**:**  
 **Jeremy?**

**Jeremy’s going to *blow up.***  
 **Eventually.**  
 **Because *Jeff’s on his back* all the time, and *he can’t handle it.***

**He’s *brilliant.***  
 **Absolutely.**  
 **But it’s *tiring*.**

**You have to *stroke his ego* like it’s an exotic pet or it starts *clawing furniture.***

---

**(*pauses, then shrugs*)**  
 **And Bill?**

**Bill *might be on mushrooms.***

**Can’t prove it.**  
 **But *if he starts speaking French backwards* during a breakdown, *I’ll call it confirmed.***

---

**Blackwell doesn’t say a word.**

**Just raises an eyebrow.**

---

**BLACKWELL (dry):**  
 **Is that all?**

---

****SARAH** (smiling now, just a little):**  
 ***Not exactly.***

---

**INT. BLACKWELL’S OFFICE – ISLAND RECORDS – MAY 11, 1992 – 4:31 P.M. EDT**

**Blackwell tilts his head ever so slightly.**

**Sarah hasn’t broken eye contact.**

**She isn’t bluffing.**

**She isn’t scared anymore.**

**She’s *reporting.***

---

****SARAH** (calm, direct):**  
 ***Cremeans* is the *real wild card.***

**But not in the way you’d expect.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **He’s *a Southern Baptist.***

***A real one.***

**And that *means something.***

---

**(*leans forward, voice low but clear*)**

---

**We *don’t understand religious men* here, Chris.**  
 **Not in *this city.***

**We think *they’re hayseeds.***  
 ***Punchlines.***  
 ***Hollow men hiding behind leather Bibles and bad country music.***

**But *he’s not a hillbilly.***

**He’s *dangerous* in *the quietest* way.**

---

**You know he *brought bear spray* to the Island meeting?**

**You know *why*?**

---

**(*pause*)**  
 **Because he *couldn’t get a concealed carry permit* in New York.**

**If this had been *Dallas?***  
 ***Atlanta?***  
 ***Dayton?***

**He wouldn’t have packed *pepper.***

**He’d have packed *a .45.***

---

**Blackwell’s fingers twitch, just once, against the armrest.**

---

****SARAH** (pointed):**  
 **They *worship him.***  
 ***All of them.***

**Even *Kathy.***

**He doesn’t manage them.**

**He *shapes* them.**

**He’s *not a label man.***  
 **He’s a *faithkeeper.***  
 **A *guardian.***

**You *try to go over his head?***  
 **He *takes you to court.***

**You *try to outmaneuver him?***

**He *castrates you.***

**(*pause*)**  
 ***Politely.***

---

**(*smiles, just a flicker of dark humor*)**  
 **And *your mother brings the hedge clippers.***

---

**BLACKWELL (finally speaking, almost a whisper):**  
 **That’s a *hell of a warning.***

---

****SARAH**:**  
 **It’s *not a warning.***

**It’s *an alert.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **You *don’t control Commuted.***

**Cremeans does.**

---

**Blackwell sits back, tapping one finger against his knee.**

***Silent. Processing. Calculating.***

---

**INT. BLACKWELL’S OFFICE – ISLAND RECORDS – MAY 11, 1992 – 4:35 P.M. EDT**

Blackwell slowly leans forward again, folding his hands over the *now-closed “MALCOM” folder* like he’s sealing a tomb. His voice drops—quiet, lethal, unmistakable authority.

**BLACKWELL:**  
I want *handwritten summaries.* Once a *month.* Do you understand me, Sarah? You were never here. This conversation? Never happened. There will be no phone calls.
 There will be no voicemails.  This is *Burn After Reading level shit.*

Sarah nods. Once. She doesn’t write that down. Because *she knows.*  This part lives *only in memory.*

**BLACKWELL (tapping the folder):**  
Give us a *competitive advantage.* Because *according to my handy little fact sheet here*? Their sales? Are *going through the roof.*

He finally cracks the faintest smile. Like an emperor who just bought shares in a volcano.

**BLACKWELL (rising slightly):**  
Oh… and Sarah? One last favor.  When you see the *people at MTV*? 
(*grins*)

Tell them *Bono sent you.*

Sarah stands.  Eyes locked with his. And for the first time since she entered the building—She *feels taller than the room.*

She turns to leave. Not shaken. Not unsure. Just *activated.*

**FADE TO BLACK.**

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – 6TH FLOOR – WOMEN’S RESTROOM – MAY 11, 1992 – 4:42 P.M. EDT**

The door swings shut behind her with a hollow thud.  No one else is inside.  Fluorescent lights hum above. The tile floor gleams too clean. The mirrors are indifferent.

Sarah walks straight past them.  Shoulders square. Heels clicking. She doesn’t pause.  Doesn’t check her reflection. She finds the *furthest stall*—the one no one likes because the lock sticks a little—and pushes the door in with the palm of her hand.

She drops to her knees. Skirt bunched under her. Fingernails pressed to cold porcelain

**And *she vomits.***

Not dainty. Not controlled. Not quiet. It’s *violent.* From the *gut.***  From somewhere buried between ambition and guilt.  She grips the edge of the toilet like a lifeline.  Like she can hold on to something solid while her body betrays her.

A minute passes. Then another. She stays there. Breathing. Eyes closed. Kneeling like a supplicant.  Or a whore. And somewhere between the nausea and the clarity…She knows:  She just crossed a threshold she can never walk back through.

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – 6TH FLOOR – WOMEN’S RESTROOM – MAY 11, 1992 – 4:49 P.M. EDT**

Sarah steadies herself. One hand on the *stall wall*. The other gripping the *edge of the bowl* like it’s a railing on a cliff.  Her breathing slows. She wipes her mouth with the back of her wrist.

Then—she stands. Not gracefully.  Not theatrically. But *deliberately.*

---

**INT. RESTROOM – SINK AREA – MOMENTS LATER**

The mirror waits for her.  She steps forward. Looks herself dead in the eye. No makeup touch-ups yet. No distractions. Just *Sarah.* Raw. Blotchy.  And *utterly real.*


**SARAH (to herself, firm, low):**  
 I *swear to God…* I’ll *never* do that again.

She turns on the tap.  Washes her hands.  Her face. ***Slow.***   ***Precise.***  Like she’s preparing for surgery.  Not to hide the mess. But to reset the mission.

**SARAH (quietly):**  
 I’m *never* going to let *fear* rule my life.

(beat)
Ever. Again.

She pats her face dry. Reaches into her purse. Pulls out the *plum lipstick*—her *armor.***
Applies it with the *exact same control* she used the night she aced her Columbia thesis defense. No tremble. No smudge. It’s a *weapon.* She caps it. Tucks it away.  And looks at herself again.

Not perfect. But *dangerous. Informed. Awake.*

She nods to her reflection. Then turns. And walks out.

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – ELEVATOR – DESCENDING TO 6TH FLOOR – MAY 11, 1992 – 5:02 P.M. EDT**

Sarah stands at the back of the elevator, arms folded, shoulders relaxed, expression carved from marble and resolve. She’s just reapplied her lipstick.  No one would know what happened ten minutes ago unless they’d *heard the retching.

The elevator *dings* at the 7th floor. Wyler steps in. Still damp from the earlier *sprinkler incident*.  Suit jacket long abandoned. He’s holding an iced coffee like it’s the last weapon he has left. He gives her a look—*half impressed, half concerned,* all Wyler.

**WYLER (quietly, pressing the button):** 
 So.  I’ve been reliably told…There's been a *restructure.

Sarah doesn’t move. Doesn’t flinch. Just waits. 

**WYLER**:
 You *no longer report to me. You and I now have a *dotted line.* Performance reviews. Feedback. That’s *me.* But *your boss?* 

**(*beat*)**

Is now *Chris Blackwell.*

Sarah nods once.  Nothing flashy.  Just *confirmation received.*

**WYLER (a faint laugh):**  
Congratulations.  

(beat)
Did you ever expect to make it this *quick?*

**SARAH (without blinking):**  
No.  But now that I’m *here*?  I’m *not leaving.*

**WYLER (grinning, sipping):**  
Good.  Because you’ve officially joined the last circle.  And trust me? There’s *no map* out of it.

The elevator dings.  Doors open. Sarah walks out first. Not faster.  Just with *purpose.***
Wyler watches her go.  Shakes his head.

**WYLER (to himself):**  
Hell of a storm you brought, Malcom. **Hell of a storm.**

---

**INT. SARAH’S APARTMENT – LONG ISLAND – THAT NIGHT – MAY 11, 1992 – 9:47 P.M. EDT**

The windows are cracked. The spring air is cool and smells like clean laundry and quiet guilt. Sarah sits on the edge of her bed, barefoot, hair down, a glass of wine untouched on the nightstand. Her cordless phone *buzzes*.  She checks the number. Gilley. She takes a deep breath. Answers it.

**SARAH (casual, controlled):**
 Hey.

**GILLEY (somewhere loud, maybe a bar, maybe just Gilley):**  
Hey yourself.  So.  Anything… happen today?

There’s a *pause.*  Sarah *smiles.*  Not fondly.  Not coy.  But like a woman holding a razor behind her teeth.


**SARAH (calmly):** 
*Yes.

**GILLEY (perking up):**  
Oh?

**SARAH (firm):**
But you don’t *find out* until *Nashville.***  So I suggest you *hydrate.

**GILLEY (laughs):**  
That sounds *ominous.*

**SARAH (smirking now):**  
 It’s earned.

**GILLEY:**  
You scare me sometimes.

**SARAH**:
 Good. Then we’re *even.*

She hangs up first. No goodbye. Just *silence* on the other end. She sets the phone down. Finally takes a sip of the wine. And smiles into the dark. Because *power* tastes better when no one sees you pour it.

---

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – NASHVILLE – NIGHT – MAY 11, 1992 – 10:01 P.M. CDT**

Gilley sits on the edge of his bed, phone still in hand, staring at the dial tone like it’s trying to explain itself.  He blinks once. Then sets the phone down. Slowly. Turns his head toward the open suite door, where Bill is cross-legged on the carpet, headphones on, noodling with a synth patch that sounds like koi arguing in a fish pond.

Gilley doesn’t say anything for a second. Then:

**GILLEY (deadpan):**
So…I’m *definitely in trouble.

**Bill (pulling off one earcup, blinking like a castrated dog):**  
Did you call her?

**GILLEY:**  
She *confirmed* something happened. Then told me *I don’t get to know* what it is…
Until Nashville.

(glances around)
 Which is *here.*

**BILL:**  
So you’re *on the clock.*

**GILLEY:**  
Apparently.

(leans back, stares at the ceiling)
I’m scared. *Turned on.* And *curious* in a way that’s *spiritually threatening.*

Bill nods like that’s a perfectly reasonable diagnosis.  Then casually lifts a bottle of something unlabeled from beside him.

**BILL:**  
Life’s good, man. Whatcha drinkin’?

**Gilley (without missing a beat):**  
Regret.  On the rocks. With a twist of *God, what did she do?***

They both laugh.  Bill pours a second glass.  And outside? The *neon flickers.*The *venue marquee hums.* And *Sarah Malcom’s presence* hasn’t even entered the building.  But *it’s already rearranging the air.*

---

**INT. HOTEL BREAKFAST ROOM – NASHVILLE – MAY 12, 1992 – 8:04 A.M. CDT**

**The room is too quiet for a group of people this famous and this recently chaotic.**

**There’s a *single waffle iron* wheezing near the coffee station.**  
 **The *TV is on mute.***  
 **Local news. Weather. *No music.***

**The band is gathered, some nursing coffee, some pretending to read, all vaguely anxious like animals who sense a change in barometric pressure.**

**Sarah hasn’t arrived yet.**

**But *everyone knows she’s in town.***

**Which is somehow *worse.***

---

**Jeremy’s flipping through a local alt-weekly, but he hasn’t turned a page in ten minutes.**

**Kathy’s stirring yogurt like she’s trying to solve it.**

**Jeff’s got a legal pad out and hasn’t written a word.**

**Gilley hasn’t touched his eggs. That’s a crisis.**

**And then—**

**Cremeans appears, tray in hand, sitting down like *absolutely nothing* is wrong.**

**He has a paper cup filled to the brim with *Mountain Dew*.**

**And a plate of *perfectly folded deli ham slices.***

---

**CREMEANS (pleasantly):**  
 **Just so y’all know—**

***Mountain Dew*** **goes *real well* with *sliced ham.***

---

**Everyone stares.**

**Kathy blinks.**

**Jeff murmurs, “Is that a warning?”**

**Gilley looks at the door like he’s bracing for an ex-girlfriend and an IRS audit to arrive at the same time.**

---

**CREMEANS (cheerfully, sipping):**  
 **I’m just saying…**

**If *Sarah’s got something nuclear* in that little planner of hers?**

**Best to *start your morning properly.***

**Sweet *meets* salt.**

**Acid *cuts* tension.**

**Breakfast *is* strategy.**

---

**JIM (deadpan):**  
 **Did he just militarize a Waffle House?**

---

**CREMEANS:**  
 ***Son, I am the Waffle House.***

---

**The room cracks—nervous laughter, eyes darting to the door.**

**Because *she’s coming.***

**And they can *feel it.***

**And nobody—not even Cremeans— knows *exactly what she’s bringing.***

**But *it tastes like ham and citrus and judgment.***

---

**INT. HOTEL BREAKFAST ROOM – NASHVILLE – MAY 12, 1992 – 8:06 A.M. CDT**

**The door swings open.**

**No announcement.**  
 **No fanfare.**  
 **No musical cue.**

**Just *heels on laminate tile.***  
 **The *quiet hush* of a woman who knows exactly how much air she pulls from the room when she walks in.**

**Sarah Malcom enters.**

**Hair tied back.**  
 **White blouse, again—but this one has a sharper collar.**  
 **Clipboard in one hand.**  
 **No coffee. No need.**

**She scans the room once.**

**Takes in everything.**

**The way Gilley straightens like a kid in church.**  
 **The way Kathy sits up but doesn’t make eye contact.**  
 **Cremeans? Sips his Mountain Dew like it’s a sacrament.**

**Sarah walks to the table.**  
 **Stops.**

**Then:**

---

****SARAH** (clear, sharp):**  
 **Good morning.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **Let’s *discuss performance metrics.***

---

**KATHY (under her breath):**  
 **Oh, fuck me.**

---

****SARAH**:**  
 **I’ve got a few *ideas.***

---

**She sets the clipboard down on the table.**

**No one dares touch it.**

**Not yet.**

**She doesn’t sit.**

**She owns the room *from a standing position.***

---

****SARAH** (firm, unfazed):**  
 **Our single is sitting *at number twenty-nine*.**  
 **You’ve *breached the walls.***  
 **Which means the enemy *knows your name.***

**They’re *watching.***

***Measuring.***

**And *waiting for you to trip over your own myth.***

---

**JEFF (murmuring to Jeremy):**  
 **Why does this feel like we’re about to be drafted?**

---

****SARAH**:**  
 **So here’s what happens next.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **We *go silent for thirty-six hours.***  
 ***No interviews.***  
 ***No unscheduled bar appearances.***  
 **We *control the narrative.***

**I’ll handle MTV.**

**Blackwell’s backing the line.**

**And you?**  
 **You’re going to *rehearse.***  
 ***Refine.***  
 ***Reshape.***

**Because *the moment you hit Top 20,* it’s *not a band anymore.***

**It’s *a movement.***

---

**GILLEY (raising a hand, sheepishly):**  
 **Uh… does *anyone* get to ask *what happened* in New York?**

---

****SARAH** (without missing a beat):**  
 **Yes.**

**In *Nashville.***

**(*smiles*)**  
 ***Starting now.***

---

**She sits.**

***Perfectly.***

**And flips the clipboard open.**

***Everything is in motion.***

---

**INT. HOTEL BREAKFAST ROOM – NASHVILLE – MAY 12, 1992 – 8:09 A.M. CDT**

**A hush settles as Sarah flips through her notes.**

**The table is quiet—not because they’re scared, but because *they know she’s already five moves ahead* and *they’re playing catch-up.***

**Jeremy, still blinking sleep out of his eyes, lifts his coffee and asks:**

---

**JEREMY (genuine, confused):**  
 **Why are we going… *undercover?***  
 **Or *incognito?***  
 **Or… *silent?***  
 **I guess?**

**What’s with the *thirty-six-hour ghost routine?***

---

**Sarah smiles.**

**Not *condescending.***

***Excited.***

**She’s been *waiting* for that question.**

---

****SARAH** (sitting forward):**  
 **Because we’re going to make *MTV squirm.***

**And we’re going to let the *British Broadcasting Corporation* *torture* the *people over at Paramount*.**

---

**Everyone’s eyes flick toward her now.**

**Even Cremeans tilts his chin, paying attention.**

---

****SARAH**:**  
 ***The video*—**

**(*beat, nods slowly*)**

***That video*****…**

***Oh my god, I love that video.***

---

**(“Come Inside Me.”)**

---

**It’s *dangerous.***  
 **It’s *perfect.***  
 **And it’s *airing at midnight across Europe* while *MTV’s hiding under their desk pretending they lost the tape.***

**So?**

**Let’s *starve the U.S. media.***

**Let’s *give them silence.***

**And let them *choke* on *foreign press.***

---

**KATHY (quietly):**  
 **You want to *go dark* so they *crave us.***

---

****SARAH** (nodding):**  
 **Exactly.**

**No quotes.**  
 **No appearances.**

**Just *BBC ratings, rising.***  
 ***NME headlines.***  
 ***Kurt Loder fidgeting in his seat.***

**And MTV?**

**They’ll have *no choice* but to play it \*\*\*or look like they got beat by the *goddamn Queen’s Channel.***

---

**GILLEY (grinning):**  
 **Oh, *I love this.***

---

**JEFF (dry):**  
 **It’s *media edging.***

---

****SARAH** (pointing at Jeff):**  
 ***Yes.***

**That’s *exactly* what it is.**

---

**CREMEANS (quietly, almost proud):**  
 **Now *she gets it.***

---

**And with that, the plan is *in motion.***

**The *air* in the room sharpens.**  
 **The *band* refocuses.**

**And *Sarah Malcom*?**

**Just drew the first *perfect silence* on the world’s loudest stage.**

---

**INT. HOTEL BREAKFAST ROOM – NASHVILLE – MAY 12, 1992 – 8:12 A.M. CDT**

**A moment of silence lingers after Sarah drops her final sentence—strategic silence as weaponized seduction.**

**Jeff, ever the tactician of *practical details and emotional temperature checks*, leans back in his chair and glances toward Cremeans, whose plate is now empty except for the last curl of deli ham.**

---

**JEFF (raising an eyebrow):**  
 **So… does this mean we get a *day off*?**

---

**Cremeans sets down his plastic fork like it’s a gavel.**

**He wipes his hands on a napkin, looks at the band with that *half-uncle, half-sergeant* expression he’s perfected.**

**Then cracks a wide, *unexpectedly wholesome* grin.**

---

**CREMEANS (brightly):**  
 ***Yes\!***

---

**Half the table exhales.**

**Gilley cheers under his breath.**

**Kathy leans back like she’s just been handed a pack of Marlboros and a bathtub full of bourbon.**

**Jeremy slaps the table and mutters, “God bless America.”**

---

**CREMEANS (raising a finger):**  
 **But—**

**(*and here comes the Southern Baptist disclaimer*)**

***Don’t be stupid.***

**Stay *within three miles* of the hotel.**  
 **No *strip clubs.***  
 **No *press.***  
 **No *hospital visits.***

**I don’t want *Sarah* chasing *anyone* through downtown in *heels* because *you* decided to *start a bar fight over music trivia.***

---

**GILLEY (mock offense):**  
 **That happened *once.***

---

****SARAH** (dry):**  
 **That happened *twice.***

---

**JEFF:**  
 **So… *day off, but stay ghost.***

---

**CREMEANS (nodding):**  
 ***Exactly.***

**Ghosts with *hydration.***  
 **Ghosts with *honor.***

---

**And just like that?**

***The machine slows.***

**Just for a moment.**

***The eye of the hurricane.***

**Before the next wave.**

---

**INT. NASHVILLE GUN RANGE – MAY 12, 1992 – 11:17 A.M. CDT – SCENE 1**

**Jeremy, *protective glasses on, ear protection snug*, shoulders the *M16 like he was born to it.***

**He squeezes the trigger in smooth, short bursts.**  
 **The *paper silhouette* downrange *blinks into a constellation of holes* right through the chest.**

**He pauses. Grins.**

---

**JEREMY (to himself):**  
 **Slide guitar tomorrow.**  
 ***Full metal therapy today.***

---

**INT. PAWN SHOP – EAST NASHVILLE – 12:42 P.M. – SCENE 2**

**Jim, wrapped in *sunglasses and an oversized vintage T-shirt*, sifts through *dusty bins of jewelry, war medals, and battered pendants.***

**He’s looking for *something that isn’t there*—yet.**

**Something *arcane. Symbolic.***

**He finds a rusted belt buckle shaped like a phoenix and holds it up to the light.**

---

**Jim (murmuring):**  
 **Close.**

**(*pockets a card, “Miller’s Pawn – Ask for Duke.”*)**

---

**EXT. BROADWAY – GUITAR SHOP STRIP – 2:03 P.M. – SCENE 3**

**Jeremy again, this time in *jeans and a tourist T-shirt*, moves down the strip of historic instrument shops like *a sommelier in a vineyard.***

**He tests a *resonator guitar*, plucks a few aching notes, then picks up *a steel slide* and grins.**

---

**JEREMY (to clerk):**  
 **This slide feels *like a sermon.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **You got one in *chrome*?**

---

**EXT. FRANKLIN CIVIL WAR BATTLEFIELD – 2:16 P.M. – SAME SCENE**

**Jeff, quiet, deliberate, walks across the *rolling green field.***

**He stops at a monument.**

**Reads the inscription.**

***Thinks long. Hard. Silent.***

---

**JEFF (to no one):**  
 **We forget too easy.**

---

**INT. NAIL SALON – THE GULCH – 2:33 P.M. – SCENE 5**

**Kathy sits at a manicure station, scrolling her phone idly, tapping her foot to *a George Michael track.***

**She glances up at the tech.**

---

**KATHY:**  
 **I was gonna *find a guy.***

**But this early?**

**They’re either *married*, *hungover*, or *terrified of women like me.***

**(*shrugs*)**  
 **So.**  
 ***French tip.***

**Let’s call it *recalibration.***

---

**INT. HOTEL – **SARAH**’S TEMP OFFICE – 3:02 P.M. – FINAL SCENE**

**Sarah sips a bottled water, pacing slowly, checking her planner and watching the clock tick.**

**She turns to Cremeans, who’s lounging in the corner with a church bulletin and a Diet Dr. Pepper.**

---

****SARAH**:**  
 **Are you *ever* going to give these people *another day off* again?**

---

**CREMEANS (sighing deeply, but smiling):**  
 ***Yes.***

**Yes, I *will.***

**Because *they’ll come back.***

**And they’ll *kick somebody’s door down tomorrow.***

**(*beat*)**  
 ***If they’re not in jail.***

---

****SARAH** (grinning):**  
 **Reasonable risk.**

---

**FADE TO BLACK.**

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – NASHVILLE – GILLEY’S SUITE – MAY 12, 1992 – 3:06 P.M. CDT**

**Sarah pauses mid-sip.**

**Planner open, pen hovering.**  
 **The room is humming with post-checklist calm.**

**And then—**

**A flicker of curiosity cuts through her mind.**

**Not concern.**  
 **Not dread.**

**Just one, sharp-edged word:**

***“Gilley.”***

**She lowers her water bottle.**

**Looks out the window, toward the direction of downtown.**

---

****SARAH** (quietly, to herself):**  
 **Oh.**

**What’s *Gilley* doing?**

---

**SMASH CUT TO:**

**EXT. ROOFTOP BAR – NASHVILLE – 3:07 P.M.**

**Gilley is shirtless.**

**In cowboy boots, borrowed aviators, and a *borrowed guitar* he convinced a wedding band to let him hold for “just five minutes.”**

**He's *serenading* a group of bachelorettes who have *no idea who he is*—**

**But *completely believe he’s famous.***

---

**GILLEY (singing):**  
 ***“My baby’s hotter than a summer in Mobile,***  
 ***She kissed me once and I forgot how to feel…”***

---

**One of the girls hands him a beer.**

**He chugs it *mid-verse.***

**Someone’s *filming* on a camcorder.**  
 **Another is *applying sunscreen to his back.***

---

**He stops.**

**Winks at the camera.**

---

**GILLEY:**  
 ***Tag MTV.***  
 **Tell ’em *they passed on this ass.***

---

**CUT BACK TO:**

**INT. HOTEL OFFICE – **SARAH****

**She smirks.**

**Makes a note in her planner.**

---

****SARAH** (muttering):**  
 **…Never change, you beautiful idiot.**

---

**EXT. ROOFTOP BAR – NASHVILLE – EARLY EVENING – MAY 12, 1992 – 5:41 P.M. CDT**

**The sun begins to drop low over the Cumberland River, casting the whole rooftop in that *magic hour gold* that makes everyone look like *they're in a music video.***

**And in the middle of it?**

**Gilley.**

**Still shirtless.**  
 **Still booted.**  
 ***Still glowing like he was poured straight from a Mason jar full of southern charm and trouble.***

---

**He’s got a *half-eaten burger on one plate, a rib basket on another, a sweet tea that’s clearly spiked*, and *four napkins in his pocket—each with a phone number written in looping, lipstick-smudged cursive.***

---

**The bartender sets down another drink.**

**This one *neatly garnished, on the house.***

---

**BARTENDER (grinning):**  
 **From the *manager.***  
 **Said to tell you *“You're good for business, but not every night.”***

---

**GILLEY (grinning):**  
 **Fair enough.**

**Tell him *he has a beautiful establishment***  
 **and *the acoustics in the bathroom are divine.***

---

**A BACHELORETTE (from across the table):**  
 **Do you *actually* play in a band?**

---

**GILLEY (leaning in like a secret):**  
 ***Sometimes.***

**Other times I *just pretend.***

**(beat)**  
 **Today?**  
 **I’m *doing both.***

---

**Laughter erupts.**

**Someone refills his beer.**  
 **Another girl slides into the seat next to him, her friend *scooting her drink over to him* as tribute.**

---

**He spins a tale about *opening for Prince in a bowling alley* (not true),**  
 ***meeting Shania Twain before she was famous* (possibly true),**  
 **and *getting kicked out of a limo for singing too loud* (100% true).**

---

**They *eat him up.***

**Every story.**

**Every wink.**

**Every *absurd, half-true line.***

**Because Gilley doesn’t lie—**  
 **He just *curates reality*.**

---

**And in this moment?**

**He’s *the center of a Nashville evening.***

**The *sunset’s outlaw prince.***

**A *raconteur* with a borrowed guitar, free food, and *not a single regret.***

---

**EXT. NASHVILLE SIDE STREET – MAY 12, 1992 – 7:13 P.M. CDT**

**Gilley strolls down the sidewalk, golden-hour breeze cutting just enough of the heat, a to-go box of ribs in one hand, his aviators perched backward on his head, and a smirk that won’t quit.**

**He’s *still barefoot.***

***Still riding the high.***

**But now?**

**He’s *thinking.***

**Specifically: *about Sarah.***

---

**GILLEY (murmuring to himself):**  
 **Alright, alright…**  
 **That rooftop crowd was *great*,**  
 **but these *ribs*?**

**These *ribs* are *otherworldly.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **And Sarah likes *intentional gestures.***

---

**He holds the box up to eye level like he’s inspecting treasure.**

---

**GILLEY:**  
 ***Brisket’s obvious.***  
 ***Pulled pork’s cliché.***  
 **But *smoked baby back ribs*?**

**That’s *southern sincerity* with *caramelized bark.***

**She’ll *know.***

---

**A car honks.**

**He flashes a finger-gun at the driver.**

**Keeps walking.**

---

**He pauses at a flower stand.**  
 **Plucks a small yellow carnation from a bucket.**  
 **Drops a fiver in the jar.**

**Tucks it behind his ear again, still balancing the ribs like *they’re sacred.***

---

**GILLEY (to himself):**  
 **Tonight?**

***Ribs.***  
 ***Respect.***  
 ***And a slow apology***  
 ***that tastes like hickory.***

---

**And with that, he disappears around the corner—**  
 **walking *back toward the hotel,***  
 **back toward *Sarah,***  
 **and *maybe toward something bigger than either of them planned.***

---

**INT. HOTEL SUITE – **SARAH**’S ROOM – NASHVILLE – MAY 12, 1992 – 7:38 P.M. CDT**

**Knock-knock.**

**Sarah looks up from her planner, pen still in hand, glasses low on her nose.**  
 **She wasn’t expecting anyone.**

**She crosses the room slowly, opens the door—**

**Gilley stands there, barefoot, slightly sun-kissed, a yellow carnation tucked behind his ear, and holding a steaming to-go box like it’s a *peace treaty signed in smoked meat.***

---

****SARAH** (eyebrow raised):**  
 **Is that… *barbecue?***

---

**GILLEY (grinning):**  
 ***Artisanal Nashville barbecue.***

***Local. Legendary.***  
 ***Unapologetically carnivorous.***

---

**Sarah blinks.**  
 **She doesn’t move to open the door wider.**

**Instead, she tilts her head.**

---

****SARAH**:**  
 **I’m not sure I *like* barbecue.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **I mean, *regional* barbecue.**  
 **Memphis? Kansas City? Texas?**  
 ***Is this even kosher?***

---

**GILLEY (smirking):**  
 **It’s *spiritually kosher.***

**(*serious now*)**  
 **No pork in the beans.**  
 **Ribs are dry-rubbed, not sauced.**

**And the guy behind the counter looked like *he could moonlight as a rabbi* if the lighting was right.**

---

****SARAH** (deadpan):**  
 **Wow.**

**You brought *ribs* and *rhetoric.***

---

**GILLEY:**  
 **I brought *a moment of kindness* and *a carbohydrate.***

**(*holds up the box*)**  
 **Just try one.**

**You can *atone later.***

---

**She eyes him for a beat longer, then steps aside.**

---

****SARAH** (sighing):**  
 **Fine.**  
 **One rib.**

**And I swear to God, if there’s *any vinegar in this…***

---

**GILLEY (walking in, triumphant):**  
 **Then I’ll *personally scrub your soul* with brisket and forgiveness.**

---

**She shuts the door behind him.**

**And smiles.**

**Just a little.**

**Just enough.**

---

**INT. HOTEL SUITE – NASHVILLE – MAY 12, 1992 – 7:49 P.M. CDT**

**Sarah stands by the dresser, *one hand on her hip, the other holding a half-eaten rib*—expression pinched like someone who's furious to be proven wrong by food.**

**Gilley lounges at the foot of the bed, looking smug and barefoot and like he belongs in a *museum dedicated to charming troublemakers.***

---

****SARAH** (grumbling):**  
 **This is…**

***Infuriatingly good.***

---

**GILLEY (grinning like he just scored a hat trick):**  
 **Mmm.**

**That’s the *sound of conversion.***

**Once you get across the *East River* and out into *flyover country*, you'll *learn a thing or two.***

**(*leans forward*)**  
 **Now, *Sarah*…**

**(*beat*)**  
 **What was that *big secret*?**

**The one that *had to wait* until *Nashville.***

---

**She freezes for half a breath.**

**The rib stalls halfway to her mouth.**

**She sets it down.**

**Walks to the sink.**  
 **Washes her hands.**  
 ***Slow. Precise. Measured.***

**Dries them on a towel.**

**Turns.**

**Leans against the counter.**

**And looks at him *like she’s about to detonate something carefully timed.***

---

****SARAH** (even):**  
 **I don’t report to *Wyler* anymore.**

---

**GILLEY (blinks):**  
 **…okay?**

---

****SARAH** (calmer now, but unwavering):**  
 **I report *directly to Chris Blackwell.***

---

**Beat.**

**\*\*Gilley’s smirk doesn’t fall—**  
 **It *recalculates.***  
 **Turns into *something real.***

**Something *serious.***

---

**GILLEY (quietly):**  
 **…That’s not just a promotion.**

**That’s *a seat at the table.***

---

****SARAH**:**  
 **It’s *the table.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **He wants *monthly reports.***  
 ***Handwritten.***  
 ***Personal intelligence.***  
 **Direct to *him.***

---

**GILLEY (soft):**  
 **So…**

**You’re *spying on us.***

**Officially now?**

---

****SARAH** (level):**  
 **I was *always* spying on you.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **Now?**  
 **It *counts.***

---

**INT. HOTEL SUITE – NASHVILLE – MAY 12, 1992 – 7:56 P.M. CDT**

**The air hums.**

**Not with tension—but with *truth finally standing still long enough to be named.***

**Sarah walks toward the bed, slow but sure, her posture composed, her eyes burning with *everything she’s withheld for weeks, maybe months.***

**Gilley watches her, chest rising slowly, the grin gone now—replaced by something heavier.**

**Something *real.***

**She sits beside him.**

**Not close.**

**But *intentionally.***

---

****SARAH** (quietly):**  
 **Don’t make me choose.**

---

**She doesn’t look at him right away.**

**Just folds her hands in her lap.**

**Voice steady. Almost soft.**

---

****SARAH**:**  
 **I’ve *already chosen.***

**Between *Michael*…**  
 **And *you.***

**Between *the career I planned*…**  
 **And *the one I have now.***

---

**Gilley doesn’t interrupt.**

**Not once.**

---

****SARAH** (finally meeting his eyes):**  
 **And the answer is *yes.***

**(*beat*)**  
 ***All of the above.***

---

**She leans in just slightly.**  
 **Not to kiss.**  
 **Not yet.**  
 **Just to let him feel the weight.**

---

****SARAH**:**  
 **Can you *handle* that for me?**

---

**The room goes still.**

**The *smoke of ribs still in the air.***  
 **The *past a breath behind.***  
 **The *future holding its breath.***

---

**INT. HOTEL SUITE – NASHVILLE – MAY 12, 1992 – 7:58 P.M. CDT**

**The words have landed.**  
 **Sarah’s still.**  
 **Gilley’s eyes don’t flinch.**

**He doesn’t posture, doesn’t grin, doesn’t play it off like a line.**

**He just *breathes.***  
 **Once.**

**And then:**

---

**GILLEY (low, steady):**  
 ***I’ll try.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **I’ll *never lie.***

**And *you* don’t lie.**  
 **Not really.**

---

**He shifts slightly on the bed, turning to face her squarely now.**  
 **Still close—but now with *terms on the table.***

---

**GILLEY:**  
 **We *don’t fuck* on *Manhattan.***

**We *don’t* pretend we’re *something we’re not.***

---

**(*beat*)**

**And don’t *ever* bring your *husband*—**  
 ***fiancé*—**  
 ***whatever the hell that guy’s name is—***  
 **to a *show.***

**Ever.**  
 ***Period.***  
 ***No.***

---

**He raises a finger like he’s about to say something dramatic—**  
 **But instead?**

**His voice *drops lower.***

**Sharper.**

---

**GILLEY:**  
 **And don’t you *look cross-eyed at me* when I *take someone else to bed.***

**Because you’re *not there.***

**Because I *needed someone.***

**Because *they wanted me* when *you weren’t around.***

**You *don’t* get to *reject* anybody I *like*—**

**Like *enough to sleep with.***

---

**He pauses, his tone now laced with something painful and honest.**

---

**GILLEY:**  
 **You want to *do your thing?***

**Well…**

***I’m going to do mine.***

---

**He lets it hang there.**

**Not like a threat.**

**Like *the weight of the truth he had to say aloud to stay whole.***

---

**INT. HOTEL SUITE – NASHVILLE – MAY 12, 1992 – 8:00 P.M. CDT**

**The room holds its breath.**  
 **Gilley’s words still hover—unapologetic, *honest like broken glass.***

**Sarah doesn’t flinch.**

**She takes them in, holds them, then nods—*once.***  
 **Sharp. Clean. Necessary.**

---

****SARAH** (softly):**  
 **Then we’re *agreed.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **And we *survive.***

---

**She looks away, just for a second, toward the *darkening skyline* outside the hotel window.**

**Her voice drops.**

**Quieter now.**

**Almost mournful.**

---

****SARAH**:**  
 **If the world wasn’t so *cruel*…**

**Maybe we’d *do something different.***

---

**GILLEY (without hesitation):**  
 **It’s a *plain, cruel world.***

**(*leans back, eyes on the ceiling*)**  
 **There’s *no escape.***

---

**(*beat*)**  
 ***We’re all going to die.***

**And *all we get to do*—**

**Is *rage.***

---

**He says it like a *truth tattooed across his ribs.***  
 **Like something *etched into the music* long before they knew they’d be famous.**

---

**Sarah turns back to him.**

**She doesn’t argue.**

**Because *he’s right.***

**Because *they’re both already burning.***

**And *rage is all that’s left to feel like fire means something.***

---

**INT. HOTEL SUITE – NASHVILLE – MAY 12, 1992 – 8:03 P.M. CDT**

**The air has cooled.**

**Not in temperature—**  
 **But in *voltage.***

**They’re not arguing.**  
 **They’re not negotiating.**

**They’re *two people staring down the edge of a cliff* and agreeing to jump *separately but at the same time.***

**Gilley picks up his glass of water.**

**Raises it like a toast.**

---

**GILLEY (softly):**  
 **To *rage.***  
 **And *ribs.***  
 **And a *damn good song.***

---

**Sarah smiles, slow, almost involuntarily.**

**She raises her water too.**

***Glass meets glass.***

**A soft *clink*.**

**Then—**

**The moment hovers.**

**And, of course, *Gilley can’t leave it alone.***

---

**GILLEY (grinning now):**  
 **So…**

***Did you like the ribs?***

---

****SARAH** (smirking):**  
 **They were *infuriatingly good.***

---

**GILLEY:**  
 **Good.**

**(*leans in just a little*)**  
 **And…**

**(*beat*)**  
 **Um…**

**(*grins wickedly*)**  
 **Are you *wearing underwear*?**

---

****SARAH** (stone-faced, but amused):**  
 **Gilley.**

---

**GILLEY:**  
 **It’s a *relevant* question.**  
 **I *brought food.***  
 **I *told the truth.***  
 **I *respected your damn fiancé.***

**You owe me *a detail.***

---

****SARAH** (leaning in, lips just barely curved):**  
 **Maybe.**

**(*beat*)**  
 **Maybe *not.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **But if I am?**

**They're *absolutely no match* for good barbecue and a man who knows *when not to lie.***

---

**GILLEY (softly, like a prayer):**  
 **That’s *so* much *hotter* than a yes.**

---

**They laugh.**

**Low.**

**Shared.**

**And dangerously close to something they’ll never quite define.**

---

**FADE TO BLACK.**

**EXT. JUST OUTSIDE THE GRAND OLE OPRY – NASHVILLE – MAY 12, 1992 – 9:05 P.M. CDT**

**The neon buzz of a honky-tonk bar slices through the warm Tennessee night.**  
 **A little off the main drag, tucked between a boot shop and a BBQ joint, sits a place called *The Buckle & Beam.***

**Inside?**

**Kathy Espich is having a full-blown hoot.**

---

**She’s kicked off her boots.**

**Feet up on the bar’s brass rail.**

**Half a glass of *whiskey and Coke* in one hand, and a *cowboy hat that doesn’t belong to her* jammed down on her head at a rakish angle.**

**Next to her?**

**A guy named Ricky.**  
 **Tight jeans.**  
 **Plaid button-up.**  
 **Big smile.**  
 ***Perfect jawline.***

**He looks like *every woman’s bad idea in college* and *every dad’s worst nightmare* rolled into a Wrangler ad.**

---

**RICKY (laughing):**  
 **I *still* don’t believe you’re in a band.**

---

**KATHY (grinning, sultry):**  
 **Why?**

**Because I *don’t look miserable enough?***

---

**RICKY:**  
 **Because *you’re way too much fun.***

**Most musicians *mope.***

---

**KATHY (winking):**  
 **I *mope* between *encores.***

---

**They clink glasses.**  
 **A song kicks up on the jukebox—*Lucinda Williams.***  
 **It gets her tapping her foot on instinct.**

**Ricky offers a hand, but Kathy waves it off.**

---

**KATHY:**  
 **No dancing.**

***I’m off duty.***

**But *you* can spin around and *impress me.***

---

**RICKY (grinning):**  
 **Only if *you* kiss me if I do.**

---

**KATHY (mock-pensive):**  
 **Hmm.**

**Depends how *dizzy* you get.**

---

**And just like that, *she laughs.***

**Big, *open-mouthed, unfiltered.***

**Like *a girl who didn’t go to war with her emotions last week.***

**Like *a woman who forgot about press tours and backstage passes and video controversies.***

**Tonight?**

***She’s just Kathy.***

**And *she’s having a hoot.***

---

**INT. THE BUCKLE & BEAM – JUST OUTSIDE THE GRAND OLE OPRY – MAY 12, 1992 – 9:32 P.M. CDT**

**The bar’s half-full now, the crowd shifting toward that soft, slow hour where *everyone knows the night has a decision to make.***

***Stay safe… or get interesting.***

**Kathy’s perched on a barstool, hat askew, boots swinging below her stool, glass almost empty.**

**Ricky’s leaned in, elbows on the counter, drink forgotten.**

**His smile is looser now.**  
 ***Sincere. Curious.***

---

**RICKY:**  
 **Will I get to see you *tomorrow?***

---

**Kathy smirks.**  
 **Leans in just close enough to make it count.**

---

**KATHY:**  
 **That *depends.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **On *how little clothing* you’re going to be wearing when I *see* you.**

**(*smiles*)**  
 **You *tell me.***

---

**Ricky sits back, clearly trying to hold his composure—**  
 **Fails *just enough.***

**He laughs, then puts a hand to his chest like he’s been *wounded by flirtation.***

---

**RICKY:**  
 **That’s *not fair.***

---

**KATHY (shrugging):**  
 **Neither is *my schedule.***

**(*beat*)**  
 **So *earn it.***

---

**She hops down from the stool, adjusts her belt like she’s preparing to disappear.**

**Ricky stands too, all boyish swagger now.**

---

**RICKY:**  
 **Can I at least walk you to your car?**

---

**KATHY:**  
 **No car.**  
 **Band van.**

**(*smirks*)**  
 **But you *can* walk me to the edge of this *very unstable decision.***

---

**She tips the hat—his hat—down over her eyes, just for a beat.**

**Then tosses it back to him.**

---

**KATHY (grinning):**  
 **Keep it warm.**

---

**And with that, she walks out into the *Nashville night*, boots hitting pavement like a snare roll.**

**Free.**  
 **Wild.**  
 ***And a little dangerous.***

---

**EXT. NASHVILLE STREETS – MAY 12, 1992 – 9:44 P.M. CDT**

Kathy walks alone now.

The honky-tonks fade behind her, the din of guitar twang and tequila shots *morphing into the low hum of streetlamps and distant traffic.*

Her boots hit the pavement with *confidence* and *intent.*

She’s not wandering.

She’s *going somewhere.*

And *she knows it.*

---

She hums as she walks.

Low at first, then with just enough under-her-breath confidence to carry:

*“Feel the pulse, racing hearts collide…”*

A slow smile pulls across her face.

*“Let’s break the rules, let’s be a little naughty…”*

---

Kathy Espich is on her way back to the Hilton.

And not just any Hilton.  
 The Hilton.

Where *tomorrow night?*

She’s getting *laid.*

No guessing.

No hoping.

Just *certainty.*

Because she’s *done the flirting, the daring, the smiling-too-wide bit.*

Now?

It’s time for *intentional pleasure.*

---

She turns a corner.  
 Light from a marquee hits her face.

She doesn’t flinch.

Just hums louder.

---

*“With every touch, we’ll turn it up… I’m ready.”*

---

**FADE TO BLACK.**  
 **END NIGHT THREE.**

**INT. WBUZ 102.9 FM – NASHVILLE – MAY 13, 1992 – 7:06 A.M. CDT**  
 **"THE BUZZ MORNING SHOW – LIVE"**

The *day has barely begun.*  
 The *coffee in the studio is bad.*  
 The *mood is worse.*

Sarah’s already on her second cup, eyes sharp behind *dark sunglasses*, clipboard in hand, and a *grim look* that says *“I will trade your soul for media exposure before 9 a.m.”*

Next to her?

Kathy.

*Sunglasses. Hoodie. Attitude.*  
 And the *hangover of a woman who had a very good night and zero intention of being on the radio at sunrise.*

---

**SARAH** (leaning in, hissing):  
 I *hauled your ass out of bed* because this station touches *two states* and *a hundred thousand cars* stuck in *rush hour traffic.*

(*beat*)  
 *Sound alive.*

---

KATHY (gravel-voiced):  
 I *sound alive.*  
 I *don’t* look it.

(*sips from a lukewarm gas station coffee Sarah shoved in her hand minutes ago*)  
 And I *smell* like… *bourbon and optimism.*

---

**SARAH**:  
 Perfect.

(*points to mic*)  
 *Turn that into legend.*

---

**INT. SOUND BOOTH – SAME TIME**

DJ CRAIG “THE BUZZMAN” THOMAS, all loud shirt and louder energy, flips on the mic and grins at the red light.

---

BUZZMAN (on air):  
 It’s *7:07 in the AM* and I’ve got *someone special* in the studio—

That’s right, folks, *Kathy Espich* from *Commuted* is *literally sitting across from me* with *half a coffee and what I believe is bourbon cologne.*

(*chuckles*)  
 Kathy, good morning.

---

KATHY (deadpan into the mic):  
 Good *something.*

---

BUZZMAN (laughing):  
 Now *that’s* a rock star entrance\!

So, tell us—what’s it like *riding up the Billboard charts* with a song that’s probably banned in *three time zones*?

---

KATHY (smirking):  
 Feels *loud.*  
 *Fast.*  
 And *exactly like the first time someone puts a hand down your pants at a concert.*

Unexpected.  
 Welcome.  
 And *hard to forget.*

---

BUZZMAN (cackling):  
 We *are live,* people\!

---

Sarah, behind the glass, doesn’t even flinch.

She just takes *one long sip of coffee* and makes *a note:*

*"Book Kathy for drive-time again. Give her caffeine and one hour of lead time."*

---

**INT. WBUZ 102.9 FM – “THE BUZZ MORNING SHOW” – LIVE – MAY 13, 1992 – 7:14 A.M. CDT**

Kathy’s eyes are sharper now.  
 The *coffee’s finally hit.*  
 The *buzz of bourbon has faded just enough to give way to clarity.*  
 And *she’s remembering* who she is—  
 *and what she can do with a live mic.*

Buzzman leans in, still chuckling from her last remark.

---

BUZZMAN:  
 You’re waking up the whole damn city, Kathy.

So, *real talk*—  
 Your band’s been called *provocative, raw, even dangerous.*

Is that intentional?  
 Or are you just *writing what you feel?*

---

Kathy turns to the mic.

Smiles.

And *something shifts.*

She’s *not tired anymore.*

She’s *awake.*

---

KATHY (clear, unapologetic):  
 You ever see an *avalanche* start?

It’s *quiet.*  
 A little crack.  
 A shift in the ice.

And then *everything moves at once.*

Can’t stop it.  
 Can’t redirect it.  
 You just *watch it come.*

---

She pauses just long enough to let the double entendre settle in the headphones of *every half-asleep commuter* in *greater Nashville.*

---

KATHY (lower, but no less sure):  
 It’s *a lot* like *a woman’s orgasm,* actually.

You *never see it coming*—  
 but when it hits?

*It tears through everything.*  
 *It changes the shape of the room.*  
 And *if you’re lucky enough to be in the blast radius,*  
 you *don’t forget it.*

---

BUZZMAN (stunned, then cackling):  
 Oh my *god.*

(*off mic*)  
 *Are we allowed to air that?\!*

---

PRODUCER (through glass, to Sarah):  
 Was this *in the briefing packet?\!*

---

**SARAH** (sipping coffee, cool as ice):  
 *She is the briefing packet.*

---

BUZZMAN (back on mic):  
 Well, *there it is, Nashville.*  
 Forget your *drive-thru biscuit.*  
 *That’s the real breakfast.*

---

KATHY (grinning):  
 You’re *welcome.*

---

The phone lines light up like *Christmas in hell.*

And outside?

The *sun keeps rising.*  
 So does *Commuted.*

---

**INT. MINIVAN – PARKING LOT – OUTSIDE A MEDICAL BILLING OFFICE – NASHVILLE – MAY 13, 1992 – 7:18 A.M. CDT**

Donna, 42, *coffee-stained scrubs, Aqua Net hair,* and a dashboard full of cassette tapes, pulls into her usual parking spot. She’s got *WBUZ 102.9 FM* dialed in on her *manual tuner*.

She reaches for her purse, ready to head into work—

But freezes.

Because *Kathy Espich’s voice is coming through the speakers like a lightning strike.*

---

*“…it’s a lot like a woman’s orgasm, actually. You never see it coming, but when it hits—it tears through everything…”*

---

Donna’s mouth drops open.

She stares at the radio like it just spoke prophecy.

---

DONNA (to herself, shocked):  
 Oh my *Lord.*

---

She yanks the keys from the ignition, *radio still blaring.*  
 Slams the door shut behind her.  
 Marches into the *modular, beige-brick office building* like she’s on a mission from God.

---

**INT. OFFICE – SAME TIME**

Phones are ringing. Fax machines are whirring. The breakroom smells like burned Folgers.

Donna storms through the cubicles, coat still on, purse swinging off her shoulder.

She reaches a beige rotary phone at the reception desk.

Slams it off the hook.

---

DONNA (frantic, dialing):  
 *Come on, come on…*

---

She dials her sister’s extension *from memory.*

---

**INT. DIFFERENT OFFICE ACROSS TOWN – SAME TIME**

Linda, 38, works reception at a dental office. She’s halfway through licking an envelope.

The phone rings.

She answers, bored.

---

LINDA:  
 Nashville Dental—this is—

---

DONNA (cutting her off):  
 *Turn on 102.9. NOW.*

---

LINDA (startled):  
 Donna? What the—?

---

DONNA:  
 The *Buzz Morning Show.*  
 There’s *some girl—Kathy, from that band—*  
 She’s on the air *saying things we never even dared to whisper in youth group.*

---

LINDA (already reaching for the battered radio under the counter):  
 Wait, wait, what’s she saying?

---

DONNA:  
 She’s *talking about women. Power. Sex. Rock.*

I swear to God, *you’re gonna cry and start a riot all at once.*

---

LINDA (fumbling the tuner):  
 What’s the station? 102 what?

---

DONNA:  
 *102.9. WBUZ.*  
 It’s like *Joan Jett met Gloria Steinem at the Grand Ole Opry.*

---

LINDA (finally getting the static-clear signal):  
 Oh… oh my *god.*

---

The sisters don’t speak.

They just *listen.*

The *crackle of FM radio* carrying Kathy’s voice like *a late-breaking revolution.*

---

**INT. WBUZ 102.9 FM – “THE BUZZ MORNING SHOW” – NASHVILLE – MAY 13, 1992 – 7:21 A.M. CDT**

Kathy’s leaned back in her chair, one leg casually crossed over the other, a *pair of black shades covering her eyes* and *a grin that belongs in a museum behind glass labeled “Handle With Caution.”*

The on-air light glows red.  
 The phones are lit up like a switchboard on fire.

*The city’s listening.*

And Kathy Espich knows it.

---

BUZZMAN (laughing nervously):  
 Well, if you weren’t *awake before*, Nashville, you *sure are now.*

(*beat*)  
 Kathy, let me ask you something—

(*leans in, trying to play it cool*)  
 What’s the *secret sauce* behind this new record?

---

KATHY (without skipping a beat):  
 Oh, I don’t know…

Probably the *friction.*

---

She lets that hang *just long enough*.

Then *adjusts her sunglasses ever so slightly.*

Not enough to reveal her eyes.

Just enough to remind everyone they *can’t see them.*

And that *drives them nuts.*

---

KATHY (voice low, deliberate):  
 There’s a *certain rhythm* to telling the *truth in bed.*

Same in *rock.*

You *press just hard enough*…

Then *back off.*  
 Then *hit again.*

(*beat*)  
 And *if you time it right?*

Even *the silence* between the notes makes a man *sweat.*

---

BUZZMAN (completely flustered, fanning himself with cue cards):  
 Well, uh—  
 Hoo boy—

---

KATHY (sweetly):  
 Too *early* for that kind of metaphor?

(*beat*)  
 *Or too late?*

---

She *smiles.*  
 Still shaded.  
 Still composed.  
 Still *coiled like poetry with teeth.*

---

Across the city, in parked cars and break rooms and dental offices, *women stop moving.*

Men *gulp* coffee they didn’t taste.

And the \*\*\*radio carries the sound of a woman holding the room by the *throat*—*and smiling.*

---

**INT. WBUZ 102.9 FM – BEHIND THE GLASS – PRODUCER’S BOOTH – MAY 13, 1992 – 7:23 A.M. CDT**

Sarah stands with her arms crossed, eyes locked on Kathy in the studio like she’s watching a *controlled burn in real time.*

Every phone line on the switchboard is flashing.  
 The *producer*—mid-thirties, mustache, \*\*\*crewneck sweatshirt with pit stains forming—\*\*\*spins his chair toward Sarah, eyes wide.

He mouths:

*“She’s killing them.”*

---

Sarah doesn’t nod.  
 Doesn’t smirk.

She just takes a long sip of her coffee and sets the mug down with surgical precision.

---

**SARAH** (quietly):  
 She knows.

---

**INT. ON-AIR BOOTH – SAME MOMENT**

Kathy’s smile is razor-thin.

She’s *leaned forward now*, elbows on the table, mic close, voice low enough that every man in a ten-mile radius is leaning toward his radio without realizing it.

---

She delivers *another line*—this one about rhythm, feedback, and "how a real woman tunes her stage presence like she does a man’s tension."

It’s *double entendre perfection.*  
 It’s *rated R* wrapped in *FM legal language.*  
 It’s *weapons-grade.*

---

BUZZMAN (visibly sweating now):  
 You’ve got, uh…  
 A *way* with words, Ms. Espich.

---

KATHY (smiling behind the mic):  
 *There are only so many ways* I can *kill somebody*.

(*beat*)  
 And it *looks* like I’m *sampling them all.*

---

She never takes off her shades.  
 Never raises her voice.

Just *delivers it like it’s already a quote on a T-shirt.*

---

**INT. PRODUCER’S BOOTH**

The producer spins back to Sarah.

---

PRODUCER (whispers):  
 This is *Joan Jett with better timing.*

---

**SARAH**:  
 No.

(*beat*)  
 This is *Kathy Espich.*

And *we just won morning drive-time.*

---

**INT. WBUZ 102.9 FM – ON-AIR BOOTH – MAY 13, 1992 – 7:29 A.M. CDT**

The “ON AIR” light flicks off.  
 Silence falls like someone just unplugged the entire city.

Buzzman and his co-host are frozen, eyes wide, mouths slightly open like they just witnessed a *car crash orchestrated by Aphrodite herself.*

The producer behind the glass slumps back in his chair, quietly whispering, “Sweet Jesus.”

Kathy?

*Unbothered.*

She reaches up.

Calmly removes the *studio headphones* and sets them down like *a sniper holstering her weapon.*

She adjusts her shades.  
 Stretches her neck.  
 Smiles.

---

KATHY (cheerfully):  
 So…

*Where’s the donuts, guys?*

---

Buzzman blinks.

Still processing her metaphors, her mic control, her verbal demolition of morning radio decorum.

---

BUZZMAN (croaking):  
 We… uh… we’ve got…  
 (*checks desk*)  
 Old fashioneds?

---

KATHY:  
 Y’all made *me* do *all the work* this morning…

(*leans in with a grin*)  
 *And there’s no goddamn jelly?*

---

Co-host (deadpan):  
 I didn’t know we were feeding *a sex-positive gunslinger today.*

---

KATHY (standing up, cracking her neck):  
 Now you know.

(*to Sarah, as she enters the booth*)  
 We’re hitting Dunkin’.

---

**SARAH** (composed):  
 No, you’re hitting *five new affiliates* and *an afternoon soundcheck*.

If you behave, *maybe* you’ll get a bagel.

---

KATHY (walking out, victorious):  
 I want *sprinkles.*

(*pauses in the doorway*)  
 And *somebody* better clip that *avalanche-orgasm quote.*

That one *goes on the live album.*

---

And with that?

She’s *gone.*

The *DJ still speechless.*  
 The *phone lines still jammed.*  
 The *city still buzzing.*

And a donut-less morning?

*Suddenly legendary.*

---

**FADE OUT.**

**INT. HOTEL BUSINESS CENTER – NASHVILLE – MAY 13, 1992 – 3:17 P.M. CDT**

Sarah sits alone, surrounded by half-drunk coffee, printouts, and a planner that now looks *more like a battlefield than a calendar.*

The *fax machine hums.*  
 A yellow *Post-it is stuck to her thigh.*  
 A pen is behind one ear and another one’s in her mouth.

She stares straight ahead.

Completely still.

And then—

---

**SARAH** (to herself, deadpan):  
 Did I… just coordinate *four live media appearances* across *three time zones*…

*Without realizing it?*

---

She flips through her notes.

* *Gilley?* Doing *on-air banter* at 92Q Nashville, flirting his way into *a second segment.*

* *Jeff and Jeremy?* Currently being interviewed *together* on *KROQ’s L.A. afternoon drive syndicate.*  
   Topic? “Midwestern grunge and the fine line between sex appeal and anarchy.”

* *Jim?* Calmly talking to her *not 45 minutes ago*…

In *German.*

Flawlessly.

---

**SARAH** (blinking):  
 I don’t even know what *station* that was.

(pauses)  
 *DW? DF? DB? D-something.*

He said *"Stahlkultur."* I *think* that means *“drum culture”* or *"steel helmet."*  
 I *don’t know.*

---

She sets the pen down.

Picks up the phone.

Dials the internal number for the tour coordinator.

---

**SARAH** (flat):  
 Hi.  
 Yes. It’s me.  
 Just checking—

Did anyone *accidentally book a fifth interview* today?

---

(*long pause on the other end*)

---

**SARAH** (sighs):  
 Of course you did.

No, it’s fine. I just—

(*she stares blankly at a wall, mutters*)  
 These people continue to *fricking scare the shit out of me.*

---

She hangs up.

Closes her planner.

*Opens it again.*

Grabs a Post-it.

Writes:

*"Threat Level: Commuted. Assume Nothing. Expect Everything."*

Sticks it to her own forehead.

---

**INT. HOTEL – **SARAH**’S SUITE – NASHVILLE – BATHROOM – MAY 13, 1992 – 5:41 P.M. CDT**

Sarah closes the door quietly behind her.

No phone.  
 No clipboard.  
 No band chaos.  
 Just *steam rising* and *one hour* that belongs *only to her.*

She turns the faucet all the way to *hot*, drops in a hotel-issued *bath bomb she packed from New York just in case*, and watches it melt into a swirl of *lavender and surrender.*

---

She peels off her clothes like *slipping out of armor.*

Bra drops with a sigh.  
 Panties, gone.  
 The towel hangs nearby, untouched.

She steps in—  
 And lets go.

---

INT. BATHTUB – MOMENTS LATER

The water wraps around her like *a hush*.

Her skin flushes pink.

She *floats.*

---

*Float.*  
 *Think.*  
 *Float.*  
 *Think.*

---

Her thoughts don’t organize themselves.

They never do.

But the silence is *good.*  
 *Useful.*

The *sting of her scalp eases.*  
 Her *pulse slows.*

---

**SARAH** (to herself, eyes closed):  
 If they make it through July…  
 I make it through July.

(*beat*)  
 And if I don’t?

I *might* make Gilley explain it on MTV.

---

She laughs once.  
 Low.  
 Alone.

Then runs her fingers down her legs.  
 Feels the faint stubble along her calf.

---

**SARAH**:  
 Huh.

(*beat*)  
 I might be… *getting lucky tonight.*

(*grins*)  
 Might as well feel like silk while I’m *breaking every ethical code I know.*

---

She reaches for the razor.  
 Lazily.  
 Thoughtfully.

The *lavender steam curls up* around her chin.

---

She leans her head back.  
 *Aimlessly floating.*  
 *Drifting.*  
 *Rebooting.*

The water isn’t just hot—

It’s *enervating.*  
 Recharging her like a *battery dipped in sin and potential.*

---

Tonight?

Anything could happen.

But right now?

She’s *naked.*  
 She’s *alone.*  
 And she’s *weightless.*

Exactly where she needs to be.

---

**FADE TO STEAM.**

**EXT. THE PARTHENON – CENTENNIAL PARK – NASHVILLE – MAY 13, 1992 – 8:00 P.M. CDT  POP-UP CONCERT – UNANNOUNCED – SUNSET CROWD GATHERING FAST**

The sky is *molten gold fading into deep velvet.*  The Parthenon looms behind the *improvised stage setup* like *a temple daring someone to make history in front of it.*

And *Commuted?*  *They came to make fire.*

Sarah stands off to the side, fresh from her bath, *hair still damp, clipboard nowhere in sight* for once. She’s just watching. Because *this isn’t marketing anymore.* This is *the invocation.*

The band is *ripped.*  Tight. Mean. *Hungry.* Jim and Jeff lock in like \*a war drum and its shadow. \*\*Jeremy’s slide guitar cries out like *a wailing ghost under moonlight.* Bill’s synths\* are *chilling and cinematic*—more *Blade Runner than Broadway.*

And Kathy? Kathy Espich is something else. They launch into “Sweet Memories in a Dive Bar.” Kathy detonates. She *doesn’t just sing.  She *confesses.  With swagger, regret, danger—and a smile like *she might steal your truck, your man, and your hometown’s reputation.

*“Anna’s tying the knot next week / But tonight it’s wild and sleek…”*

By the *second verse*, the crowd is *completely hers.* People with *no idea who this band is* are *singing along* by the final chorus. Sarah glances at a *Nashville Scene reporter* scribbling in real time.

Then Kathy doesn’t pause. They *pivot hard* into *“Tangled Up.”* And everything *goes silent.* That *hypnotic bassline*.  That *smoke-drenched groove.*   That *lyric about a tongue and a soul and “wet and wanting.”*

Kathy moves like a slow storm.  Shirt half-unbuttoned.  Hair wild.  Her vocals are *breath against skin and steel against bone.* And when she hits the “Now\! Now\! Now\!” at the end? Half the crowd *actually gasps.*

Sarah exhales.   Slow. Because *this?* This was *the plan.* And *they pulled it off like a heist with a microphone.*

**FADE TO BLACK.**  But the headlines are already being written.  And *Commuted just declared war on the expected.*

---

**EXT. THE PARTHENON – CENTENNIAL PARK – NASHVILLE – MAY 13, 1992 – 8:12 P.M. CDT**

The final synth notes from *"Tangled Up"* linger in the night air like *perfume and gunpowder.* The band doesn’t bow. They *don’t speak.* They *don’t wave.* They just *walk off stage.* Fast. Clean. 10 minutes in, 10 minutes out.

The crowd? Left *stunned.*   *Breathless.*   *Lit up like they just saw a UFO make out with Joan Jett.* Phones off the hook.   Not a single T-shirt sold.   Not a *whiff* of pre-show hype.
Just *impact.* Sarah is grinning now.  She doesn’t clap.  Doesn’t cheer. She just whispers, *exactly to herself:*

**SARAH**:  
*Boy was that a thrill.*

She slips into the darkness behind the stage, the sound of the *crowd roaring in confusion and awe* behind her. And deep down? She knows. *This was the one.* The *inflection point.* The *moment they became myth.*

---

**EXT. BEHIND THE PARTHENON STAGE – NASHVILLE – MAY 13, 1992 – 8:14 P.M. CDT**

The buzz of the crowd still echoes through Centennial Park, a giddy, confused, electric roar that’s only growing louder as the realization sets in: *That just happened.* And *it’s already over.*

Sarah jogs down the access ramp, hair loose, boots scuffed, *grinning like a madwoman.*
She catches up to Kathy, who’s just grabbed a bottle of water and is *still sweating glitter and sin.* They lock eyes. Kathy’s cheeks are flushed.  Sarah’s pupils are wild.

**SARAH** (shrieking):  
*I sure as hell did\!*

**KATHY (laughing):**  
Right?\! That was *obscene.*

**SARAH**:  
That was *the Rolling Stones* in *a flash mob’s body.*

They both double over in laughter, trying not to lose composure in front of the few techs still lingering around. Then they pause. Look at each other. Eyes narrow. Both of them just a little too radiant.  A little too satisfied with themselves. A little too *ready.*

**KATHY (eyebrow raised):**  
So… *where you headed?*

**SARAH** (playing coy):  
I don’t know… *somewhere private.*   And *horizontal.*

KATHY:  
*God bless America.*

(*beat*)  
Same.

They both start giggling again.   Giddy. Relieved. Alive.   Like *teenagers who just robbed a gas station and got away with it.*

**SARAH** (smiling, extending a hand for a shake):  
*Good luck.*

KATHY (clapping her hand):  
Break hearts.*

hey part ways. Two *shadows disappearing into the Nashville dark.*  Each on a mission. Each full of music and teeth and unspeakable power.

FADE OUT.   THE NIGHT ISN’T DONE YET.

---
**EXT. DOWNTOWN NASHVILLE – LOWER BROADWAY – NEAR THE CUMBERLAND RIVER – MAY 13, 1992 – 8:39 P.M. CDT**

Kathy walks like she owns the street. Boots striking pavement with just enough delay to suggest *predator pacing.*  Leather jacket on over a thin tank top that still smells faintly of *smoke, perfume, and applause.* In her hand? A *folded napkin.*  On it: an address scrawled in black Sharpie and one word: *Ricky.*

She reaches the apartment building—an *old walk-up above a tattoo shop.*  The kind of place where *ACs rattle, the mailboxes are dented, and the lights inside are all different colors.*

Perfect.

KATHY (murmuring to herself):  
Alright, *Ricky.* Let’s see *what kind of welcome mat* you’re laying down.

She climbs the steps.   Second floor.   Third door on the left. Raises her hand. And *bangs.*Three sharp knocks. Followed by two more. *Deliberate. Intimate. Challenging.*

KATHY (quietly, to herself):   Let’s see the *fit, cowboy.*

The door opens. Slow. And there he is. Ricky. Shirtless.   In sweatpants and holding a bottle of beer. Eyes wide.  Grinning in *surprise and something much less polite.*

RICKY:  
You found me.

KATHY (eyes scanning up and down):  
Mmm.

*Sweatpants.*  No socks.   *No shirt.*

(grins)  
That’s a *solid signal.*

RICKY:  
I had a feeling.

KATHY (stepping inside, not waiting for an invitation):  
Good. Then *you already know* this isn’t about *talking.*

(*beat, glancing around*)  
Unless *your couch* has better *posture* than you do.

RICKY:  
It *doesn’t.*

She shuts the door behind her. Hard.

FADE TO BLACK.  *MAYBE THERE’S TALKING. MAYBE NOT.*   *BUT KATHY’S NIGHT IS DEFINITELY GOING HER WAY.*

**INT. RICKY’S APARTMENT – DOWNTOWN NASHVILLE – MAY 13, 1992 – 8:47 P.M. CDT**

The apartment is *small, warm, messy in that bachelor-charm sort of way.* A record player’s on low—*some outlaw country, dusty and slow.* Kathy stands near the window, lit only by the *glow from the streetlights outside* and the *dim bulb over the kitchen sink.* She kicks off her boots. *Deliberate. Quiet. Heavy.* Ricky watches from across the room, still shirtless, still stunned. She turns toward him, eyes veiled by her hair, and *slowly unzips her jeans.* Not showy. Not shy. Just *decisive.*

KATHY (softly, challenging):  
Do you *like what you see?*

(*beat*)  
If you do, *get naked.* I *might watch you.*

Ricky blinks once.  Then laughs, low and nervous. Starts peeling off the sweatpants like a man *who knows he’s already won but doesn’t want to blow the lead.* Kathy doesn’t move. Just grins. Then—She calls toward the kitchen:

KATHY:  
*Oh.* *Bring me some peanuts, too.*

RICKY (half-laughing, half-naked):  
You’re *serious.*

KATHY (deadpan):  
*I always am.*

And with that? The night *officially* begins.  Somewhere between *laughter, salt, and bare skin.*

THE PEANUTS? OPTIONAL. THE CONTROL? NOT A CHANCE.

---

**INT. RICKY’S APARTMENT – DOWNTOWN NASHVILLE – MAY 13, 1992 – 8:51 P.M. CDT**

Ricky drops his sweatpants with the flair of a man auditioning for something he never rehearsed but desperately wants to nail. Kathy bursts out laughing—full-bodied, rich, delighted. She claps once, grinning from ear to ear, and calls out—

KATHY (shouting):  
*Oh my God\!*  We are *having a great evening\!*

(*pointing toward the kitchen*)  
And *don’t forget the peanuts\!*

Ricky freezes.   Mid-strut.   Half-proud, half-panicked.  Fully erect. His brain catches up. 
Peanuts.  She *wasn’t kidding.* He does a quick mental inventory of the *cupboard he hasn’t opened since he moved in.*

RICKY (to himself, frantic whisper):  
Please, God, *just one jar.* Dry roasted.  Honey glazed.   I *don’t care.*

He scrambles toward the kitchen like it’s a mission briefing.

KATHY (calling after him, still giggling):  
*No peanuts?*   No *encore\!*

RICKY (digging through shelves):  
Don’t worry\! I *got this\!*

(*beat*)  
I think.

He yanks open the last cabinet and—Victory. A dusty jar of *Planters, half full, slightly suspect but technically still edible.* He holds it up like *Indiana Jones with the idol.*

RICKY (relieved, triumphant):  
*I FOUND THE PEANUTS.*

KATHY (offscreen):  
*Then you may proceed.*

(*beat*)  
*With enthusiasm.*

FADE OUT.  
Because sometimes, *a little salt, a little humor, and a lot of nerve* go a long way.

---

**INT. RICKY’S APARTMENT – DOWNTOWN NASHVILLE – MOMENTS LATER**

Ricky returns from the kitchen, victorious, holding the jar of peanuts like a man who just earned his place in a hall of fame he didn’t know existed.

He sets them on the coffee table and looks at Kathy, who’s now *lounging across his couch*, jeans off, tank top still on, hair wild and eyes glinting with mischief.

RICKY (half-laughing, half-serious):  
So… is *this* foreplay?

KATHY (grinning):  
*No.*

(*she stretches, casual, dangerous*)  
*Me sitting on your face is foreplay.*

RICKY (gulping):  
Oh.

KATHY (reaching for the peanuts):  
*You* can *eat me.*

(*pops the lid, starts shaking a few into her palm*)  
And *I’m gonna eat these.*

(*pops one in her mouth*)  
*Win-win.*

RICKY (grinning, hands raised):  
I mean, if this is a negotiation—*I accept the terms.*

KATHY (beaming):  
Smart man.

She leans back, tossing a peanut in the air and catching it with her mouth, like *a goddess of chaos and confidence.*

Fade out on the sound of peanuts rattling in the jar and laughter turning into something warmer. Because for Kathy? *This night is entirely hers.* And *Ricky’s just lucky to be invited.
